Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
6 min
The Qawida of Referring Branches to Principles (رد الفروع إلى القواعد)
Explains the method of referring branches back to legal principles using qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'رد الفروع إلى القواعد' by constructing a qiyas argument from a universal principle to a particular case in a fatwa context.

Core Idea
Every branch ruling is linked to a universal principle; qiyas recovers the ruling by combining the case with the principle.

This passage clarifies the method of deriving rulings from qawaid using qiyas. The author demonstrates that once a universal principle is established, any particular case falling under it can be ruled upon by simply applying the principle via analogy—no need for a separate textual ruling for each branch. The example from taharah illustrates how certainty (al-yaqin) is preserved against doubt (al-shakk).

Guided Path
1
Identify the universal principle (major premise)
From the passage, find the general rule that applies to all similar cases. Here it is: 'Every certainly pure substance has its purity not removed by doubt.'
2
Identify the particular case (minor premise)
Locate the specific instance being considered. Here it is: 'This cloth is certainly pure.'
3
Apply qiyas to derive the branch ruling
Combine the minor and major premises by dropping the middle term (certainty of purity) to produce the conclusion: 'This cloth's purity is not removed by doubt.'
This is a classic syllogism of the first figure.
4
Recognize the sufficiency of the method
The author notes that this derivation makes the phrase 'وفرعوا الأحكام عليها' (and they derived rulings from them) unnecessary, because the ruling is implicitly contained in the qiyas.
5
Connect to the complementary qawida
The principle used here is closely related to the well-known qawida 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' (certainty is not removed by doubt). Understand how the two qawaid reinforce each other.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نرد الفروع اليها: سے مراد یہ ہے کہ جزئیات کو ان قواعد کی طرف پھیرنا جن قواعد کے ذریعہ ان جزئیات کو ا گیا ہے اور کلیات سے جزئیات نکالنے کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ صغری کو کبری کے ساتھ ملا کر استخراج آسان ہے کہا جاتا ہے
مثلا هذ الثوب طاهر يقينا وكل طاهر يقينا لا تزول طهارته بالشك شكل اول سے حد اوسط گرانے کے بعد تيمي نكل گا هذا الثوب لا تزول طهارته بالشك اس تقریر سے یہ ظاہر ہو گیا کہ وفرعوا الاحكام عليها کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں تھی ۔
'We refer the branches to them' means to turn the particulars back to those rules by which those particulars were derived. The method of extracting particulars from universals is to combine the minor premise with the major to facilitate extraction. For example: This cloth is certainly pure, and every certainly pure substance has its purity not removed by doubt. After dropping the middle term from the first figure, the conclusion emerges: This cloth's purity is not removed by doubt. From this explanation it is clear that there was no need for 'and they derived rulings from them.'
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage explains the qawida 'رد الفروع إلى القواعد' (referring branches to principles). It demonstrates the logical method of qiyas: from a universal rule (major premise) and a particular case (minor premise) one derives the ruling. The example uses the principle of istishab (presumption of continuity): certainty is not removed by doubt. The cloth is certainly pure; every such pure thing remains pure unless proven otherwise. Thus, the derived ruling is that doubt does not remove its purity.

Key Terms
قاعدة (qa'idah): A universal legal principle from which particular rulings are derived.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction connecting a particular to a universal rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the qiyas example given, what is the universal rule (major premise)?
A) This cloth is pure.
B) Every certainly pure thing has its purity not removed by doubt.
C) Impurity is the removal of purity.
D) Cloth is pure by default.

Key Takeaway
The method of qiyas allows the mufti to derive branch rulings from universal principles without needing a specific textual ruling for every case.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
6 min
How Qawa'id Elevate a Muqallid to Ijtihad
Explains how qawa'id elevate a muqallid to ijtihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the function of qawa'id in the Hanafi hierarchy of legal authority and identify the criteria for attaining the rank of mujtahid al-fatwa.

Core Idea
Qawa'id are the ladder by which a muqallid ascends to ijtihad.

This passage from the commentary on al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair reveals a transformative idea: that mastery of legal maxims (qawa'id) can elevate a mere follower (muqallid) to the rank of ijtihad within the madhhab. It defines the level of mujtahid al-fatwa and explains how even without explicit transmissions from the founding imams, a scholar can derive rulings for novel cases using these principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the example and its purpose
Read the opening example about certainty and doubt. Understand that the author uses a logical syllogism to illustrate how a qa'ida (maxim) yields a ruling.
The example is drawn from the well-known maxim 'al-yaqin la yuzalu bi al-shakk'.
2
Define key terms (faqih, daraja, ijtihad, mujtahid al-fatwa)
Locate the definitions in the passage. Note that 'faqih' here means a muqallid, not a mujtahid, and 'mujtahid al-fatwa' is a specific rank below absolute ijtihad.
The author clarifies that even a muqallid can progress to this rank through practice of qawa'id.
3
Understand the role of qawa'id in the madhhab
The passage states that qawa'id function like usul al-fiqh for deriving particulars (furu'). They are universal maxims from which many rulings are deduced.
Contrast this with the view that qawa'id are merely summary statements; here they are active tools for istinbat.
4
Trace the author's methodology
The author claims to have searched rare books and unexpected sources to collect furu' under each qa'ida. He clarifies that he relied on sahih and zahir al-riwayah narrations.
This shows the epistemological weight: qawa'id are built on sound transmissions.
5
Apply the concept: from muqallid to mujtahid al-fatwa
Synthesize: What are the conditions for a muqallid to become a mujtahid al-fatwa? The passage says: continuous practice of qawa'id, mastery of the principles set by Imam Abu Hanifa and his students, and ability to deduce rulings for new cases.
This highlights the dynamic nature of the Hanafi school: it allows for growth within the tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثلا ہذا الشك طاہر یقینا وكل طاہر یقینا لاتزول طهارته بالشك شكل اول سے حد اوسط گرانے کے بعد تیمی نكلے گا ہذا الثواب لاتزول طهارته بالشك اس تقریر سے یہ ظاہر ہو گیا کہ وفرعوا الاحكام عليها کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں تھی۔ يرتفى: ارتقاء سے ہے بلند ہونا چڑھنا اور جب صلہ میں الی آئے تو معنی میں عظمت و بزرگی حاصل کرنا۔ الفقيه عالم سمجھدار (۲) اصول شریعت اور احکام سے واقف اس کا استعمال ان لوگوں کے لئے ہوتا ہے جو قرآن کریم پڑھا ئیں جمع فقہاء یہاں پر فقیہ سے مراد مقلد فی الفقہ ہے۔ الدرجة: بمعنی سیڑھی مراد یہاں مرتبہ ہے۔ الاجتهاد : اس ملکہ کو کہتے ہیں جس کی وجہ سے انسان احکام کے نکالنے پر قادر ہو جاتا ہے۔ مجتہد الفتوی: اس سے مراد وہ مجتہد ہے جو ان حوادث اور نوازل کے احکام کے نکالنے پر قادر ہو جس کے سلسلہ میں امام صاحب اور ان کے شاگردوں سے کوئی تصریح منقول نہ ہو ان کے وضع کردہ قواعد اور اصول کی روشنی میں ۔ فروع فرع کی جمع بمعنی جزئیات ۔ ظفرت : ( س ) كامیاب ہونا پا لینا۔ غريبة : كلام کا نا مانوس ہوتا اور خفی المراد ہونا جمع عزائب یہاں پر کتب غریبہ سے مراد وہ كتا میں جن تک ہم مالم کی رسائی نہ ہو۔ عترت (ن) سے کسی چیز پر مطلع ہوتا اور متعدی بعلی ہوتا ہے نہ كہ بالیا مگر یہاں كامیابی کے معنی کو شامل ہے۔ المظنة بكسر الظاء المعجمة وكان القياس فتح الظاء وانما كسر لاجل الهاء، كذاذكره الامام ابن هشام اللخمي في شرح شواهد كتاب الجمل وفى التعليل المذكور نظر فليتأمل. اس کے معنی وہ جگہ جہاں کسی چیز کے وجود کا گمان ہو جمع مظان والمظان جن کی طرف محقق رجوع کرتا ہوں ان مراجع کو كہتے ہیں۔ الحول : بمعنى قدرت في التصرف والتنبه - نبهت : واقف کرانا متنبہ کرنا۔ اس عبارت میں صاحب کتاب مشمولات کتاب پر متنبہ کر رہے ہیں فرمایا كہ میری یہ کتاب الاشباہ والنظائر جین فونی سبعہ پر مشتمل ہے ان میں پہلا قائد وان قواعد کے بیان میں سے جن کے ذریعہ بہت سی جزئیات نکالی جاتی ہں اور میتواعد كلیہ حقیقت میں اصول فقہ کی طرح ہیں اور جو ان قواعد کی مشق کرتا رہتا ہے اور ان قواعد سے قائد و انتھاتارہتا ہے تو وہ قبہ جو مقلد محض ہوتا ہے وہ بھی ترقی کر کے درجہ اجتہاد تك پہنچ جاتا ہے اس کے اندر بھی اتنی صلاحیت ولیاقت پیدا ہو جاتی ہے كہ جن حادثات و واقعات اور نوازل کے سلسلہ میں امام صاحب اور ان کے اصحاب سے كوئی روایت نہ ہودہ مقلد محض بھی امام صاحب اور ان كے شاگردوں کے وضع كردہ اصول وضوابط کی روشنی میں ان نوازل کے متعلق جزئیات كا استفہاہا واستخراج كر لیتا ہے۔ ان قواعد کی روشنی میں ان کے تحت آنے والی جزئیات كے نکالنے میں، میں نے پوری جدو جہد كی ہے اور میں نے ان جزئیات کو ایسی ایسی کتابوں میں تلاش كیا۔ جن كتابوں تك ہر ایک کی رسائی نہیں تھی چونكہ كتا ہیں دستیاب نہیں تھیں ۔ اور ایسی ایسی جگہوں سے ان جزئیات و فروعات پر میں مطلع ہوا، جہاں وہم و گمان بھی نہیں تھا۔ لیكن یہ سب كچھ بفضل خدا وندی ہے اور حتی الامكان میں نے اس كتاب میں اقوال صحیح كو نقل كرنے کی كوشش كی ہے اور جن پر مذہب میں اعتماد كیا ہے وہی روایات فقہ کی میں نے ذكر كی ہے اور اگر كسی جگہ قول ضعیف یا ضعیف روایت پر تفریع کر دی گئی ہے تو اكثر و بیشتر میں نے اس پر متنبہ كر دیا ہے فى كتـب عـزيبـة يـا عثرت في غير مظنة سے یہ شك و شبہ نہیں ہوں چاہئے كہ غیر صحیح اقوال یا ظاہر الروایہ مذہب كے خلاف روایات كو میں نے كتاب میں بھر مارا ہے۔
For example, this garment is certainly pure, and every certainly pure thing, its purity is not removed by doubt. After removing the middle term from the first figure, the conclusion becomes: this garment's purity is not removed by doubt. From this explanation it became clear that there was no need for 'and they derived the rulings upon it'. 'Yartafi': from irtiqa', meaning to rise, ascend, and when 'ila' comes in the connection, it means to attain greatness and majesty. 'Al-Faqih': a knowledgeable, understanding person, aware of the principles of Sharia and its rulings. Its usage is for those who teach the Quran. Plural: fuqaha'. Here, 'faqih' refers to a muqallid in fiqh. 'Al-Daraja': meaning a step, here meaning rank. 'Al-Ijtihad': the faculty by which a person becomes capable of extracting rulings. 'Mujtahid al-Fatwa': the mujtahid who can extract rulings for incidents and calamities for which no explicit statement from Imam (Abu Hanifa) and his students is transmitted, in the light of the rules and principles they laid down. 'Furu'': plural of far', meaning particulars. 'Zafartu': to succeed, to find. 'Gharibah': unfamiliar speech and obscure meaning; plural 'azā'ib; here 'kutub gharibah' means books to which we have no access. 'Ittala'a': to become aware of something; transitive with 'ala' not with 'bi', but here it includes the meaning of success. 'Al-Mazinnah': with kasra of the emphatic za'; the analogy would be fatha, but kasra is due to the ha', as Imam Ibn Hisham al-Lakhmi mentioned in his commentary on the shawahid of Kitab al-Jumal; there is consideration in the mentioned reasoning, so reflect. Its meaning: the place where something is expected to exist; plural 'mazānn'; 'al-mazann' refers to the references that a researcher consults. 'Al-Hawl': meaning power of disposal and awareness. 'Nabbaha': to inform, alert. In this passage, the author of the book alerts about the contents of the book. He said: My book al-Ashbah wa al-Nazā'ir comprises seven arts (funun). The first is [the art] of qawā'id (maxims) through which many particulars are derived. And these universal maxims are in reality like the principles of fiqh. And whoever continuously practices these qawā'id and persists with them, even if he is a pure muqallid, he progresses and reaches the level of ijtihad; he acquires such ability and competence that for incidents, events, and calamities for which there is no transmitted report from Imam Abu Hanifa and his companions, that pure muqallid can also deduce and extract the relevant particulars in the light of the principles and regulations laid down by Imam Abu Hanifa and his students. In extracting the particulars that fall under these qawā'id, I made every effort, and I searched for these particulars in such books to which not everyone had access, because the books were not available. And I became aware of these particulars and branches from such places where I had no suspicion. But all this is by divine favor. And as much as possible, I tried to transmit correct statements in this book, and I mentioned only those narrations of fiqh that are relied upon in the madhhab. And if at some place a weak statement or a weak narration has been used for branching (tafri'), I have, in most cases, alerted about it. So from the phrase 'in rare books or I came across in unexpected places', one should not doubt that I have filled the book with incorrect statements or narrations contrary to the relied-upon (zahir al-riwayah) madhhab.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the role of qawā'id (legal maxims) in Hanafi fiqh. The author begins with an example applying the famous maxim 'اليقين لا يزال بالشك' (Certainty is not removed by doubt) to illustrate logical deduction. He then defines key terms: 'faqih' here means a muqallid (follower) of the Hanafi school, not a independent jurist; 'daraja' is a rank; 'ijtihad' is the faculty of deriving rulings; 'mujtahid al-fatwa' is a scholar capable of issuing fatwas for new cases using the principles of imams. The author asserts that his book 'al-Ashbah wa al-Nazā'ir' contains seven arts, the first being qawā'id, which function like usul al-fiqh. He emphasizes that even a pure muqallid, by practicing these qawā'id, can ascend to the level of ijtihad and derive rulings for novel situations. The author further states his methodology: he derived particulars from rare books and unexpected sources, relying on correct and relied-upon (zahir al-riwayah) narrations, and he flagged weak narrations. This passage underscores the epistemological weight of qawā'id within the Hanafi school: they are not mere mnemonics but practical tools for extending fiqh to new cases, and they carry authority analogous to principles of usul.

Key Terms
فقيہ (faqih): Here it means a muqallid (follower) in fiqh, not an independent mujtahid.
مجتہد الفتوی (mujtahid al-fatwa): A mujtahid who can deduce rulings for new incidents by applying the qawa'id and usul set by the founding imams.
قواعد (qawa'id): Universal legal maxims from which many particular rulings are derived, functioning like principles of fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the benefit of practicing qawa'id for a muqallid?
A) He becomes a pure muqallid without any ijtihad ability.
B) He can progress to the level of ijtihad and derive rulings for new cases.
C) He must abandon the madhhab and become an independent mujtahid.
D) He memorizes more rulings without understanding principles.

Key Takeaway
Qawa'id empower a muqallid to become a mujtahid al-fatwa, enabling the Hanafi school to address novel issues while remaining faithful to its principles.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

The Guide Bears the Penalty: 'Ala al-Dall al-Jaza'
Applies the maxim to multiple hunters and guides in ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'ala al-dall al-jaza' to scenarios involving multiple hunters and guides in ihram and evaluate the cross-madhhab dispute regarding the guide's liability.

Core Idea
Guidance to hunting in ihram incurs liability—partnership in the act is even stronger.

This lesson explores the Hanafi maxim 'ala al-dall al-jaza' (the guide bears the penalty) as applied to multiple hunters and guides in the state of ihram. The passage discusses whether the penalty multiplies with the number of hunters or game, and addresses an objection from the Shafi'i school. By understanding this maxim, you will be able to determine liability in complex hunting scenarios during ihram.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its rank
Identify the maxim 'ala al-dall al-jaza' as a minor (sughra) legal maxim. Understand its meaning: the one who guides to a prohibited act is liable for the penalty.
This maxim is established by transmitted evidence and consensus.
2
Apply the maxim to the furuat
Work through the two furuat: (1) multiple hunters jointly kill a single game – each owes a penalty; (2) a guide directs the hunter – the guide is liable even if not the direct killer.
The penalty multiplies with the number of game, not with the number of doers in one game.
3
Analyze the cross-madhhab dispute
Compare the Hanafi position (guide liable) with the Shafi'i position (guide not liable). Evaluate the Hanafi response using transmitted evidence and priority of partnership.
The Hanafi school relies on the consensus of Companions like Umar, Ali, and Ibn Abbas.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Shafi'is do not impose penalty on the guide; Hanafis do. This affects fatwa in cases where multiple parties are involved in hunting.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi due to stronger evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحد اور متعدد ہونے کی صورت میں بھی جزاء واحد ہی ہوگی البتہ اگر شکار واحد ہے تو جزاء بھی واحد اور اگر شکار متعدد ہیں تو جزاء بھی متعدد و اذا كان بدلاً محضاً عنده يتعدد باتحاد المحل ويتعدد بتعدده ولا اعتبار لتعدد الفاعل ولا لاتحادہ " جب کہ ہمارے نزدیک اس میں کفارہ کے معنی بھی ہیں شکار کرنے والے اگر متعدد ہیں تو جزاء بھی متعدد ہوگی۔ اگر کوئی یہ اعتراض کرے کہ شکار میں شرکت کرنے والے پر آپ نے جزاء لازم کرنے کے لئے علی الدال الجزاء سے امام شافعی کے مد مقابل استدلال کیا ہے حالانکہ وہ رہنمائی کرنے والے پر جزاء کے قائل ہی نہیں ہیں تو آپ کا یہ استدلال علی الدال الجزاء سے امام شافعی کے مد مقابل کیسے درست ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ دلیل تحقیق میں وضاحت کے لئے مختلف فیہ سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے کیونکہ جب دلیل سماعی سے دال پر جزاء واجب ہے تو شریک پر بدرجہ اولی جزاء واجب ہوگی کیونکہ ان الشركة احــق لـوجـوب الجزاء من الدلالة بالكل ظاہر ہے۔

حضرت عمر ، حضرت علی اور حضرت عبداللہ بن عباس رضوان اللہ تعالیٰ علیہم اجمعین فرماتے ہیں کہ علی الدال الجزاء کہ رہنمائی کرنے والے پر جزاء واجب ہے۔ حضرت عطاء فرماتے ہیں کہ تمام لوگوں کا اس بات پر اتفاق ہے کہ شکار کی طرف رہنمائی کرنے والے پر جزاء واجب ہے اور انہوں نے علی الدال الجزاء کو متفق علیہ قرار دیا ہے اور امام شافعی کے اختلاف کو غیر معتبر قرار دیا ہے، تو جب دلیل سماعی سے دال پر جزاء واجب ہے تو جو قتل صید میں شریک ہوگا اس پر بدرجہ اولی جزاء واجب ہوگی ۔
Whether the penalty is single or multiple: if the game is single, the penalty is single; if the game is multiple, the penalty is multiple. 'And when it is a mere substitute according to him, it multiplies by the unity of the locus and multiplies by its multiplicity, and no consideration is given to the multiplicity of the doer nor to his unity.' While according to us, there is also the meaning of expiation in it; if the hunters are multiple, the penalty is also multiple. If someone objects: 'You have used the proof from 'ala al-dall al-jaza' to impose the penalty on the participant in hunting, while Imam Shafi'i's opponent (the guide) is not liable for the penalty according to him. How can your deduction from 'ala al-dall al-jaza' be valid against Imam Shafi'i?' The answer is that in verification of the proof, reasoning from a disputed matter is permissible for clarification, because when the transmitted evidence makes the guide liable for the penalty, then the partner is all the more liable, because partnership is more entitled to liability than guidance is. This is clear. Umar, Ali, and Abdullah ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) say: 'On the guide is the penalty' — that the guide is liable. Ata says: 'All people agree that the one who guides to the game is liable for the penalty' and he declared 'ala al-dall al-jaza' as agreed upon, and considered Imam Shafi'i's disagreement as invalid. So when the transmitted evidence makes the guide liable for the penalty, then the one who participates in killing the game is all the more liable.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a qawida (maxim) with its furuat (applications). The maxim is 'ala al-dall al-jaza' — the one who guides (to a haram act) is liable for the penalty. The context is hunting in ihram. The text first states the ruling: if multiple hunters participate, each owes a separate penalty; if the game is single, the penalty is single. Then it discusses the case of the guide (dal). The author defends the use of this maxim against those who object that Imam Shafi'i does not hold the guide liable. The Hanafi response is that the maxim is established by transmitted evidence and consensus of the Companions (Umar, Ali, Ibn Abbas) and early scholars (Ata). Therefore, it is valid to use it as a proof against the Shafi'i position. Moreover, partnership in the act (shirkah) is even more deserving of liability than mere guidance. So the Hanafi position is that both the guide and the direct hunters are liable.

Key Terms
على الدال الجزاء (ala al-dall al-jaza'): A legal maxim meaning the one who guides (to a prohibited act) is liable for the penalty.
جزاء (jaza'): The penalty (fine or expiation) for hunting in ihram.
صید (sayd): Hunting, specifically of game animals while in the state of ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in the passage, if two pilgrims in ihram jointly kill a single game, what is the penalty?
A) One penalty divided between them
B) Each owes a separate penalty
C) Only the one who struck the fatal blow owes a penalty
D) No penalty because it was unintended

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'ala al-dall al-jaza' establishes that indirect causation (guidance) incurs liability, and partnership in the act is even more deserving of penalty.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
6 min
The Qawida: Intention Not Required for Validity of Means (Wasail) – Application to Wudu
Applying the hadith interpretation to wudu: niyyah is not required for validity as a means, but only for reward.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-wasail la tushtarat fiha al-niyyah' to identify when intention is required and when it is not in acts of worship, and to evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding wudu.

Core Idea
Intention is the key to reward, not to validity – means like wudu are valid without niyyah, but only as keys to prayer, not as worship.

This passage refines our understanding of a key Hanafi qawida: intention (niyyah) is not required for the validity of means (wasail) to other acts of worship, only for the acts themselves to be counted as worship. The specific case of wudu is used to illustrate the rule and to respond to the Shafi'i argument that intention is necessary for wudu's validity. By the end, you will grasp how Hanafis distinguish between the physical prerequisite and the spiritual act, and how this distinction plays out in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
Locate the key phrase: 'wudu without intention is not commanded but is the key to prayer'. This encapsulates the maxim that means do not require intention for validity.
The maxim applies to all wasail, e.g., wudu, ghusl, covering private parts, purifying garments.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'i position relies on the Quranic verse 'When you stand up to prayer, wash your faces', interpreting 'stand up' as intention. They argue that the command to wash is conditioned on intending prayer, so intention is necessary.
This is a dalil naqli – textual evidence that appears to support their view.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses other Quranic verses about purifying garments and covering private parts, which also mention prayer. If the Shafi'i logic were consistent, those would also require intention, but they do not. This shows the Shafi'i inference is not exclusive.
This is a critical refinement – it shows the opponent's dalil proves too much.
4
Apply the maxim to the case of wudu
According to the maxim, wudu without intention is still a valid key to prayer – it fulfills the physical condition. However, it is not an act of worship, so no reward is earned.
The practical effect (thamarah) is that prayer performed with such wudu is valid in the Hanafi school.
5
Derive the fatwa hierarchy
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi. The Shafi'i position is a legitimate ikhtilaf but is not operative in the Hanafi madhhab. The maxim is rooted in the distinction between wasail and maqasid.
This lesson connects the qawida to fatwa practice.

سے استدلال کیا ہے مثلاً قرآن کی آیت ہے " إذا قمتم إلى الصلاة فاغسلوا وجوهكم " جب تم نماز کا ارادہ کرو تو اپنے چہرے کو دھو لیا کرو ۔ اس آیت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نماز کے لئے اپنے چہرہ کو دھو لیا کرو یعنی Then at that time (the hadith) does not indicate the conditionality of intention for correctness in the means (wasail) nor in the ends (maqasid). And in some books it is that the wudu which is not intended is not commanded (ma'mur bih) but it is the key to prayer. Translation: So at that time the mentioned hadith does not indicate that intention is a condition for correctness in the means nor in the ends, and in some books it is that the wudu in which intention was not made is not commanded, but it is the key to prayer. Explanation: When from the preceding detail it has become known that in the hadith, by hukm, worldly ruling is not meant but otherworldly ruling is meant, then this hadith provides no proof for or against the conditionality of intention for correctness in non-intended acts of worship, and the hadith is also silent about the obligation of intention in intended acts of worship. In some books it is explicitly stated that if someone performs wudu without intention, then according to the Hanafis, that wudu becomes the key to prayer but will not be counted as an act of worship; to make it an act of worship, intention is necessary. Whereas according to the Shafi'is, wudu without intention will not even be a cause for the key to prayer. Upon this, Imam Shafi'i and his followers have argued from many noble verses of the Quran, for example the verse 'When you stand up to prayer, wash your faces.' The meaning of this verse is: for prayer, wash your face, i.e., perform wudu. The reasoning is that 'wash your faces' in the noble verse stands in place of the result (jaza), and the result is suspended upon a condition, so 'when you stand up' means the intention for prayer, and that is called niyyah. Similarly, take another verse of the Quran: 'As for the thief, male and female, cut off their hands,' i.e., for theft. In the noble verse, cutting of the hand stands in place of the result, and theft is the condition, and the result is suspended upon conditions, i.e., the condition is a restriction for the result, and that restriction is called intention. From the first verse it is known that intention is necessary for the correctness of wudu; if intention is not made in wudu, it will not become the key to prayer. We have two answers to this: (1) The argument you made from Quranic verses is broken by other Quranic verses themselves, as in the Quran it is said: 'And purify your garments' and 'Take your adornment at every mosque.' Their meaning is: for prayer, purify your clothes, for prayer, cover your private parts. Similarly, the commentator has presented many Quranic verses which show that purifying clothes and covering private parts, etc., are for prayer?
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage applies the earlier discussion of the hadith 'Innama al-a'mal' to a specific fiqh issue: the requirement of intention (niyyah) in wudu. The author first reiterates that the hadith does not indicate that intention is necessary for validity (sihhah) in the means (wasail) like wudu, nor even in the ends (maqasid) like prayer. He then quotes from some Hanafi books that wudu without intention is not 'commanded' (ma'mur bih) in the sense of being an act of worship, but it still serves as a key to prayer, meaning it fulfills the physical requirement for prayer. The Hanafi position is clearly stated: wudu without intention is valid as a means to make prayer permissible, but it does not earn reward as an act of worship. The Shafi'i position is then presented: they argue from Quranic verses that intention is inherent in the command because the phrase 'when you stand up to prayer' indicates that the command to wash is conditioned on the intention to perform prayer. The author provides two Hanafi responses. The first response (given here) is that the same reasoning would apply to other commands related to prayer, like purifying garments and covering private parts, which are not contingent on intention in the same way. This shows that the Shafi'i argument proves too much. The passage ends abruptly but the point is clear: Hanafis maintain a distinction between the action as a means (which does not require intention) and as an act of worship (which does).

Key Terms
وسائل (wasail): Means, actions that are prerequisites for other acts of worship, e.g., wudu for prayer.
مفتاح صلوۃ (miftah al-salah): The key to prayer; wudu that fulfills the physical requirement for prayer even without intention.
مامور بہ (ma'mur bih): That which is commanded; here, an action that is both commanded and rewarded as an act of worship.
جزاء (jaza): The result or consequence of a condition; in the Shafi'i argument, the command to wash is the result suspended on the condition of intending prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is completely invalid and does not allow prayer.
B) It is valid as a key to prayer (miftah al-salah) but not as an act of worship.
C) It is valid only if the person retroactively intends.
D) It is sinful because intention is wajib.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, intention distinguishes worship from mere means; wudu without intention is a valid key to prayer but not an act of worship.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

The Hanafi Principle: Intention Not Required in Wasa'il
Clarifying that intention is not required for validity of means like wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to distinguish acts that are means (wasa'il) from ends (maqasid), and state the ruling on intention for each category.

Core Idea
Intention is required for ends, not means — wudu without intention is valid as a key to prayer but not as worship.

The famous hadith 'Innama al-a'malu bil-niyyat' (Actions are but by intentions) is often understood as requiring intention for all acts. However, the Hanafi school distinguishes between acts that are ends in themselves (maqasid) and acts that are preparatory means (wasa'il). This lesson explores that distinction and its application to wudu, ghusl, and other purifications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act: end or means?
Classify the act as either an end (maqsad) like prayer and zakat, or a means (wasila) like wudu and ghusl. This determines the role of intention.
Ends are commanded for themselves; means are commanded for the sake of something else.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for means
In means, intention is not a condition for validity (sihha). The act fulfills its purpose even without explicit intention.
Example: wudu without intention still enables prayer.
3
Apply to the furuat
List the specific acts: wudu, ghusl, wiping over khuffs, removal of impurity from clothes, body, place, and vessels. In all these, intention is not required for validity.
These are wasa'il, not maqasid.
4
Note the istithna: acts that are ends
Acts that are ends in themselves (prayer, zakat, fasting, hajj) require intention for validity by consensus and Quranic evidence.
The maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' applies fully to ends.
5
Connect to the qawida
The underlying principle is the major maxim: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are by their intentions). The dabt (sub-maxim) is: intention is required in intended acts of worship, not in means.
This qawida is a cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh.

ہماری طرف سے ان آیات کا سمجھ لینا جو تم نے اپنے استدلال میں پیش کیا ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ نیت ان جزاؤں میں ضروری ہے جن میں حکم خود مقصود ہوا اور دوسرے حکم کے لئے شرط نہ ہو اور اگر وہ جزاہ ایسا حکم ہو جو دوسرے حکم کے لئے شرط ہو تو اس میں نبیت شرط نہیں ہے۔ ہم نے جن آیات سے استدلال کیا ہے یا جن آیات قرآنیہ کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے وہ جزاء کی قسم ثانی میں سے ہے کہ وہ جزا ء ایسا حکم ہے جو دوسرے علم کیلئے شرط ہے اس لئے اس میں نیت کرنا شرط نہ ہوگا۔ پس تیا بک فطهر میں تطہیر ثوب اور خذوا زينتكم عند كل مسجد میں آرائش نماز کے لئے ہے خود مستقل حکم نہیں ہے اس لئے ان میں نیت شرط نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ آیات میں جزاء کا تعلق ان احکام سے ہے جن میں حکم خود مقصود نہیں ہے بلکہ دوسرے کیلئے شرط ہے اس لئے ان میں نیت کرنا ضروری نہ ہوگا جیسے آیت وضو میں جزاء یعنی وضو خود مقصود نہیں ہے بلکہ نماز کیلئے شرط ہے لہذا اس شرط کا بھی مطلق وجود کافی ہے اس میں قصد و نیت ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اس کی تائید اس سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ قصد وارادہ فعل اختیاری کے لئے شرط ہے فعل غیر اختیاری میں نہیں ہے اور وضو بندے کا فعل غیر اختیاری ہے تو اس میں بھی نیست وارادہ شرط نہ ہوگا یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر اعضاء وضو پر بارش کا پانی بہہ جائے یا پورے بدن پر بہہ جائے تو وضو اور غسل کی طرف سے کافی ہوگا۔ انما الاعمال بالنيات " والی حدیث سے یہ بات معلوم ہو جاتی ہے کہ وہ وضو جو قربت وعبادت ہے وہ وضو ہے جس میں نیت کی گئی ہو بدون نیست وضو قربت و عبادت نہیں بنے گی اگر چہ مفتاح صلوۃ بن جائیگی جیسا کہ قرآن و حدیث سے ثابت ہے۔ وَإِنَّمَا اشْتَرِطَتِ النِّيَّةُ فِي الْعِبَادَاتِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ أَوْ بِايَةٍ وَمَا أُمِرُوا إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُو اللَّهَ مُخْلِصِيْنَ لَهُ الدِّينَ حُنَفَاءَ وَالْاَوَّلُ أَوْجَة لأنَّ الْعِبَادَةَ بِمَعْنَى التَّوْحِيْدِ بِقَرِيْنَةِ عَطْفِ الصَّلَوةِ وَالزَّكَوةِ فَلَا تُشْتَرَطُ فِى الْوُضُوْءِ وَالْغُسْلِ وَمَسْحِ الْحُفَّيْنِ وَإِزَالَةِ النِّجَاسَةِ الْحَقِيقِيَّةِ عَنِ الثَّوْبِ وَالْبَدَنِ وَالْمَكَانِ وَالْأَوَانِي لِلصَّحَةِ. ترجمہ: اور عبادات میں نیت کو شرط قرار دیا گیا ہے صرف اجماع کی وجہ سے یا قرآنی آیت و ما امروا الا ليعبدوا الله الخ ( اور نہیں حکم دیئے گئے مگر یہ کہ عبادت کریں صرف اللہ کی ادیان باطلہ سے کٹ کر دین قیم کی طرف مائل ہو کر) کی وجہ سے اور اول دلیل زیادہ مناسب ہے اس لئے کہ عبادت تو حید کے معنی میں ہے نماز اور زکوۃ کے علف کے قرینے سے لہذا نیت وضو غسل موزوں پر مسح اور کپڑر بدن ، مکان اور برتنوں سے نجاست حقیقیہ کے زائل کرنے میں وہ صحت کے لئے شرط نہیں ہے۔
Then it is not necessary that punishment follows it; rather sometimes punishment is given and sometimes Allah forgives. However, the entitlement to punishment is established by committing sin, so the author mentioned the word 'istihqaq' with punishment. So in that case, it does not indicate the condition of intention for validity in means, nor for ends. And in some books: 'Wudu without intention is not commanded, but it is the key to prayer.' Commentary: When from the previous detail you have understood that the command in the hadith does not refer to worldly command but rather to the Hereafter, then this hadith provides no proof for intention being a condition for validity of non-intended acts of worship, nor for it not being a condition, and it is also silent regarding the obligation of intention in intended acts of worship. In some books it is stated: If someone performs wudu without intention, according to the Hanafis that wudu becomes a key to prayer but is not counted as worship. To make it worship, intention is necessary. Whereas according to the Shafi'is, wudu without intention does not even cause it to be a key to prayer. Upon this, Imam Shafi'i and his companions have argued from many noble Quranic verses. For example, the verse: 'When you rise for prayer, wash your faces.' The meaning is: for prayer, wash your faces, i.e., perform wudu. The mode of argument is that 'faghsilu wujuhakum' stands in place of the result, and the result is suspended on the condition; so it is as if the command is for prayer, and that is called intention. Similarly, another Quranic verse: 'As for the thief, male and female, cut off their hands' – i.e., for theft. In the verse, cutting the hand stands in place of the result, and theft is the condition, and the result is suspended on conditions, meaning the condition is a restriction for the result, and such a restriction is called intention. From the first verse, it is understood that intention is necessary for the validity of wudu; if one does not intend in wudu, it will not become a key to prayer. We have two responses to this. (1) The argument you made from Quranic verses is refuted by other Quranic verses themselves, such as: 'And purify your garments' and 'Take your adornment at every mosque.' Their meaning is: for prayer, purify your clothes; for prayer, cover your private parts. Similarly, the commentator has presented many Quranic verses indicating that purifying clothes and covering private parts etc. are for prayer – yet in these, intention is not required. Since these verses are similar to those you presented, then why is intention not required in them? So whatever answer you give for the verses we presented, take that as our answer for the verses you presented. The second response is that intention is required in those results where the command is an end in itself and not a condition for another command. If the result is a command that is a condition for another command, then intention is not a condition in it. The verses we argued from or indicated are of the second type: the result is a command that is a condition for another command, so intention will not be required. Thus, 'purify your garments' purifying the garment and 'take your adornment at every mosque' adorning are for prayer, not independent commands, so intention is not a condition. Similarly, in the verses presented by Imam Shafi'i, the result relates to commands that are not ends in themselves but conditions for others, so intention is not necessary. For example, the verse of wudu: the result, i.e., wudu, is not an end in itself but a condition for prayer; therefore, mere existence of this condition is sufficient, and intention and purpose are not necessary. This is supported by the fact that purpose and intention are conditions for voluntary acts, not for involuntary acts, and wudu is an involuntary act of the servant, so intention will not be a condition. This is why if rainwater flows over the limbs of wudu or over the entire body, it will suffice for wudu and ghusl. The hadith 'Actions are but by intentions' indicates that wudu that is an act of devotion and worship is the wudu in which intention is made; without intention, wudu will not become devotion and worship, though it will become a key to prayer, as established by Quran and Hadith. And intention is made a condition in acts of worship only by consensus or by the verse 'And they were not commanded except to worship Allah, being sincere to Him in religion, inclining to truth.' The first (consensus) is stronger because 'ibadah' means tawhid, by the context of the conjunction of prayer and zakat. So intention is not a condition for validity in wudu, ghusl, wiping over khuffs, and removal of actual impurity from clothes, body, place, and vessels.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a legal discussion on the role of intention (niyyah) in acts that are means (wasa'il) versus ends (maqasid). The author explains the Hadith 'Innama al-a'malu bil-niyyat' and its application to wudu and similar acts. The passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Shafi'i school argues that intention is required for the validity of wudu based on Quranic verses that treat wudu as a result suspended on condition of prayer. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, similar Quranic verses (e.g., 'And purify your garments') also imply conditions for prayer yet do not require intention; second, acts that are conditions for other acts (like wudu for prayer) are not themselves ends, so intention is not required for their validity. The text states that wudu without intention is still a valid key to prayer (miftah al-salat) but not a meritorious act of worship. The ruling concludes: intention is required only in acts that are ends in themselves (maqasid), such as prayer and zakat, not in preparatory acts (wasa'il) like wudu, ghusl, wiping over khuffs, and removal of impurity. The authority weight is from the Hanafi madhhab, and the text references consensus and Quranic verses.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; the purposeful resolve to perform an act for the sake of Allah
وسائل (wasa'il): Means or preparatory acts that are not ends in themselves
مقاصد (maqasid): Ends or goals; acts that are worship in themselves

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is intention required for the validity of wiping over khuffs?
A) Yes, intention is required for validity.
B) No, intention is not required; wiping over khuffs is a means.
C) Intention is required only if the khuffs are worn for travel.
D) Only wiping over khuffs with water requires intention.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, intention (niyyah) is a condition for validity only in acts that are ends in themselves (maqasid), not in preparatory acts (wasa'il) like wudu, ghusl, and removal of impurity.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications

The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Intention for Wudu
Clarifying that intention is not required for validity of means like wudu, with a dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on whether intention is required for wudu, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the distinction between means and ends.

Core Idea
Hanafis hold wudu valid without intention; Shafi'is require it. The debate hinges on whether wudu is an end or a means.

The requirement of intention (niyyah) for wudu is a point of contention between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. This lesson unpacks the proofs from both sides—Quranic verses and logical reasoning—and the Hanafi rebuttal that wudu, as a condition for prayer, does not require intention.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that intention is required for the validity of wudu. Without intention, wudu is invalid and prayer performed with it is void.
2
Identify the Shafi'i proof
They cite the Quranic verse: 'When you rise for prayer, wash your faces' (5:6), arguing that the command to wash is conditioned on the intention to pray, implying wudu is a result of that intention.
They also analogize with the verse on theft (5:38) where the cut is conditioned on theft.
3
State the Hanafi position and response
Hanafis respond that intention is not required for wudu. Their first response: other Quranic verses like 'purify your garments' (74:4) also command actions for prayer but do not require intention. Their second response: acts that are conditions for other acts (like wudu for prayer) are not ends, so intention is not required.
They further support by noting that wudu is involuntary (rainwater analogy).
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a person performs wudu without intention, the Hanafi school says prayer with it is valid; the Shafi'i school says it is invalid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon opinion in Hanafi fatwa, based on the maxim that intention is required only for ends, not means.
Consensus and Quran are cited for ends; the weaker opinion is the Shafi'i one.

شرط ہے اس لئے اس میں نیت کرنا شرط نہ ہوگا۔ پس تیا بک فطهر میں تطہیر ثوب اور خذوا زينتكم عند كل مسجد میں آرائش نماز کے لئے ہے خود مستقل حکم نہیں ہے اس لئے ان میں نیت شرط نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح امام شافعی کی شرط ہے لہذا اس شرط کا بھی مطلق وجود کافی ہے اس میں قصد و نیت ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اس کی تائید اس سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ قصد وارادہ فعل اختیاری کے لئے شرط ہے فعل غیر اختیاری میں نہیں ہے اور وضو بندے کا فعل غیر اختیاری ہے تو اس میں بھی نیست وارادہ شرط نہ ہوگا یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر اعضاء وضو پر بارش کا پانی بہہ جائے یا پورے بدن پر بہہ جائے تو وضو اور غسل کی طرف سے کافی ہوگا۔ انما الاعمال بالنيات " والی حدیث سے یہ بات معلوم ہو جاتی ہے کہ وہ وضو جو قربت وعبادت ہے وہ وضو ہے جس میں نیت کی گئی ہو بدون نیست وضو قربت و عبادت نہیں بنے گی اگر چہ مفتاح صلوۃ بن جائیگی جیسا کہ قرآن و حدیث سے ثابت ہے۔ وَإِنَّمَا اشْتَرِطَتِ النِّيَّةُ فِي الْعِبَادَاتِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ أَوْ بِايَةٍ وَمَا أُمِرُوا إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُو اللَّهَ مُخْلِصِيْنَ لَهُ الدِّينَ حُنَفَاءَ وَالْاَوَّلُ أَوْجَة لأنَّ الْعِبَادَةَ بِمَعْنَى التَّوْحِيْدِ بِقَرِيْنَةِ عَطْفِ الصَّلَوةِ وَالزَّكَوةِ فَلَا تُشْتَرَطُ فِى الْوُضُوْءِ وَالْغُسْلِ وَمَسْحِ الْحُفَّيْنِ وَإِزَالَةِ النِّجَاسَةِ الْحَقِيقِيَّةِ عَنِ الثَّوْبِ وَالْبَدَنِ وَالْمَكَانِ وَالْأَوَانِي لِلصَّحَةِ. ترجمہ: اور عبادات میں نیت کو شرط قرار دیا گیا ہے صرف اجماع کی وجہ سے یا قرآنی آیت و ما امروا الا ليعبدوا الله الخ ( اور نہیں حکم دیئے گئے مگر یہ کہ عبادت کریں صرف اللہ کی ادیان باطلہ سے کٹ کر دین قیم کی طرف مائل ہو کر) کی وجہ سے اور اول دلیل زیادہ مناسب ہے اس لئے کہ عبادت تو حید کے معنی میں ہے نماز اور زکوۃ کے علف کے قرینے سے لہذا نیت وضو غسل موزوں پر مسح اور کپڑر بدن ، مکان اور برتنوں سے نجاست حقیقیہ کے زائل کرنے میں وہ صحت کے لئے شرط نہیں ہے۔
Then it is not necessary that punishment follows it; rather sometimes punishment is given and sometimes Allah forgives. However, the entitlement to punishment is established by committing sin, so the author mentioned the word 'istihqaq' with punishment. So in that case, it does not indicate the condition of intention for validity in means, nor for ends. And in some books: 'Wudu without intention is not commanded, but it is the key to prayer.' Commentary: When from the previous detail you have understood that the command in the hadith does not refer to worldly command but rather to the Hereafter, then this hadith provides no proof for intention being a condition for validity of non-intended acts of worship, nor for it not being a condition, and it is also silent regarding the obligation of intention in intended acts of worship. In some books it is stated: If someone performs wudu without intention, according to the Hanafis that wudu becomes a key to prayer but is not counted as worship. To make it worship, intention is necessary. Whereas according to the Shafi'is, wudu without intention does not even cause it to be a key to prayer. Upon this, Imam Shafi'i and his companions have argued from many noble Quranic verses. For example, the verse: 'When you rise for prayer, wash your faces.' The meaning is: for prayer, wash your faces, i.e., perform wudu. The mode of argument is that 'faghsilu wujuhakum' stands in place of the result, and the result is suspended on the condition; so it is as if the command is for prayer, and that is called intention. Similarly, another Quranic verse: 'As for the thief, male and female, cut off their hands' – i.e., for theft. In the verse, cutting the hand stands in place of the result, and theft is the condition, and the result is suspended on conditions, meaning the condition is a restriction for the result, and such a restriction is called intention. From the first verse, it is understood that intention is necessary for the validity of wudu; if one does not intend in wudu, it will not become a key to prayer. We have two responses to this. (1) The argument you made from Quranic verses is refuted by other Quranic verses themselves, such as: 'And purify your garments' and 'Take your adornment at every mosque.' Their meaning is: for prayer, purify your clothes; for prayer, cover your private parts. Similarly, the commentator has presented many Quranic verses indicating that purifying clothes and covering private parts etc. are for prayer – yet in these, intention is not required. Since these verses are similar to those you presented, then why is intention not required in them? So whatever answer you give for the verses we presented, take that as our answer for the verses you presented. The second response is that intention is required in those results where the command is an end in itself and not a condition for another command. If the result is a command that is a condition for another command, then intention is not a condition in it. The verses we argued from or indicated are of the second type: the result is a command that is a condition for another command, so intention will not be required. Thus, 'purify your garments' purifying the garment and 'take your adornment at every mosque' adorning are for prayer, not independent commands, so intention is not a condition. Similarly, in the verses presented by Imam Shafi'i, the result relates to commands that are not ends in themselves but conditions for others, so intention is not necessary. For example, the verse of wudu: the result, i.e., wudu, is not an end in itself but a condition for prayer; therefore, mere existence of this condition is sufficient, and intention and purpose are not necessary. This is supported by the fact that purpose and intention are conditions for voluntary acts, not for involuntary acts, and wudu is an involuntary act of the servant, so intention will not be a condition. This is why if rainwater flows over the limbs of wudu or over the entire body, it will suffice for wudu and ghusl. The hadith 'Actions are but by intentions' indicates that wudu that is an act of devotion and worship is the wudu in which intention is made; without intention, wudu will not become devotion and worship, though it will become a key to prayer, as established by Quran and Hadith. And intention is made a condition in acts of worship only by consensus or by the verse 'And they were not commanded except to worship Allah, being sincere to Him in religion, inclining to truth.' The first (consensus) is stronger because 'ibadah' means tawhid, by the context of the conjunction of prayer and zakat. So intention is not a condition for validity in wudu, ghusl, wiping over khuffs, and removal of actual impurity from clothes, body, place, and vessels.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a legal discussion on the role of intention (niyyah) in acts that are means (wasa'il) versus ends (maqasid). The author explains the Hadith 'Innama al-a'malu bil-niyyat' and its application to wudu and similar acts. The passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Shafi'i school argues that intention is required for the validity of wudu based on Quranic verses that treat wudu as a result suspended on condition of prayer. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, similar Quranic verses (e.g., 'And purify your garments') also imply conditions for prayer yet do not require intention; second, acts that are conditions for other acts (like wudu for prayer) are not themselves ends, so intention is not required for their validity. The text states that wudu without intention is still a valid key to prayer (miftah al-salat) but not a meritorious act of worship. The ruling concludes: intention is required only in acts that are ends in themselves (maqasid), such as prayer and zakat, not in preparatory acts (wasa'il) like wudu, ghusl, wiping over khuffs, and removal of impurity. The authority weight is from the Hanafi madhhab, and the text references consensus and Quranic verses.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; the purposeful resolve to perform an act for the sake of Allah
وسائل (wasa'il): Means or preparatory acts that are not ends in themselves
مقاصد (maqasid): Ends or goals; acts that are worship in themselves

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on intention for wudu?
A) Hanafis require intention for wudu; Shafi'is do not.
B) Hanafis consider wudu without intention valid for prayer; Shafi'is do not.
C) Both schools agree, but differ on ghusl.
D) Shafi'is consider wudu without intention valid for prayer; Hanafis do not.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that intention is not required for wudu because it is a means (wasila), not an end (maqsad); the Shafi'i school holds it is required, leading to different fatwas on prayer validity.

Intention in Washing the Deceased: Principle and Branching Ruling
Clarifies intention's role and branches to drowned person wash count.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the role of intention in ghusl al-mayyit and apply the branching ruling to determine the number of washes for a drowned person given different intentions.

Core Idea
Intention is needed to discharge the communal obligation, not to purify the deceased.

This lesson clarifies a common confusion: why intention is needed when washing the deceased. The Hanafi jurists explain that intention is a condition for dropping the fard kifayah, not for the validity of the funeral prayer. They then branch this principle to the case of a drowned person, revealing an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the number of washes required.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two functions
Identify the two purposes of ghusl al-mayyit: (1) purifying the deceased for valid funeral prayer, and (2) discharging the communal obligation (fard kifayah) upon the living.
Intention is required for the second, not the first.
2
Identify the shart
State the Hanafi ruling: intention is a condition (shart) for dropping the obligation from the responsibility of the mukallafin, but not for the purity of the deceased or the validity of the prayer.
This is the core principle.
3
Apply the principle via tafri'
The author applies the principle to the drowned person (ghariq). Since the water may have already purified the body, the number of washes depends on whether the rescuer intended to fulfill the obligation when removing the body from water.
The tafri' shows how the principle yields specific rulings.
4
Compare the positions
Examine the views: Abu Yusuf says three washes regardless of intention. Muhammad says if intention at removal, two washes; otherwise three. Another narration from Muhammad says one wash.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab dispute.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later fatwa often follows Abu Yusuf's three washes, but all narrations are considered valid. The key is that intention is necessary for obligation, not for purity.
In practice, a mufti may choose any view based on preference or context.

Source Text

وَأَمَّا غُسْلُ الْمَيَّتِ فَقَالُوا لا تُشْتَرَطُ لِصِحَّةِ الصَّلوةِ عَلَيْهِ وَتَحْصِيْلِ طَهَارَتِهِ وَإِنَّمَا هِيَ شَرْطُ لِإِسْقَاطِ الْفَرْضِ عَنْ ذِمَّةِ الْمُكَلَّفِيْنَ تَفَرَّعَ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّ الْغَرِيْقَ يُغْسَلُ ثَلَاثًا فِي قَوْلِ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ وَفِي رَوَايَةٍ عَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّهُ إِنْ نَوَى عِنْدَ الْإِخْرَاجِ مِنَ الْمَاءِ يُغْسَلُ مَرَّتَيْنِ وَإِنْ لَّمْ يَنْوِ فَثَلاثاً وَعَنْهُ يُغْسَلُ مَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً كَمَا فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ. ترجمہ: اور رہا غسل میت تو فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ اس پر نماز کے صحیح ہونے اور طہارت کے حصول کے لئے نیت کو شرط قرار نہیں دیا گیا البتہ مکلفین کے ذمہ سے فرض کو ساقط کرنے کے لئے نیت شرط ہے اس پر مصنف نے تفریح پیش کی ہے کہ بقول ابی یوسف فریق کو تین مرتبہ غسل دیا جائیگا اور امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ اگر پانی سے نکالتے وقت نفس کی نیت کی تو دومرتبہ غسل دیا جائیگا اور اگر نیت نہں کی تو تین مرتبہ اور انہی سے مروی ہے کہ ایک مرتبہ غسل دیا جائیگا جیسا کہ فتح القدیر میں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب کتاب علیہ الرحمہ فرماتے ہیں جو بظاہر ایک سوال کا جواب بھی ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ جب زندہ آدمی پر بوقت غسل نیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے تو میت کو غسل دیتے وقت نیت کرنا ضروری کیوں ہے اس کا جواب پیہ ہے کہ میت کی دو حیثیتیں ہیں۔ (1) میت پاک ہو جائے تاکہ اس پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی جاسکے کیونکہ نماز جنازہ کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے میت کا پاک ہونا ضروری ہے، میت کو غسل دیئے بغیر جو نماز جنازہ پڑھی جائیگی وہ درست نہ ہوگی۔ دوسری حیثیت یہ ہے کہ زندوں پر میت کو غسل دینا ضروری ہے اور غسل دینا زندوں پر فرض کفایہ ہے۔ اس فرض
And as for washing the deceased, the jurists say that intention is not required for the validity of the prayer over him and for obtaining his purity. Rather, it is a condition for dropping the obligation from the responsibility of the legally responsible (mukallafin). Branched from this: that the drowned person is washed three times according to Abu Yusuf; and in a narration from Muhammad, if he intended at the time of removal from the water, he is washed twice, and if he did not intend, then three times; and from him, he is washed once, as in Fath al-Qadir. Translation: And regarding the washing of the deceased, the jurists say that intention is not made a condition for the validity of the funeral prayer over him and for the attainment of his purity; rather, it is a condition for dropping the obligation from the responsibility of the legally responsible. Upon this, the author branched that according to Abu Yusuf, the drowned person is washed three times; and in a narration from Muhammad, if he intended at the time of removal from the water, he is washed twice, and if he did not intend, then three times; and from him, that he is washed once, as in Fath al-Qadir. Explanation: The author says, which is also an answer to an apparent question: When on a living person at the time of bathing, intention is not obligatory, then why is intention necessary when washing the deceased? The answer is that the deceased has two aspects: (1) That the deceased becomes pure so that the funeral prayer may be performed over him, because for the validity of the funeral prayer, the purity of the deceased is necessary; the funeral prayer performed without washing the deceased will not be valid. The second aspect is that washing the deceased is obligatory upon the living, and washing the deceased is a communal obligation (fard kifayah). This obligation...
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage addresses the requirement of intention in ghusl al-mayyit (washing the deceased). The Hanafi jurists distinguish between two purposes: first, the deceased's purity to enable valid funeral prayer—for this, no intention is needed; simply washing suffices. Second, the obligation (fard kifayah) upon the living to wash the deceased—to discharge this obligation, intention is necessary. The author then presents a secondary ruling (tafri') regarding a drowned person: if the person dies in water, the ruling differs based on intention. Abu Yusuf says wash three times regardless; Muhammad says if the rescuer intended at the moment of pulling out, wash twice; otherwise three times; another narration from Muhammad says once. These differences arise from the role of intention in fulfilling the communal obligation. The text cuts off but the explanation continues.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (fard kifāyah): A collective obligation; if some Muslims perform it, the obligation is lifted from the rest; if none perform, all sin.
غريق (gharīq): A person who drowned; the rules for washing may differ due to the water's effect.
غسل الميت (ghusl al-mayyit): The act of washing a deceased Muslim; a fard kifayah upon the living.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is intention required when washing a deceased person?
A) To make the deceased pure for funeral prayer
B) To ensure the washer is in a state of ritual purity
C) To discharge the communal obligation from the living
D) Because the deceased commanded it

Key Takeaway
Intention in ghusl al-mayyit is a condition for discharging the fard kifayah, not for the validity of funeral prayer.

Intention in Tayammum and Washing the Deceased
Explains intention in tayammum and ghusl al-mayyit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida that intention is required in acts where the ruling depends on linguistic meaning or discharge of a communal obligation, and distinguish the roles of intention in tayammum and ghusl al-mayyit.

Core Idea
Intention is required in tayammum by linguistic necessity; in ghusl al-mayyit only to discharge the fard kifayah.

This passage clarifies why intention is required in two acts of purification: tayammum and washing the deceased. In tayammum, the very word means 'to intend', while in ghusl al-mayyit, intention is not needed for the validity of the funeral prayer but only for the living to fulfill their communal obligation. The Hanafi school uniquely distinguishes these cases, and the passage also explores a practical furu' about washing a drowned person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and the role of intention
Read the passage to see that intention is required in tayammum because the word 'tayammum' literally means intention, based on the Qur'anic verse. In ghusl al-mayyit, intention is not a condition for the validity of the prayer but for discharging the fard kifayah upon the living.
Focus on the different justifications for each act.
2
Analyze the dalil for tayammum
The passage cites the Qur'anic verse (5:6) using 'tayammamu' meaning 'intend'. The Hanafi position relies on the linguistic meaning being carried into the legal meaning.
3
Examine the Shafi'i counterargument and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes tayammum to wudu: if the deputy needs intention, the original needs it more. The Hanafi response is that wudu does not require intention because it is a combination of washing and wiping.
4
Understand the two aspects of ghusl al-mayyit
The deceased becomes pure through washing; intention is not needed for that. But intention is required to drop the communal obligation from the living. This leads to the subsidiary ruling on the drowned person.
5
Apply to the furu' of the drowned person
If a person drowns, the water purifies the body, but the living must still wash the deceased with intention to fulfill the fard. The number of washes differs among Hanafi imams based on intention and circumstances.
Refer to the three opinions of Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غیر مقصودہ میں شامل ہے پھر اس میں نیت کو کیوں شرط قرار دیا گیا ہے اس کا جواب مصنف دے رہے ہیں کہ تیم کے اندر نیت کے شرط ہونیکی دلیل خود آیت تیم "فلم تجدوا ماء فتيممو صعیداً طبیبا" ہے کیونکہ تمیم کے معنی ہی قصد وارادہ کے ہیں لغوی معنی کا لحاظ شرعی معنی میں بھی رکھا جاتا ہے اس لئے تمیم کے اندر نیت کو شرط قرار دیا ہے۔ اگر چہ امام شافعی بھی تیم میں نیت کو شرط قرار دیتے ہیں لیکن انہوں نے ایک بات اور فرمائی کہ تیم وضو کا نائب اور خلیفہ ہے اور جب نائب وخلیفہ کی صحت کے لئے نیت کو ضروری قرار دیا گیا ہے تو اصل یعنی وضو میں بدرجہ اولی نیت کو شرط قرار دیا جائے گا لیکن ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ وضو غسل اور مسح کا مجموعہ ہے اس میں نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے جبکہ تمیم کے معنی ہی قصد وارادہ کے ہیں لہذا وضو کو تیم پر قیاس نہیں کر سکتے ۔
بعض علماء نے ایک جواب اور بھی دیا ہے کہ طہارت کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) طہارت حقیقیہ (۲) طہارت غیر حقیقیہ ، اللہ نے پانی کو مظہر بنا کر ہی اتارا ہے اس لئے اس سے ازالہ نجاست کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں بخلاف مٹی کے اس کا وصف خاص تلویث ہے بوقت حاجت مٹی کو طہارت کے لئے استعمال کیا جاتا ہے اور حاجت کا پتہ نیت سے چلتا ہے اس لئے اس میں نیت کو شرط قرار دیا گیا ہے۔
وَأَمَّا غُسْلُ الْمَيَّتِ فَقَالُوا لا تُشْتَرَطُ لِصِحَّةِ الصَّلوةِ عَلَيْهِ وَتَحْصِيْلِ طَهَارَتِهِ وَإِنَّمَا هِيَ شَرْطُ لِإِسْقَاطِ الْفَرْضِ عَنْ ذِمَّةِ الْمُكَلَّفِيْنَ تَفَرَّعَ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّ الْغَرِيْقَ يُغْسَلُ ثَلَاثًا فِي قَوْلِ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ وَفِي رَوَايَةٍ عَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّهُ إِنْ نَوَى عِنْدَ الْإِخْرَاجِ مِنَ الْمَاءِ يُغْسَلُ مَرَّتَيْنِ وَإِنْ لَّمْ يَنْوِ فَثَلاثاً وَعَنْهُ يُغْسَلُ مَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً كَمَا فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ. ترجمہ: اور رہا غسل میت تو فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ اس پر نماز کے صحیح ہونے اور طہارت کے حصول کے لئے نیت کو شرط قرار نہیں دیا گیا البتہ مکلفین کے ذمہ سے فرض کو ساقط کرنے کے لئے نیت شرط ہے اس پر مصنف نے تفریح پیش کی ہے کہ بقول ابی یوسف فریق کو تین مرتبہ غسل دیا جائیگا اور امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ اگر پانی سے نکالتے وقت نفس کی نیت کی تو دومرتبہ غسل دیا جائیگا اور اگر نیت نہں کی تو تین مرتبہ اور انہی سے مروی ہے کہ ایک مرتبہ غسل دیا جائیگا جیسا کہ فتح القدیر میں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب کتاب علیہ الرحمہ فرماتے ہیں جو بظاہر ایک سوال کا جواب بھی ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ جب زندہ آدمی پر بوقت غسل نیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے تو میت کو غسل دیتے وقت نیت کرنا ضروری کیوں ہے اس کا جواب پیہ ہے کہ میت کی دو حیثیتیں ہیں۔ (1) میت پاک ہو جائے تاکہ اس پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی جاسکے کیونکہ نماز جنازہ کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے میت کا پاک ہونا ضروری ہے، میت کو غسل دیئے بغیر جونماز جنازہ پڑھی جائیگی وہ درست نہ ہوگی۔ دوسری حیثیت یہ ہے کہ زندوں پر میت کو غسل دینا ضروری ہے اور غسل دینا زندوں پر فرض کفایہ ہے۔ اس فرض کفایہ کو اپنے اوپر سے ساقط کرنے کے لئے نیت کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ فرض کفایہ ادا ہو جائے تو ہم نے حصول طہارت اور میت پر نماز جنازہ کے بیچ ہونے کے لئے نیت کو شرط قرار نہیں دیا ہے بلکہ مظلفین کے ذمہ سے فرض کو ساقط کرنے کیلئے ہم نے نیت کو ضروری قرار دیا ہے دونوں کے فرق کو سمجھ لیجئے۔ بقول علامہ حموی عسل دینے والے ہی کا نیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ بوقت غسل مکلفین میں سے کوئی بھی نیت کرلے سب کی طرف سے کافی ہے۔
اسی پر صاحب کتاب ایک تفریح پیش کرتے ہیں: کہ اگر کوئی شخص تالاب میں ڈوب کر مر جائے تو تالاب میں ڈوب کر مرنے سے میت پاک ہو جائیگی لیکن مکلفین کے ذمہ سے فرض کو ساقط کرنے کے لئے غریق کو غسل دینا ضروری ہے۔ غسل میت میں دو چیزیں ہیں: (۱) حصول طہارت (۲) مکلفین کے ذمہ سے فرض کو ساقط کرنا۔ ڈوب کر مرنے سے طہارت میت تو حاصل ہو جائیگی اور اس پر نماز جنازہ بھی پڑھنا درست ہوگا لیکن دوسری چیز ہے مکلفین کے ذمہ سے فرض کا ساقط ہونا اول میں نیت ضروری نہیں ہے دوسرے میں نیت کرنا ضروری ہے۔ پانی میں ڈوب کر مرنے والے کی میت کو غسل دینے کی تین صورتیں ہیں:
(1) میت کو تین مرتبہ غسل دینا ضروری ہے سی امام ابی یوسف کا قول ہے۔ (۲) امام محمد کے نزدیک اگر میت کو پانی سے نکالتے وقت غسل کی نیت کی ہے تو دومرتبہ نسل دینا ضروری ہے اور نیت نہ کرنے کی صورت میں تین مرتبہ مسل دینا ضروری ہے۔ (۳) امام صاحب کے نزدیک ایک مرتبہ غسل دیا جائیگا یہی ایک روایت امام محمد کی ہے جیسا کہ فتح القدیر میں اسکی تفصیل موجود ہے۔
It is included in non-intentional acts. Then why is intention made a condition in it? The author answers that the proof for intention being a condition in tayammum is the verse 'And you do not find water, then perform tayammum with pure earth' because tayammum literally means intention and purpose; the linguistic meaning is also considered in the legal meaning, therefore intention is made a condition in tayammum. Although Imam al-Shafi'i also makes intention a condition in tayammum, he added another point: that tayammum is a deputy and successor of wudu, and when intention is required for the validity of a deputy, then in the original (wudu) intention should be required with greater reason. But we say that wudu is a combination of washing and wiping; intention is not needed in it, while tayammum literally means intention and purpose, so wudu cannot be analogized to tayammum. Some scholars gave another answer: that purification is of two types: (1) real purification, (2) non-real purification. Allah sent down water as a manifest purifier, so intention is not a condition for removing impurity with it, unlike earth, whose specific characteristic is soiling; at the time of need, earth is used for purification, and need is known through intention, so intention is made a condition in it. As for washing the deceased, they said: intention is not a condition for the validity of the prayer over him or for obtaining his purification; rather, it is a condition for dropping the obligation from the responsibility of the legally responsible persons. Derived from this: the drowned person is washed three times according to the saying of Abu Yusuf, and in a narration from Muhammad: if he intended at the time of removal from the water, he is washed twice; if he did not intend, then three times; and from him [another narration]: he is washed once, as in Fath al-Qadir. Translation: As for washing the deceased, the jurists say that intention is not made a condition for the correctness of the prayer over him or for obtaining purification; however, it is a condition for dropping the obligation from the responsibility of the legally responsible persons. On this, the author derives: according to Abu Yusuf, the drowned person is washed three times; from Imam Muhammad, it is narrated that if he intended at the time of removal from the water, then washed twice; if he did not intend, then three times; and from him, it is narrated that he is washed once, as in Fath al-Qadir. Explanation: The author, may mercy be upon him, says, which is apparently also an answer to a question: when for a living person intention is not necessary at the time of washing, why is intention necessary when washing the deceased? The answer is that the deceased has two aspects: (1) The deceased becomes pure so that the funeral prayer can be offered over him, because for the prayer to be valid, the deceased's purity is necessary; without washing, the funeral prayer will not be valid. The second aspect is that washing the deceased is obligatory upon the living, and it is a communal obligation. To drop this communal obligation from themselves, intention is necessary so that the communal obligation is fulfilled. So we do not make intention a condition for obtaining purification or for the validity of the funeral prayer; rather, we make intention necessary for dropping the obligation from the responsibility of the legally responsible persons. Understand the difference between the two. According to al-Hamawi, it is not necessary that the one washing intends; rather, at the time of washing, any one of the legally responsible persons may intend, and it suffices for all. Upon this, the author derives: if a person drowns and dies in a pond, the deceased becomes pure by drowning, but to drop the obligation from the legally responsible persons, it is necessary to wash the drowned person. In washing the deceased, there are two things: (1) obtaining purification, (2) dropping the obligation from the legally responsible persons. By drowning, purification is obtained and funeral prayer is valid, but the second matter, dropping the obligation, requires intention. There are three scenarios for washing a drowned person: (1) It is necessary to wash the deceased three times – that is the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf. (2) According to Imam Muhammad, if he intended washing at the time of removal from the water, then washing twice is necessary; if he did not intend, then three times. (3) According to Imam Sahib, he is washed once – that is one narration from Imam Muhammad, as detailed in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rule regarding intention in tayammum and washing the deceased. The author begins by addressing why intention is required in tayammum even though it is a substitute for wudu, which does not require intention. The proof is from the Qur'anic verse (5:6) where the word 'tayammum' itself means 'to intend'. The Hanafi position is that wudu does not require intention because it is a combination of washing and wiping, and the linguistic meaning of tayammum necessitates intention. The passage then contrasts the Shafi'i position, which analogizes tayammum to wudu and argues that since the deputy needs intention, the original needs it more. The Hanafi response is that this analogy is invalid because wudu does not require intention. A second argument is presented: water is inherently purifying, so no intention is needed for removal of impurity, while earth is inherently soiling and requires intention to indicate the need. Next, the ruling on washing the deceased is discussed. Intention is not required for the validity of the funeral prayer, but it is required to discharge the communal obligation (fard kifayah). This leads to a subsidiary issue: if a person drowns, the water itself purifies him, so the deceased is already pure for prayer; however, the living must still perform ghusl to fulfill the fard kifayah. The number of washes differs among the Hanafi imams: Abu Yusuf says three, Muhammad has two narrations (two or three depending on intention, or one), and one narration from Muhammad says once. The author also notes al-Hamawi's point that intention does not have to be specifically by the one washing; any responsible person can intend on behalf of all.

Key Terms
تیمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with pure earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl
غسل المیت (ghusl al-mayyit): Washing the deceased Muslim's body before burial
نیة (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform an act of worship

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is intention required in tayammum but not in wudu?
A) Because tayammum is a substitute for wudu
B) Because the word 'tayammum' literally means intention
C) Because water is more purifying than earth
D) Because the Shafi'is require intention in wudu

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires intention in tayammum due to its linguistic meaning, and in ghusl al-mayyit only to discharge the communal obligation, not for the validity of the prayer or purification.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
Intention and Utterance in Islam and Kufr
Explaining the qawida on intention and utterance in Islam and kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi qawida that for worldly Islam, verbal declaration is sufficient without intention, and for kufr, intention is required except in mockery, and apply it to cases of coercion, jest, and inward faith.

Core Idea
Islam is valid outwardly by speech; kufr requires intent, except mockery reveals intent.

In Hanafi legal theory, the relationship between inner faith (iman) and outward submission (Islam) has distinct consequences for worldly and afterlife rulings. This passage from Sharah al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair clarifies when intention (niyyah) is required and when utterance alone suffices, using examples of coercion and mockery to delineate the boundaries of the qawida. Understanding this distinction is essential for a mufti dealing with cases of apostasy, conversion, and religious identity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Qawida
First, locate the core legal maxim: for worldly Islam, mere verbal declaration is sufficient; for kufr, intention is required. This is the rule that governs all subsequent applications.
The maxim applies to legal rulings in this world; afterlife acceptance requires inner iman.
2
Analyze the Proof
Examine the proof from the hadith of Usama and the Quranic verse on coercion. The hadith shows that the Prophet did not require inner intention after verbal declaration; the verse {Except him who is forced while his heart is at peace with faith} shows that coercion negates kufr if the heart is firm.
Note that the dalil uses both hadith (Sunnah) and Quran, giving the maxim strong evidentiary support.
3
Apply to the Coerced Person
Apply the maxim: a person coerced into uttering the shahada is considered Muslim for worldly rulings, even without inner intention. Conversely, a coerced person who utters kufr without internal consent does not become a disbeliever.
This shows that for Islam, utterance overrides lack of intent; for kufr, lack of intent overrides utterance.
4
Distinguish Mockery
The exception: uttering kufr words in jest nullifies the need for explicit intention because mockery of religion is itself an intentional act of contempt, which constitutes an implicit intention to disbelieve.
This is not a contradiction but a refinement: the qawida's 'intention' includes implicit intents like jest.
5
Derive Practical Rulings
From this qawida, derive three furuat: (a) a disbeliever who merely intends Islam but does not speak is not Muslim worldly; (b) a Muslim who intends kufr silently becomes a disbeliever even without speech; (c) a person who performs kufr actions without any intent (e.g., under hypnosis) is not a disbeliever.
These applications show the qawida's scope in ibadat, muamalat, and criminal law.
