دنیوی اسلام مطلب یہ ہے کہ دنیا کے اندر اسلامی حکومت یا اسلامی معاشرہ میں رہنے والا محض زبان سے اظہار اسلام کر دے تو اس پر اسلامی احکام جاری ہوں گے لہذا اسے اپنے وارثین کی میراث بھی ملے گی اور مسلمانوں کے قبرستان میں دفن بھی ہو گا اس حیثیت سے اظہار اسلام کافی ہے، البتہ اخروی اعتبار سے کہ اس کے ساتھ آخرت میں وہی اعزاز و اکرام کیا جائے گا جو مسلمانوں کے ساتھ کیا جائے گا تو اس کے لئے زبان و قلب سے ایمان لانا ضروری ہے محض اسلام کا اظہار کافی نہیں ہوگا۔

انقیاد باطنی کو ایمان کہتے ہیں اور انقیاد ظاہری کو اسلام کہتے ہیں۔

بصح دنیوی اسلام کے معتبر ہونے کے لئے محض اظہار اسلام کافی ہے نیت ضروری نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے کسی پر زبردستی کی اور کہا کہ اسلام قبول کر لے ورنہ جان سے مار ڈالونگا اور وہ مکروہ زبان سے اظہار اسلام کر دے تو اس کے اسلام کا اعتبار ہوگا اور اسے قتل کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا اور یہ نہیں کہا جائے گا جان بچانے کی خاطر اس نے اسلام قبول کیا ہے۔ جس کی تائید ایک حدیث سے ہوتی ہے جس میں حضرت اسامہ نے اظہار اسلام کے بعد بھی ایک آدمی کا قتل کر دیا تھا اور جب پورا واقعہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے سامنے پیش کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا ” أفلا شققت عن قلبه حتى تعلم أقالها أم لا“ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اسلام کے معتبر ہونے کے لئے اظہار اسلام کافی ہے نیت ضروری نہیں۔

ولا يكون مسلما لا یکون کی ضمیر میں دو احتمال ہیں (۱) مکرہ (۲) کافر۔ اول صورت : میں مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی پر زبردستی کی گئی اور اس نے اسلام کی نیت کر لی زبان سے کلمہ شہادتین کا تلفظ نہ کیا تو اس کا اسلام معتبر نہ ہوگا اور وہ مسلمان شمار نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اسلام اوامر و نواہی کا نام ہے اور یہ افعال صرف نیت سے ادا نہیں ہوں گے بلکہ ان کے لئے فعل کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے۔

دوسری صورت : جب یکون کی ضمیر کا مرجع کافر ہو جیسا کہ سیاق و سباق سے سمجھا جا سکتا ہے اس صورت میں مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ اگر کوئی کافر صرف اسلام کی نیت کر لے اور زبان سے کلمہ شہادتین کا تلفظ نہ کرے تو دنیوی اعتبار سے اس کا اسلام معتبر نہ ہوگا، اخروی اعتبار سے مسلمان ہوگا یا نہیں یہ تو صرف اللہ ہی جانتا ہے۔ بخلاف کفر کے اگر کوئی کفر کی نیت کر لے تو وہ کافر ہو جائے گا کیونکہ کفر کسی چیز کو چھوڑنے اور ترک کا نام ہے اور ترک فعل میں نیت کافی ہے جیسا کہ اس کی تفصیل آرہی ہے۔ واما الكفر الخ: اگر کوئی شخص اعمال کفریہ کا ارتکاب کرے لیکن اس کی نیت کفر کی نہ ہو تو محض اعمال کفریہ کرنے سے وہ شخص کافر نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اسلام کے معتبر ہونے کے لئے اظہار اسلام شرط ہے اسی طرح کافر ہونے کے لئے بھی نیت شرط ہے۔ دلیل : اس کی یہ ہے کہ فقہاء نے تصریح کی ہے کہ اگر کسی مسلمان پر جبر و اکراہ کر کے کلمات کفر [؟] زبان سے ادا کرائے گئے اور اس نے زبان سے کلمات کفریہ کا ارتکاب جان بچانے کی وجہ سے کر لیا لیکن کفر کی نیت نہ کی تو مکرہ کا کفر صحیح نہ ہو گا جیسا کہ ارشاد باری تعالی ہے {إلا من أكره وقلبه مطمئن بالإيمان} سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ کافر ہونے کے لئے دل سے کافر ہونا ضروری ہے۔

و أما قولهم إنه إذا تكلم بكلمة الكفر [؟] مذاق میں بھی کلمہ کفر نکالنا موجب کفر ہے یہ ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔

اعتراض یہ ہے کہ ابھی آپ نے بتایا کہ کافر بننے کے لئے نیت و ارادہ ضروری ہے حالانکہ فقہاء نے تصریح کی ہے کہ اگر کوئی زبان سے کفر کا کلمہ مذاق میں بھی نکال دے تو وہ کافر ہو جاتا ہے چاہے اس نے کفر کی نیت نہیں کی اس سے معلوم ہوا کفر کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ ایسے شخص کو کافر اس کی نیت اور عدم نیت کی وجہ سے نہیں کہا جا رہا ہے بلکہ دراصل مذاق میں کفریہ جملہ کہنا ہی کفر ہے 'فإنه استخفاف بالدين فهو كفر قال الله تعالى {قل أبالله وآياته ورسوله كنتم تستهزئون لا تعتذروا قد كفرتم بعد إيمانكم}

دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس نے شریعت مقدسہ کے ساتھ ہزل و استہزاء کا ارادہ کیا ہے اور ارادہ ہی کا نام نیت ہے لہذا یہاں بھی بدون نیت کافر نہ ہوا بلکہ کفر کی نیت استہزا و مذاق میں بھی پائی گئی و به يظهر فساد ما قبل ان عينه كفر الى عين الهزل بمعنى انه قصد الهزل فتحصل النية بهذا القصد
The meaning of worldly Islam is that one living in an Islamic government or society merely declares Islam verbally; then Islamic rulings apply to him. Therefore he will inherit from his heirs and be buried in the Muslim cemetery. In this respect, declaration of Islam is sufficient. However, for the afterlife, that he be honored as Muslims are honored, it is necessary to have faith in heart and tongue; mere declaration is not enough. Inward submission is called iman, and outward submission is called Islam. For worldly Islam to be valid, mere declaration is sufficient; intention is not necessary. The proof is that if someone coerced another and said 'Accept Islam or I will kill you,' and he under coercion declared Islam verbally, his Islam is valid and it is not permissible to kill him. One will not say he accepted Islam to save his life. This is supported by a hadith in which Usama killed a man after his declaration of Islam, and when the Prophet ﷺ was informed, he said: 'Why did you not split his heart to know whether he said it truthfully or not?' This hadith shows that for the validity of Islam, declaration is sufficient; intention is not necessary. The pronoun in 'la yakunu musliman' has two possibilities: (1) the coerced person, (2) the disbeliever. First: if someone is coerced and intends Islam but does not utter the shahada verbally, his Islam is not valid and he is not considered a Muslim, because Islam is obedience to commands and prohibitions, and these actions are not performed merely by intention; they require actual performance. Second: if the pronoun refers to a disbeliever, as context indicates, the meaning is that if a disbeliever merely intends Islam but does not utter the shahada, then his Islam is not valid from a worldly perspective; as for the afterlife, only Allah knows if he is a Muslim. Unlike kufr: if someone intends kufr, he becomes a disbeliever because kufr is abandonment and leaving; for omission, intention is sufficient, as details will come. As for kufr acts: if someone commits kufr acts without intending kufr, he does not become a disbeliever because for Islam to be valid, declaration is a condition; similarly, for kufr, intention is a condition. The proof: the jurists have stated that if a Muslim is forced to utter words of kufr under compulsion and he utters them to save his life but does not intend kufr, his kufr is not valid, as Allah says: 'Except him who is forced while his heart is at peace with faith'—this shows that to become a disbeliever, inner disbelief is necessary. As for their saying that uttering a word of kufr even in jest causes kufr, this is a response to an objection. The objection: You said that for kufr, intention is necessary, but jurists have stated that if someone utters a word of kufr in jest, he becomes a disbeliever even if he did not intend kufr. This shows intention is not a condition for kufr. The answer: Such a person is called a disbeliever not because of his intention or lack thereof, but because uttering a kufr statement in jest is itself kufr, for it is mockery of religion, and it is kufr. Allah says: 'Say: Is it Allah and His verses and His Messenger that you were mocking? Make no excuse; you have disbelieved after your faith.' The second answer: He intended jest and mockery of the sacred law, and intention is exactly what is meant by niyyah. So here, too, he did not become a disbeliever without intention; rather, the intention of kufr was present in the mockery. And thus the corruption of what preceded is apparent. The essence of kufr is present; the essence of jest is that he intended jest, so intention is attained by this intent.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is a detailed ruling on the conditions for the validity of Islam and kufr concerning intention and utterance. The author first distinguishes between worldly and afterlife acceptance of Islam. For worldly rulings (inheritance, burial, etc.), mere verbal declaration of Islam is sufficient, even without inner conviction. For afterlife salvation, inner faith is required. The author then defines iman as inward submission and Islam as outward submission. He argues that for worldly Islam, intention is not required, citing the example of coercion and the hadith of Usama. Next, he explains the phrase 'la yakunu musliman' (he is not a Muslim), offering two interpretations: (1) a coerced person who intends Islam but does not utter the shahada is not a Muslim worldly; (2) a disbeliever who intends Islam but does not utter it is not considered Muslim worldly. Regarding kufr, intention alone suffices for disbelief because kufr is abandonment, which is achieved by intent. However, if one performs kufr actions without intent, he does not become a disbeliever, as intention is required. The exception is mockery: uttering kufr words in jest constitutes kufr because it implies contempt for religion, which is itself an intention of kufr. The author provides two answers to the objection that mockery contradicts the requirement of intention. Thus, the rule is established: for Islam, utterance is essential; for kufr, intention is essential, except where mockery indicates intent.

Key Terms
ایمان (iman): Inward submission of the heart; required for afterlife salvation.
اسلام (islam): Outward submission through verbal declaration; suffices for worldly rulings.
نیت (niyyah): Intention (qasd); required for kufr (except mockery) but not for worldly Islam.
کفر (kufr): Disbelief; can occur by intention alone (since it is abandonment) or by mockery regardless of explicit intent.
مکرہ (mukrah): One coerced; his declaration of Islam is valid; his utterance of kufr under duress without intention does not make him a disbeliever.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for a person to be considered a Muslim for worldly legal purposes (e.g., inheritance, burial)?
A) Inner faith (iman) in the heart
B) Verbal declaration of the shahada
C) Both verbal declaration and intention
D) Performance of Islamic obligations

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi qawida: for worldly Islam, utterance is sufficient; for kufr, intention is required, but mockery inherently contains intention and thus constitutes kufr.

Intention (Niyyah) is a Condition for All Prayers
Stating the maxim that no salah is valid without niyyah, including funeral prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim that intention is required for every prayer, including the funeral prayer, and identify its scope and basis in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
No prayer is valid without intention — even the funeral prayer requires niyyah.

This lesson explores a foundational maxim from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair: intention (niyyah) is essential for the validity of all prayers, from obligatory to supererogatory. The author explicitly includes the funeral prayer, correcting a possible misconception that it might be exempt. This maxim is a branch of the broader principle that intended acts of worship require niyyah, and it forms a key anchoring point in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim
Locate the core statement: 'Thus, no prayer is valid absolutely, even the funeral prayer, except with it (intention).' This is the legal rule being established.
The Arabic 'فلا تصح صلوةٌ مطلقاً' is absolute in scope.
2
Recognize the scope
Note that the maxim covers all types of salah: fard, wajib, sunnah, nafl, and janazah. No prayer is exempt.
This includes prayers that lack ruku or sujud, like the funeral prayer.
3
Understand the usul basis
This maxim is a branch of the general rule that al-'ibadat al-maqsudah (intended acts of worship) require niyyah. The author builds on that foundation.
The maxim is a sughra (minor) qa'ida in the Hanafi qawaid hierarchy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا تصح صلوةٌ مطلقاً ولو صلوة جنازة إلا بها فرضاً أو واجباً أو سنةً أو نفلاً. ترجمہ: چنانچہ نماز مطلقا صحیح نہیں ہوتی اگر چہ نماز جنازہ ہو خواہ فرض نماز ہو یا واجب یا سنت یا نفل۔ تشریح: اوپر یہ ذکر کیا گیا تھا کہ عبادات مقصودہ بدون نیت صحیح نہیں ہوتیں اس پر تفریع کرتے ہوئے مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ کوئی بھی نماز بدون نیت صحیح نہیں ہوتی خواہ نماز جنازہ ہو یا نمازوں میں سے فرض ہو، یا واجب نفل ہو یا سنت۔

وإذا نوى قطعها لا يخرج عنها إلا بمناف ولو نوى الانتقال عنها إلى غيرها فإن كانت الثانية غير الأولى وشرع بالتكبير صار منتقلاً وإلا فلا. ترجمہ: اور جب نماز کو ختم کرنے کی نیت کر لی تو نماز سے خارج نہ ہوگا مگر ایسے عمل سے جو نماز کے منافی ہو اور اگر ایک نماز سے دوسری نماز کی طرف منتقل ہونے کی نیت کر لی اور دوسری نماز پہلی نماز کی غیر ہو اور تکبیر شروع کر دی تو منتقل ہو جائے گا ورنہ نہیں۔ تشریح: ماسبق سے معلوم ہو گیا کہ بدون نیت نماز معتبر نہ ہوگی تو اگر کسی نے اثناء صلوۃ نماز کو ختم کرنے کی نیت کر لی تو نماز ختم نہ ہوگی اور وہ نماز سے خارج نہیں ہو گا جب تک کہ کوئی ایسا کام نہ کر لے جو نماز کے خلاف ہو مثلا
Thus, no prayer is valid absolutely, even the funeral prayer, except with it (intention), whether obligatory, wajib, sunnah, or nafl. Translation: So no prayer is valid absolutely, even the funeral prayer, whether it be obligatory prayer or wajib or sunnah or nafl. Commentary: Above it was mentioned that intended acts of worship are not valid without intention; building on that, the author says that no prayer is valid without intention, whether it be funeral prayer or obligatory, wajib, nafl, or sunnah. And if he intends to cut it, he does not exit from it except with something contrary (to prayer). And if he intends to transfer from it to another [prayer], then if the second is different from the first and he begins with takbir, he becomes transferred; otherwise not. Translation: And when he intends to end the prayer, he does not exit from it except with an action that contradicts the prayer. And if he intends to transfer from it to another prayer, and the second prayer is different from the first, and he begins with takbir, then he transfers; otherwise not. Commentary: From the preceding, it became clear that prayer is not valid without intention. So if someone during prayer intends to end it, the prayer does not end and he does not exit from it until he performs an action contrary to prayer, e.g.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental maxim of Hanafi fiqh: 'No prayer is valid without intention (niyyah).' The author applies this to all types of salah, including the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah), which some might think is exempt because it does not have ruku' or sujud. The commentary explains that this maxim is a branch of the general principle that intended acts of worship (al-'ibadat al-maqsudah) require niyyah. The second part deals with the effect of intending to end the prayer or transfer to another. In Hanafi fiqh, merely intending to cut the prayer does not automatically invalidate it; one must actually perform an action that is contrary to prayer (e.g., speaking, eating, or moving excessively). Similarly, if one intends to switch from one prayer to another, the transfer only occurs if the second prayer is different (e.g., from Zuhr to Asr) and one begins with takbir. If the second is the same (e.g., intending to repeat the same prayer), transfer does not occur. This illustrates the precision of Hanafi jurisprudence: intention alone does not change the state; actual action is required.

Key Terms
صلوة (salah): Formal Islamic prayer, obligatory or supererogatory, which requires intention for validity.
نیت (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform a specific prayer; essential for the validity of salah.
قطع (qat'): To cut or end the prayer; merely intending to cut does not exit one until a contradictory action is performed.
انتقال (intiqal): Transfer from one prayer to another during salah, which requires the second prayer to be different and the initiation of takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the maxim, which of the following prayers does NOT require intention?
A) Fardh prayer
B) Funeral prayer
C) Nafl prayer
D) None – all prayers require intention

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that intention is indispensable for the validity of all prayers, including funeral prayer, and it must be present at the beginning.

The Effect of Intending to End or Switch Prayers
Explaining the effect of intending to cut or transfer salah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that merely intending to cut prayer does not invalidate it, and identify the conditions for a valid transfer to another prayer.

Core Idea
Intention alone does not end prayer; only a contrary action does.

In this lesson, we examine a subtle point: while intention is crucial to start prayer, what about the intention to end it? The Hanafi school teaches that merely thinking of ending the prayer does not invalidate it; only an actual contradictory action exits one. Similarly, intending to switch to another prayer is effective only if the second prayer is different and one begins the takbir. These rules demonstrate the principle that actions, not mere intentions, determine fiqh outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule for cutting
Read the text: 'If he intends to cut it, he does not exit from it except with something contrary (to prayer).' This means intention alone is insufficient; an action that contradicts the prayer (like speaking, eating, or excessive movement) is required.
The key phrase is 'لا يخرج عنها إلا بمناف' – does not exit except by a contrary act.
2
Identify the rule for transferring
For transferring to another prayer, two conditions are listed: (a) the second prayer must be different from the first, and (b) he must begin with takbir. Both must be present for the transfer to be valid.
If the second prayer is the same type (e.g., intending to repeat the same Zuhr), transfer does not occur.
3
Understand the rationale
Intention alone does not change the external state; the prayer remains valid until a contradictory act is performed. This underscores the Hanafi commitment to tangible actions over mere inner thoughts.
This differs from some other schools where intention alone might invalidate.

Source Text

Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental maxim of Hanafi fiqh: 'No prayer is valid without intention (niyyah).' The author applies this to all types of salah, including the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah), which some might think is exempt because it does not have ruku' or sujud. The commentary explains that this maxim is a branch of the general principle that intended acts of worship (al-'ibadat al-maqsudah) require niyyah. The second part deals with the effect of intending to end the prayer or transfer to another. In Hanafi fiqh, merely intending to cut the prayer does not automatically invalidate it; one must actually perform an action that is contrary to prayer (e.g., speaking, eating, or moving excessively). Similarly, if one intends to switch from one prayer to another, the transfer only occurs if the second prayer is different (e.g., from Zuhr to Asr) and one begins with takbir. If the second is the same (e.g., intending to repeat the same prayer), transfer does not occur. This illustrates the precision of Hanafi jurisprudence: intention alone does not change the state; actual action is required.

Key Terms
قطع (qat'): To cut or end the prayer; merely intending to cut does not exit one until a contradictory action is performed.
انتقال (intiqal): Transfer from one prayer to another during salah, which requires the second prayer to be different and the initiation of takbir.
مناف (munafin): Something contrary to prayer, such as speaking, eating, or excessive movement, which invalidates the prayer.
تكبير (takbir): The phrase 'Allahu Akbar' used to initiate the prayer; in the context of transfer, it marks the start of the new prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for a valid transfer from one prayer to another?
A) Only a sincere intention to switch
B) The second prayer must be different and one must begin with takbir
C) The second prayer must be of the same type
D) One must finish the first prayer then start again

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, intending to end prayer requires a contradictory action; transferring requires a different prayer and the initiation of takbir.

Intention Required in Apostasy: Coercion and Jest
Dissects the role of intention in rulings of kufr under coercion and jest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to distinguish between the rulings for coercion and jesting in apostasy.

Core Idea
Intent matters: coercion with a firm heart saves from kufr; jesting with religion is itself contempt and thus kufr.

The famous Hanafi maxim 'Matters are judged by their intentions' governs many areas of fiqh, including the grave matter of apostasy. This passage tackles a seeming paradox: a person coerced into uttering kufr does not leave Islam if his heart remains firm, yet a jester who jokingly says the same words becomes a disbeliever. How can both rulings be true? The answer lies in understanding what 'intention' means in each context—the coerced person intends to save his life, while the jester intends to mock, which is itself a form of disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for the coerced person
The passage first establishes that a person forced to utter kufr does not become a kafir if his heart remains firm in faith. The proof is Quran 16:106.
This is the base case.
2
Understand the proof for the coerced case
The verse explicitly saves the one coerced while his heart is firm, showing that inner conviction overrides the outward utterance.
The dalil is Quranic and clear.
3
Recognize the objection about jesting
An opponent objects: if intention is required, why do jurists rule that a jester becomes a kafir even without intending to disbelieve? This seems to contradict the rule.
The objection is a common point of confusion.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response has two parts: first, jesting with religion is inherently contempt (istikhfaf), which is itself kufr regardless of subjective intent (Quran 9:65-66). Second, the jester does have an intention—to mock—so intention is present.
The response preserves the qawida without exception.
5
Conclude the consistency
Thus both rulings are consistent: the coerced person lacks the intention to mock or disbelieve, while the jester intentionally mocks, fulfilling the requirement of intention.
The qawida remains universal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ادا کرائے گئے اور اس نے زبان سے کلمات کفریہ کا ارتکاب جان بچانے کی وجہ سے کر لیا لیکن کفر کی نیت نہ کی تو مکرہ کا کفر صحیح نہ ہو گا جیسا کہ ارشاد باری تعالی ہے الا من اكره وقلبه مطمئن بالایمان‘ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ کافر ہونے کے لئے دل سے کافر ہونا ضروری ہے۔
واما قولهم انه اذ اتكلم بكلمة الكفر " نداق میں بھی کلمہ کفر نکالنا موجب کفر ہے یہ ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔
اعتراض یہ ہے کہ ابھی آپ نے بتایا کہ کافر بننے کے لئے نیت وارادہ ضروری ہے حالانکہ فقہاء نے تصریح کی ہے کہ اگر کوئی زبان سے کفر کا کلمہ مذاق میں بھی نکالدے تو وہ کافر ہو جاتا ہے چاہے اس نے کفر کی نیت نہیں کی اس سے معلوم ہوا کفر کے لئے نیست شرط نہیں ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ ایسے شخص کو کافر اس کی نیت اور عدم نیت کی وجہ سے نہیں کہا جا رہا ہے بلکہ در اصل مذاق میں کفریہ جملہ کہنا ہی میں کفر ہے 'فانه استخفاف بالدين فهو كفر قال الله تعالى قل ابالله و آیاته ورسوله كنتم تستهزئون لا تعتذروا قد كفرتم بعد ایمانکم
دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس نے شریعت مقدسہ کے ساتھ ہنرل و استہزاء کا ارادہ کیا ہے اور ارادہ ہی کا نام نیت ہے لہذا یہاں بھی بدون نیت کا فرنہ ہوا بلکہ کفر کی نیت استہز او مذاق میں بھی پائی گئی و به يظهر فساد ماقبل
ان عينه كفر الى عين الهزل بمعنى انه قصد الهزل فتحصل النية بهذا القصد
If a person is coerced and utters words of kufr to save his life but does not intend kufr, then his kufr is not valid, as Allah said: 'Except one who is coerced while his heart is firm in faith.' This shows that to become a disbeliever, one must disbelieve in the heart. And as for their statement that when he utters a word of kufr, even in jest, it causes kufr, this is a response to an objection. The objection: You said that intention and will are necessary to become a kafir, yet jurists have stated that if a person utters a word of kufr in jest, he becomes a kafir even if he did not intend kufr. This shows that intention is not a condition for kufr. The answer: Such a person is not called a kafir because of his intention or lack thereof, but rather uttering a kufr statement in jest itself is kufr because it is contempt of religion. Allah said: 'Say: Is it Allah and His verses and His Messenger that you were mocking? Make no excuse; you have disbelieved after your belief.' A second answer: He intended mockery and ridicule of the sacred law, and intention is the same as niyyah. Thus here also it is not without intention, but rather the intention of kufr is found in jesting. And by this the corruption of the previous [objection] is shown. That which is kufr in essence is [considered] in the essence of jest, meaning he intended jest, so intention is achieved by this intent.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a legal analysis of the maxim 'Acts are judged by intentions' as applied to apostasy. It first states the rule: a coerced person does not become a kafir if his heart remains firm in faith, based on Quran 16:106. Then it addresses an objection: why then does jesting with kufr cause apostasy even without explicit intention? The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) Jest with religion is inherently contempt (istikhfaf), which is itself kufr regardless of subjective intent, as per Quran 9:65-66. (2) The jester actually intends mockery, so intention is present. The passage concludes that the jesting case does not violate the intention requirement.

Key Terms
مکرہ (mukrah): A person compelled by force or threat to do something against his will.
نية (niyyah): Deliberate intention in the heart to perform an action for a specific purpose.
هزل (hazl): Jesting or joking; speech intended as humor rather than serious statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition does a coerced person (mukrah) not become a kafir according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) If they utter words of kufr in jest
B) If their heart is firm in faith
C) If they are forced at gunpoint
D) If they are asleep

Key Takeaway
The qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' governs apostasy: coercion with firm heart prevents kufr, but jesting with religion is itself an intention to mock and thus constitutes kufr.

Intention in Salah: Essentials and Exceptions
Details the requirement of intention for the validity of salah and related rules.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to derive rulings on the role of intention in salah, including conditions for validity, effects of intending to cut or transfer, and the imam's intention.

Core Idea
Intention is essential for salah validity, but imam's intent only matters for reward, except with women.

This lesson expands the major legal maxim 'Acts are judged by intentions' into specific rules concerning salah. The text establishes that no prayer — be it fard, wajib, sunnah, nafl, or even janazah — is valid without niyyah. It then addresses edge cases: merely intending to end salah does not exit you until a contradictory act occurs; transferring from one salah to another requires a fresh takbir. Finally, it explains the nuanced role of intention for the imam versus the follower, including an intra-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the governing maxim and its scope
The lesson applies the qa'ida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to salah. Note that intention is a condition (shart), not a rukn.
This maxim is one of the five major maxims (kubra).
2
Apply the maxim to the validity condition
All salah requires intention. Even janazah? Yes, because it is an act of worship. The text explicitly includes it.
No exception except where specified.
3
Analyze the boundary of intention: ending salah
Intention to cut does not suffice; a contradictory action (munafin) is needed. Why? Because the maxim judges external actions, not mere internal thought.
The maxim 'matters by intentions' applies to the act's category, not to ending it.
4
Examine the transfer rule
Transfer from one salah to another requires starting the second with takbir, not just intention. This prevents mixing intentions.
The second salah must be different from the first.
5
Distinguish between follower and imam
Follower must intend iqtida; imam generally does not need intend imamah, except when women follow (to avoid invalidation due to alignment) and, according to some, for Jumu'ah and Eid. This shows the maxim's nuances: validity vs. reward.
The dispute with al-Karkhi and Abu Hafs al-Kabir is resolved by the majority.

Thus no salah is valid at all, even if it is a funeral prayer, whether obligatory, wajib, sunnah, or nafl. And when he intends to cut it, he does not exit from it except by an action that contradicts it. And if he intends to transfer from it to another, then if the second is different from the first and he begins with takbir, he transfers; otherwise not. And following an imam is not valid except with intention, and leading is valid without intention for it, contrary to al-Karkhi and Abu Hafs al-Kabir, as in al-Binayah, except when women pray behind him, for their following him without the imam's intention for imamah is not valid. And some exclude Friday and the two Eids, and that is correct, as in al-Khulasah. Explanation: Following is linking the prayer of the follower to the prayer of the imam. A person who prays behind another must intend to follow his imam; otherwise his prayer is not valid. However, the imam does not need to intend imamah; his leading is valid without it, though he does not earn reward for imamah because of the famous legal maxim: no reward except with intention. Imam al-Karkhi and Abu Hafs al-Kabir said that just as the follower must intend to follow, so must the imam intend to lead. Yes, in one case if an imam leads as a substitute, then he must intend imamah; otherwise his imamah is not valid, as in al-Shami. Except when women pray behind him: if women pray behind the imam, then just as the follower must intend following, so must the imam intend regarding the women. The reason is that if a woman aligns with the imam, his prayer becomes invalid, and the imam suffers such harm.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage expands the maxim 'Acts are judged by intentions' into specific salah rulings. First, it establishes that intention is a condition for the validity of all salah, including funeral prayer. Second, merely intending to end salah does not exit one from it until a contradictory action (e.g., speaking, moving excessively) occurs. Third, transferring from one fardh salah to another (e.g., zuhr to asr) requires starting the second with takbir after ending the first. Fourth, in congregational prayer, the follower must intend to follow the imam. The imam need not intend to lead, per the majority Hanafi view, contrary to al-Karkhi and Abu Hafs al-Kabir. However, if women are behind, the imam must intend to lead them to avoid invalidating his own salah if a woman aligns with him. Some scholars also require intent for Jumu'ah and Eid prayers. This illustrates how the same maxim yields nuanced rules.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Deliberate intention in the heart to perform an act of worship.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in congregational prayer by intending to follow.
امامة (imamah): Leading the congregation in prayer.
مناف (munafin): An action that contradicts the nature of salah, such as speaking, eating, or moving three consecutive limbs deliberately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the validity of congregational prayer according to the major Hanafi view?
A) The follower must intend to follow the imam.
B) The imam must intend to lead the congregation.
C) The imam's intention is required when women are behind.
D) The follower's intention is required for his salah.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' governs niyyah in salah: it is a condition for validity of the prayer itself, but for leadership it only affects reward, not validity, except where women or special prayers are involved.

beginner

Mere Thought of Leaving Prayer Does Not Break It
Ruling on the effect of mere thought of leaving prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a mere thought of breaking prayer does not invalidate the prayer, distinguishing between internal thoughts and overt actions.

Core Idea
A mere thought of leaving prayer does not break it; only action or speech does.

When you are in prayer, your mind may wander. Sometimes you might even think of stopping. Does that thought invalidate your prayer? The Hanafi school provides a clear answer: no. This lesson establishes that mere internal intention to break, without any accompanying action or utterance, leaves the prayer valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act in progress
The person has already started the prayer. No action has been taken to break it.
This is the baseline: a valid prayer is in progress.
2
Recognize the internal thought
The thought 'I am not praying' or 'I want to leave' crosses the mind.
This is a mere internal event, not external.
3
Apply the ruling
According to the source text, such mere thought does not break the prayer.
4
Distinguish from external invalidators
If the person had spoken, moved significantly, or done something contrary to prayer, that would break it.
Action matters, not thought.
5
Note the underlying principle
Internal thoughts do not affect the outward validity of the prayer; only actions or explicit utterances count.
This is a key Hanafi legal maxim applied here.

The Rule of Transferring between Prayers: Intention Alone is Insufficient
Ruling on intending to switch from one prayer to another

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that mere intention to transfer between prayers does not effect transfer until the first prayer is terminated and the second is commenced with takbir tahrimah.

Core Idea
Intending to switch prayers does not transfer you; you must end and begin afresh.

In Hanafi fiqh, intention (niyyah) is crucial, but for transferring from one prayer to another while already in prayer, intention alone is not enough. This lesson explains the precise requirement: you must conclude the current prayer and start the new one with the opening takbir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the intended transfer
Consider a person who has started one prayer (e.g., Zuhr) and then wishes to change to another (e.g., Asr). Recognize the specific sequence of actions.
2
Recognize that mere intention does not transfer
Understand that simply making the intention (niyyah) to switch does not legally change the prayer. The initial prayer continues until explicitly ended.
This is the core ruling.
3
Understand the required actions
The person must first end the current prayer (e.g., by completing it or nullifying it) and then begin the new prayer with the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah).
The opening takbir is the essential initiating act for any prayer.
4
Apply the rule to similar scenarios
Use the same principle for any case of intending to change from one prayer to another (e.g., from Maghrib to Isha, or from a supererogatory to an obligatory prayer). The method remains: terminate and restart with takbir.

Oath Not to Lead: Scope of 'Prayer' and Qada/Diyanah
Explains when leading Jumu'ah breaks an oath, but Janazah and Sajdah do not

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-yamin tuftasaru 'ala al-'urf' to determine whether an oath not to lead prayer is broken by leading Jumu'ah, Janazah, or Sajdat al-Tilawah, and distinguish between qada and diyanah rulings.

Core Idea
Leading Friday prayer breaks an oath not to lead; funeral prayer and prostration do not.

Oaths in Islamic law are interpreted according to customary usage. When someone swears not to 'lead prayer', what counts as leading prayer? This passage from the Ashbah wa al-Nazair clarifies that Jumu'ah falls under the absolute meaning of prayer, but Janazah and Sajdat al-Tilawah do not. Additionally, the distinction between qada (judicial ruling) and diyanah (religious duty) affects whether expiation is required. Understanding these nuances is essential for a mufti issuing fatwas on oath-related cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath and its scope
State the exact oath: the person swore not to lead prayer (imamah) without specifying which prayer. This is an absolute oath, and its interpretation relies on the customary understanding of 'prayer' in the Shariah.
The oath is general, so we refer to 'urf to determine what is included.
2
Analyze the three cases: Jumu'ah, Janazah, Sajdah
For each case, determine whether it is considered 'prayer' in the absolute sense. Jumu'ah is a full prayer with ruku' and sujud; Janazah has no ruku' or sujud; Sajdat al-Tilawah is only a single prostration. Only full prayers (fard or nafl) fall under the oath.
The passage explicitly states Janazah and Sajdah are outside the scope.
3
Apply the qada/diyanah distinction
In qada (judicial ruling), the external act determines the breach. For Jumu'ah, the imam's outward leading makes him hanith in qada, even if he had no intention to lead. In diyanah, intention matters: if he genuinely did not intend to lead, he may not be hanith before Allah. For Janazah and Sajdah, he is not hanith in either realm because the acts themselves are not covered by the oath.
The text mentions an analogy: traveling without intention of legal travel does not break the oath in diyanah.
4
Derive the governing legal maxim
The underlying rule is 'al-yamin tuftasaru 'ala al-'urf' (an oath is interpreted according to custom). Also relevant: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' in matters of diyanah. Note the exception: Jumu'ah triggers the oath, but Janazah and Sajdah are exceptions because they are not 'prayer' in the absolute sense.
This maxim is a qawida kubra in the Ashbah wa al-Nazair.

Source Text

In iqtida he stood with hands folded, then in that case in qada he is not a hanith, and the absence of intention for imamah is completely apparent. Likewise, if the one who swore: If the imam swore an oath that he would not lead the prayer, and then he led the Friday prayer, then in that case in qada and diyanah he becomes a hanith, and qada obligates expiation upon him, because when he swore not to lead and after the oath he led the Friday prayer, this is a sign that he was content with breaking the oath, because Friday prayer obligates at least three followers, and even if before starting the imamah he makes a witness, he still becomes a hanith and making a witness is not considered. The author said halath qada here, while in this issue in qada and diyanah he becomes a hanith. It can be interpreted that due to the absence of intention for imamah, it is as if he did not lead, and due to not leading, he will not be a hanith in diyanah, just as if someone swore an oath that he would not perform a legal travel, and he left his house without intention of legal travel, then no matter how far he goes, he will not be a hanith in diyanah. And he does not become hanith at all if he leads them in funeral prayer and prostration of recitation. Explanation: If someone swore that he will not lead, then he led the funeral prayer, the one who swore will not become hanith in his oath. Allama Humawi in Sharh Ashbah, quoting from Fatawa Qadikhan, mentioned that when he swore an absolute oath, his oath will refer to absolute prayer, and that is obligatory or supererogatory prayer; funeral prayer does not fall under absolute prayer, therefore such a person will not become hanith. And prostration of recitation: If the imam swore an oath not to lead, then he became imam in prostration of recitation, he will not become hanith and expiation is not obligatory upon him, because he swore an absolute oath not to lead, so it is referred to absolute imamah, and prostration of recitation is outside that absolute.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on oaths (yamin). It clarifies the scope of an oath not to lead prayer. When the oath is absolute (without specifying a particular prayer), it is interpreted according to the common usage of 'imamah' in Islamic law. Common usage refers to the full prayer—either fard or nafl—that is performed with the two prostrations and the salutation. Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) qualifies as a full prayer, so leading it breaks the oath in both qada (judicial ruling) and diyanah (religious duty). The author explains that even if the imam had a secret intention not to lead, the external act determines the qada ruling. For funeral prayer (Janazah) and prostration of recitation (Sajdat al-Tilawah), however, these are not considered 'prayer' in the absolute sense. Janazah has no ruku' or sujud, and Sajdat al-Tilawah is only a single prostration. Therefore, leading these does not violate the oath. The passage thus illustrates the legal maxim that an oath is interpreted according to the customary usage ('urf) of the term. The distinction between qada and diyanah is also highlighted: in qada, the external act suffices for the oath to be broken; in diyanah, the intention matters.

Key Terms
حانث (ḥānith): One who breaks an oath and becomes liable for expiation (kaffarah).
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Judicial ruling based on external evidence; outward judgment.
دیانة (diyānah): Religious duty based on inner state; one's personal responsibility before Allah.
اليمين تُفسر على العرف (al-yamin tuftasaru 'ala al-'urf): Legal maxim: An oath is interpreted according to customary usage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, because Janazah is a form of prayer.
B) No, because Janazah is not considered 'prayer' in the absolute sense.
C) Yes, only in qada but not in diyanah.
D) Yes, because he has an intention to lead.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an absolute oath not to lead prayer is broken only by leading a full prayer (fard or nafl) with ruku' and sujud; Janazah and Sajdat al-Tilawah do not count.

Oath Not to Lead a Specific Person: The Qada/Diyanah Distinction
Ruling on an oath not to lead a specific person when that person joins the prayer unintentionally.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between qada and diyanah to an oath regarding leading a specific person, and identify when the maxim 'La thawab illa bi al-niyyah' governs reward.

Core Idea
An oath is broken in qada by the outward act of leading, but in diyanah intention matters; reward requires intention.

This lesson examines a nuanced case: an imam swears not to lead Zayd, but Zayd unknowingly joins his prayer. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the outward legal ruling (qada) and the religious duty before Allah (diyanah). Understanding this distinction is crucial for a mufti when issuing fatwas.

Guided Path
1
State the Oath and Scenario
Identify the precise terms of the oath: 'I will not lead Zayd.' Then note the imam's action: he leads a group intending to exclude Zayd, but Zayd joins.
2
Identify the Apparent Act (Zahir al-Hal)
Recognize that imamah (leading) is established by the external act of taking the position of imam. The imam's inner intention does not change the external reality.
This is a key principle: rulings on oaths are based on apparent actions, not hidden intentions.
3
Distinguish Qada vs Diyanah
In qada (judicial ruling), the imam is a hanith because the act of leading Zayd occurred outwardly. In diyanah (religious duty before Allah), he is not a hanith because he did not intend to lead Zayd.
This distinction allows the mufti to give a ruling that respects both the external evidence and the internal intention.
4
Apply the Maxim on Reward
Apply the qawida 'La thawab illa bi al-niyyah' (no reward without intention). Since the imam did not intend to lead Zayd, he earns no reward for that part, even though the prayer is valid.
Validity and reward are separate: an act can be valid (sahih) yet unrewarded.
5
Determine the Fatwa Hierarchy
The mufta bihi (operative ruling for fatwa) is that the imam becomes hanith in qada and must expiate. This is the ruling based on the external act, as per the later Hanafi masters.
The mufti should also advise the imam about diyanah but the legal consequence is the qada ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if someone swore that he would not lead Zayd, and he led the people intending that he would not lead him but would lead others, then Zayd followed him, he becomes a hanith even if he did not know about it. End quote. But there is no reward for him for the imamah, and the prostration of recitation is like prayer. Translation: And if someone swore that he will not lead a particular person, and he led the people with the intention that he will not lead him and will lead others, then that particular person followed him, he becomes a hanith even if he did not know. But he will receive no reward for the imamah, and prostration of recitation is like prayer. The exclusion: Explanation: If the imam swore that he will not lead, for example, Zayd, and the imam, having this intention, led the remaining people, and that specific person regarding whom the imam swore not to lead also joined the prayer behind the imam, then the imam will become a hanith and expiation becomes obligatory upon him, whether the imam knew of his joining or not, because it has passed earlier that for imamah to occur, intention is not necessary. The imam's intention or lack thereof is a hidden matter, and a ruling is not given on a hidden matter; rather, ruling is based on the apparent. Here, imamah exists and is found, therefore the imam becomes a hanith in qada, not in diyanah, because his intention or lack thereof is between him and Allah. But no reward: If the imam did not intend imamah, then he does not receive reward for leading, because the rule is 'no reward except with intention.' Also, the imam receives reward according to the number of followers, so he will not get reward for those he did not intend to lead, even though the prayer of all is valid, because intention for imamah is not a condition for the validity of following. Quoted: In al-Durr al-Mukhtar, 'Intention of the imam for the follower is not a condition for the validity of following; rather, there is no reward when someone follows him without his intention.' (Sawi? 224)
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage addresses a more specific oath: swearing not to lead a particular person (e.g., Zayd). The ruling is that if that person joins the prayer, even without the imam's knowledge or intention, the oath is broken in qada. The reason is that imamah, as a legal act, is established by the external act of leadership; the imam's inner intention does not affect the external occurrence of imamah. Therefore, in qada (judicial ruling), he becomes liable for expiation. However, in diyanah (religious duty), since he did not intend to lead that person, he is not considered a breaker of the oath before Allah. But the outward ruling is that the oath is broken. The passage also clarifies that reward for leading is contingent upon intention; without it, the imam earns no reward. The validity of the followers' prayer, however, is not affected because intention for imamah is not a condition for the correctness of following. This distinction between validity and reward is a key Hanafi principle: acts can be valid without reward. The text also notes that in al-Durr al-Mukhtar it is stated that the imam's intention for the follower is not required for valid iqtida.

Key Terms
حانث قضاء (ḥānith qaḍāʾ): Oath-breaker in judicial ruling based on outward act.
حانث دیانة (ḥānith diyānah): Oath-breaker in religious duty based on inner intention.
لا ثواب إلا بالنية (lā thawāb illā bi al-niyyah): No reward without intention; a legal maxim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An imam swears, 'I will not lead Zayd.' He then leads a group prayer, and Zayd joins without the imam's knowledge. Does the imam become a hanith?
A) Yes, both in qada and diyanah
B) Yes, only in qada, not in diyanah
C) No, because he did not know
D) No, because he did not intend to lead Zayd

Key Takeaway
An oath broken by the outward act of leading requires expiation (qada), but reward and religious accountability depend on intention (diyanah).

The Requirement of Intention for Prostrations: A Hanafi Legal Maxim
Clarifies that these prostrations require intention and are only partially analogous to prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal maxim that 'ibadah maqsudah requires niyyah to determine the validity of Sajdat al-Tilawah, Sajdat al-Shukr, and Sajdat al-Sahw, and distinguish between their similarity to prayer and complete identity.

Core Idea
Prostrations outside prayer require intention but are not identical to prayer in all rulings.

This passage from Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair clarifies the legal status of three types of prostrations in Hanafi fiqh. The key principle is that any act of worship that is an intended goal ('ibadah maqsudah) requires intention (niyyah). However, these prostrations share only some rulings with formal prayer (salah), not all. Additionally, the passage resolves a common misunderstanding about Sajdat al-Shukr and Sajdat al-Sahw.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common requirement
Recognize that all three prostrations (tilawah, shukr, sahw) are 'ibadah maqsudah, thus niyyah is required for their validity.
The text explicitly says سجدہ تلاوت بھی نماز کی طرح عبادة مقصودہ ہے.
2
Apply the principle of partial similarity
Understand that Sajdat al-Tilawah is like prayer in some rulings (niyyah) but not in others (e.g., kaffarah for oaths). Do not over-extend the analogy.
The text warns that calling them identical in every respect is incorrect.
3
Resolve the intra-madhhab dispute and sahw ruling
For Sajdat al-Shukr, note that all agree on permissibility; the disagreement is over being Sunnah. For Sajdat al-Sahw, the intention not to perform it at the time of salam does not invalidate the prayer.
The mu'tamad is that the khilaf is in sunniyyah, not jawaz.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسجود التلاوة كالصلوة : سجدہ تلاوت بعض احکام میں نماز کی طرح ہے جیسے نماز میں نیت ضروری ہے اسی طرح سجدہ تلاوت میں بھی نیت ضروری ہے کیونکہ سجدہ تلاوت بھی نماز کی طرح عبادة مقصودہ ہے مسجود التلاوة كالصلوۃ“ سے بعض لوگوں کو وہم ہو گیا تھا جس کی وجہ سے انہوں نے اس کے بارے میں فیہ نظر کہ دیا۔ اور اگر سجدہ تلاوت اور نماز کو من کل الوجوہ ایک کہا جائے تو یہ درست نہ ہوگا کیونکہ کفارہ یمین کے الزام میں دونوں کا حکم مختلف فیہ ہے تو ماحصل یہ ہے کہ سجدہ تلاوت حقیقتہ نماز کے مانند نہیں ہے ہاں بعض احکام میں نماز کے مانند ہے۔ وَكَذَا سَجْدَةُ الشُّكْرَ عَلَى قَوْلِ مَنْ يَّرَاهَا مَشْرُوْعَةً وَالْمُعْتَمَدُ أَنَّ الْخِلَافَ فِي سُنِّيَّتِهَا لَا في الجواز وكذا سُجُودُ السَّهْوِ وَلَا تَضُرُّهُ نِيَّةُ عَدَمِهِ وَقْتَ السَّلَامِ. ترجمه اور ایسے ہی سجدہ شکر ان حضرات کے قول پر جو اس کو مشروع خیال کرتے ہیں اور معتمد یہ ہے کہ اختلاف اس کی سنیت میں ہے جواز میں نہیں اور ایسے ہی سجدہ سہو ہے اور اس کے لئے نقصاندہ نہیں عدم مجود کی نیت سلام کے وقت ۔ تشریح سجدہ شکر کی صحت کے لئے بھی نیت شرط ہے اس لئے کہ یہ بھی عبادۃ مقصودہ ہے، علامہ ابن نجیم مصری فرماتے ہیں کہ سجدہ شکر کے جواز و عدم جواز میں امام صاحب وصاحبین کے مابین کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے جس طرح حضرات صاحبین مسجدۂ شکر کر کے جواز کے قائل ہیں امام ابی حنیفہ بھی جواز کے قائل ہیں، اختلاف صرف ال کے مسنون ہونے اور مسنون نہ ہونے کے بارے میں ہے جہاں امام صاحب سے انها ليست مشروعة
And the prostration of recitation is like prayer: Sajdat al-Tilawah is like prayer in some rulings, just as intention is necessary in prayer, similarly intention is necessary in Sajdat al-Tilawah because Sajdat al-Tilawah, like prayer, is an intended act of worship. From the phrase 'the prostration of recitation is like prayer' some people had a misunderstanding, due to which they expressed a reservation about it. And if Sajdat al-Tilawah and prayer are said to be identical in every respect, it will not be correct, because in the obligation of expiation for an oath, the ruling of both is different. So the conclusion is that Sajdat al-Tilawah is not like prayer in reality; rather, it is like prayer in some rulings. And similarly, Sajdat al-Shukr (prostration of gratitude) according to those who consider it legislated, and the relied-upon opinion is that the disagreement is about its being Sunnah, not about its permissibility. And similarly, Sajdat al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness), and the intention of not performing it at the time of salam does not harm him. Translation: And similarly, the prostration of gratitude according to the opinion of those who consider it legislated, and the relied-upon opinion is that the disagreement is about its being Sunnah, not about its permissibility. And similarly, the prostration of forgetfulness, and the intention of not doing it at the time of salam does not harm him. Explanation: For the validity of Sajdat al-Shukr, intention is also a condition, because it too is an intended act of worship. Allama Ibn Nujaym al-Misri said that there is no disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifah and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the permissibility of Sajdat al-Shukr; the disagreement is only about whether it is Sunnah or not, where Imam Abu Hanifah said that it is not legislated.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage clarifies the status of various prostrations in Hanafi fiqh. First, Sajdat al-Tilawah (prostration upon reciting a verse of prostration) is likened to prayer (salah) in some rulings, particularly the requirement of intention (niyyah). However, it is not identical to prayer in all respects; for example, in the matter of expiation for an oath, a different ruling applies. Therefore, Sajdat al-Tilawah is considered a separate act of worship that shares some characteristics with prayer but is not a full prayer. Second, Sajdat al-Shukr (prostration of gratitude) is also legislated according to the school, and its validity requires intention. The difference between Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn is not about permissibility (all consider it permissible), but about whether it is Sunnah (recommended) or just permissible. Imam Abu Hanifah is reported to have said it is not legislated (laysat mashru'ah), meaning not Sunnah, while the Sahibayn consider it Sunnah. The relied-upon (mu'tamad) view is that the disagreement is in its being Sunnah, not in permissibility. Third, Sajdat al-Sahw (prostration for forgetfulness) is also discussed: if one intends not to perform it at the time of salam, that intention does not harm the validity of the prayer, because it is not an essential part but a corrective act. The common thread is that all these prostrations require intention for validity and reward, even though they differ from the full prayer.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): Prostration upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran.
سجدة الشكر (sajdat al-shukr): Prostration performed upon receiving a blessing or deliverance from harm.
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness performed at the end of prayer to correct errors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Regarding Sajdat al-Shukr (prostration of gratitude), what is the difference between Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn?
A) Abu Hanifah says it is permissible, Sahibayn say it is impermissible
B) Abu Hanifah says it is not Sunnah, Sahibayn say it is Sunnah
C) Abu Hanifah says it requires no intention, Sahibayn say it requires intention
D) Abu Hanifah says it is obligatory, Sahibayn say it is recommended

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim that 'ibadah maqsudah requires intention governs all three prostrations, but they are not fully analogous to salah.

The Role of Intention in Imamah: A Qā'idah Analysis
Ruling on imam's oath and role of intention in imamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'La thawaba illa bilniyyah' (No reward except with intention) to a case in imamah and distinguish between validity and reward.

Core Idea
Intention is not required for validity of imamah but is essential for reward.

This passage explores a nuanced application of the Hanafi legal maxim 'La thawaba illa bilniyyah'. It examines how an imam's oath can be broken even without explicit intention, while reward for leading prayer depends on intending to lead specific followers. Understanding this distinction is crucial for issuing fatwas in congregational prayer and oath-related cases.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim: 'La thawaba illa bilniyyah'
Begin by identifying the key ruling: intention is required for reward in acts of worship.
This is a sughra (minor) maxim that restricts the general principle 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
2
Identify the scope of the maxim
Explain that the maxim applies only to reward, not to the validity of the act. In imamah, intention is not a condition for the prayer to be valid.
The passage explicitly states that validity does not require intention.
3
Apply the maxim to the furu' case
If an imam leads someone without intending to lead him, the prayer is valid but the imam gets no reward for that follower.
This is the furu' given in the passage and quoted from al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
4
Recognize the istithna' (exception) in the oath scenario
In the oath example, the imam's hidden intention is not considered; he breaks his oath based on the apparent act of leading. This shows that hidden matters are not considered for legal consequences like oath-breaking.
This principle complements the maxim but is not an exception to it; it is a separate rule that hidden intentions are not counted for legal effects.
5
Draw the fatwa implication
For fatwa purposes, the mufta bihi is that intention is not a condition for validity of imamah. The maxim 'La thawaba illa bilniyyah' determines reward only.
A mufti must clearly distinguish between validity and reward to avoid confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
A. میں کا استثنا تشریح: اگر امام نے قسم کھائی کہ میں مثلا زید کی امامت نہیں کرونگا امام صاحب نے اس من کر کے بقیہ لوگوں کو نماز پڑھائی اور وہ متعین شخص جس کے بارے میں امام نے امامت نہ کرنے کی قسم کھائی تھی وہ بھی امام صاحب کے پیچھے نماز میں شریک ہو گیا تو امام صاحب حانث ہو جائیں گے اور امام پر [نیم؟] کا کفارہ لازم ہو گا خواہ امام کو اس کی شرکت کا علم ہوا ہو یا نہ ہوا ہو، اس لئے کہ یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی ہے کہ امامت کے [بیج؟] ہونے کے لئے نیت کا ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے، امام صاحب کا نیت امامت اور عدم نیست امر حفی ہے اور امر خفی پر حکم نہیں لگایا جاتا لہذا امر ظاہر پرحکم کا ترتب ہوگا یہاں وہ امامت ہے اور وہ پائی گئی اس لئے امام صاحب حانث ہو جائیں گے قضا نہ کہ دیا یہ اس لئے کہ اس کا نیت کرنا یا نہ کرنا فيما بينه وبين اللہ معاملہ ہے ۔ ولكن لاثواب : اگر امام نے امامت کی نیت نہ کی تو امامت کرنے پر ثواب مرتب نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ قاعدہ ہے لاثواب الا بالنية ، نیز امام کو مقتدیوں کی تعداد کے اعتبار سے ثواب ملتا ہے لہذا جن کی امامت نہیں کرے گا ان کی امامت کا ثواب امام کو نہ ملے گا اگر چہ نماز سب کی صحیح ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ صحت امامت کے لئے امام کا امامت کی نیت کرنا شرط نہیں ہے ۔ " وفى الدر المختار ولا يشترط لصحة الاقتداء نية امامة المقتدى بل ليس الثواب عند اقتداء احد به قبله ( شای جراس (۲۲۴)
A. Exception in intention. Explanation: If the imam swore that he will not lead, for example, Zaid, and the imam led the remaining people in prayer, and that specific person about whom the imam swore not to lead also joined the prayer behind the imam, then the imam becomes guilty of oath-breaking and the expiation of the oath becomes obligatory upon him, whether the imam knew of his joining or not, because it has passed earlier that for the occurrence of imamah intention is not necessary. The imam's intention or non-intention of imamah is a hidden matter, and a ruling is not based on a hidden matter, so the ruling is attached to the apparent matter, which is imamah, and it occurred, therefore the imam becomes guilty of oath-breaking. It is not said that he did not intend it, because his intending or not intending is between him and Allah. But no reward: If the imam did not intend imamah, then no reward is attached to leading, because the rule is 'no reward except with intention.' Also, the imam receives reward according to the number of followers, so the reward for leading those whom he did not intend to lead will not be given to the imam, even though the prayer of all is valid, because for the validity of imamah, the imam's intention of imamah is not a condition. And in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 'For the validity of following, the follower's intention of imamah is not a condition; rather, there is no reward when one follows him without intention.'
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on an imam's oath and the role of intention in imamah. It explains that if an imam swore not to lead a specific person, but that person joins his congregational prayer, the imam breaks his oath because imamah is established externally regardless of the imam's inner intention. Intention is a hidden matter, so the ruling is based on the apparent act of leading. However, for reward, intention is essential: without intending to lead the specific person, the imam gets no reward for that person's prayer, though the prayer is valid. The quoted text from al-Durr al-Mukhtar confirms that intention is not a condition for the validity of following but affects reward.

Key Terms
حنث (hanith): Breaking an oath, incurring liability for expiation.
نیت (niyyah): Intention; in this context, the imam's intention to lead a specific person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, which of the following is correct regarding an imam's intention to lead a specific follower?
A) It is a condition for the follower's prayer to be valid.
B) It is a condition for the imam to receive reward for leading that follower.
C) It is not required at all, neither for validity nor reward.
D) It is required for validity but not for reward.

Key Takeaway
Intention in imamah distinguishes between validity (no intention needed) and reward (intention required).

Intention in Sujood: The Qawida Applied
Application of a qawida to three sujood types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'كل عبادة مقصودة تحتاج إلى نية' to sujood al-tilawah, sujood al-shukr, and sujood al-sahw, and identify the correct timing of intention for each.

Core Idea
Intention is the spine of every independent worship—including all three special prostrations.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair establishes a key qawida: every independent act of worship requires intention (niyyah). It then tests this qawida against three types of prostration: tilawah, shukr, and sahw. For the mufti, the practical question is when intention must be present, especially for sujood al-sahw, where the timing differs from the other two. Let us trace the application of this qawida step by step.

Guided Path
1
Recall the Qawida
State the maxim: 'Every independent act of worship requires intention.' Understand that 'independent' (maqsudah) means the act is an end in itself, not a part of another worship.
This qawida is a sughra (minor) maxim, but its furuat cover all three sujood types.
2
Identify Each Sujood as Independent Worship
Classify sujood al-tilawah, sujood al-shukr, and sujood al-sahw as ibadat maqsudah (independent acts of worship). Note that sujood al-tilawah is like prayer in some rulings but not all, yet it is still independent.
Sujood al-sahw is attached to prayer but becomes independent after salam for the purpose of this qawida.
3
Apply the Qawida and Note Timing Nuances
For sujood al-tilawah and sujood al-shukr, intention must be present at the start of the prostration. For sujood al-sahw, intention is required at the time of performing the two sajdas (after salam), not at the salam itself.
This nuance is captured in the dabt (restriction) of the qawida: intention at the time of performance, not at salam.
4
Recognize the Disagreement on Sujood al-Shukr
The passage clarifies that the khilaf among Hanafi imams is only about whether sujood al-shukr is sunnah or not (sunniyyah), not about its permissibility (jawaz). All agree it is permissible and requires intention.
The mufti should rely on the permissibility and treat it as sunnah according to the fatwa hierarchy.

امام ابی حنیفہ بھی جواز کے قائل ہیں، اختلاف صرف ال کے مسنون ہونے اور مسنون نہ ہونے کے بارے میں ہے جہاں امام صاحب سے انها ليست مشروعة منقول ہے تو وہ سجدہ شکر کے وجوب کی نفی ہے یعنی امام صاحب کے نزدیک سجدہ شکر واجب نہیں ہے ( تفصیل کے لئے دیکھئے عمدۃ الایضاح شرح نور الایضاح ج ۲ ص ۳۶) سجدہ شکر کو مجمع عام میں کرنے سے بچنا چاہئے تا کہ لوگ اسے فرض یا واجب نہ سمجھنے لگیں اگر کوئی تنہائی میں کرتا ہے تو پھر اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ وكذا سجود السهو: جس طرح صحت صلوۃ کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے اسی طرح سجدۂ سہو کی صحت کے لئے بھی نیت ضروری ہے نیت کے بغیر سجدہ سہو درست نہ ہوگا۔ (الاشباہ مع الحموی ص ۳۶) ولا تضره نية عدمه وقت السلام : یہ بات ماقبل میں واذانوى قطعها لا يخرج عنها الا بمناف کے تحت گذر چکی ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص نماز کو قطع کرنے کی نیت کرے تو جب تک وہ منافی صلاۃ عمل نہ کرے اس وقت تک اس کی نماز منقطع نہ ہوگی یہ مسئلہ بھی اصلا اسی عبارت سے متعلق ہے چنانچہ اس مسئلہ کو اسی کے ساتھ ذکر کرنا چاہئے تھا۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ محض منافی صلاۃ عمل سے نیت کے بغیر آدمی نماز سے نکل جاتا ہے تو اب اگر کسی شخص نے سجدہ سہو کے لئے سلام پھیر اور بوقت سلام اس کی سجدہ سہو کی نیت نہیں تھی تو اس سے نہ سجدہ سہو میں کوئی فرق آئیگا اور نہ نماز نوٹے گی کیونکہ نیت سجدہ سہو کے لئے بوقت سلام ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ بوقت اداء سجدہ ضروری ہے اور یہاں نفس نیست موجود ہے اگر چہ بوقت سلام استحضار نیت نہیں ہے اس لئے عبارت یہ ہونی چاہئے تھی "لا نصر مريد السجود نية عدم السجود وقت السلام"
And prostration of recitation is like prayer: prostrating during recitation is like prayer in some rulings, just as intention is necessary in prayer, similarly intention is necessary in prostration of recitation, because prostration of recitation is also an independent act of worship like prayer. Some people were deluded by the statement 'prostration of recitation is like prayer' and therefore they considered it the same in every respect. But if prostration of recitation and prayer are said to be identical in all respects, that is not correct, because in the obligation of expiation of an oath the ruling of the two differs. So the conclusion is that prostration of recitation is not really like prayer; rather, it is like prayer in some rulings. And likewise the prostration of gratitude according to those who consider it legislated; and the relied-upon position is that the disagreement is regarding its being sunnah, not regarding its permissibility. And likewise the prostration of forgetfulness, and it is not harmed by the intention of its absence at the time of salam. Explanation: For the validity of prostration of gratitude, intention is also a condition, because it too is an independent act of worship. Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says that there is no disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifah and the two companions regarding the permissibility of prostration of gratitude; they all consider it permissible. The disagreement is only regarding its being sunnah or not. The statement attributed to Imam Abu Hanifah that 'it is not legislated' is a negation of its obligation, meaning that according to Imam Abu Hanifah it is not obligatory. (For details see 'Umdat al-Idah Sharh Nur al-Idah vol. 2 p. 36). It is better to avoid performing prostration of gratitude in public gatherings so that people do not consider it obligatory or necessary; if one does it in private, there is no harm. And likewise prostration of forgetfulness: just as intention is necessary for the validity of prayer, similarly intention is necessary for the validity of prostration of forgetfulness; without intention, prostration of forgetfulness is not valid. (al-Ashbah ma'a al-Hamawi p. 36). And the intention of its absence at the time of salam does not harm it: This issue has already passed under the topic 'and if he intends to cut it, he does not exit it except with an act contrary to prayer.' If a person intends to cut the prayer, as long as he does not perform an act contrary to prayer, his prayer is not cut off. This issue is also originally related to this expression, so it should have been mentioned with it. The issue is: a person exits prayer by merely doing an act contrary to prayer without intention. So if a person performed salam for the purpose of prostration of forgetfulness and at the time of salam he did not have the intention of prostration of forgetfulness, then neither does it affect the prostration of forgetfulness nor does the prayer become invalid, because intention for prostration of forgetfulness is not necessary at the time of salam, but rather at the time of performing the prostration. And here the act of prostration is present even though at the time of salam he did not have the presence of intention. Therefore, the expression should have been: 'The intention of not prostrating at the time of salam does not harm the one who intends to prostrate.'
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage discusses the necessity of intention for various types of prostration in Hanafi fiqh. First, it explains that sujood al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) is like prayer in some rulings but not all; intention is required because it is an independent act of worship. However, it differs from prayer in that its absence does not invalidate the prayer. Then it covers sujood al-shukr (prostration of gratitude), clarifying that all Hanafi jurists agree on its permissibility; the difference is only regarding whether it is sunnah. Intention is also required for its validity. Finally, it addresses sujood al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness): intention is required at the time of performing the prostration, but not at the time of salam. If a person performs salam intending to do sujood al-sahw, but at the moment of salam he does not have the intention for it, the prostration is still valid as long as he intends it when actually prostrating.

Key Terms
سجدہ تلاوت (sajdah al-tilawah): Prostration performed when reciting a verse of prostration in the Quran.
سجدہ شکر (sajdah al-shukr): Prostration performed upon receiving a blessing or deliverance from calamity.
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is intention required for sujood al-sahw?
A) At the time of salam
B) At the time of performing the prostration
C) At the beginning of prayer
D) Intention is not required

Key Takeaway
Every independent act of worship, including sujood al-tilawah, shukr, and sahw, requires intention, but for sujood al-sahw the intention is needed at the act itself, not at the preceding salam.

Intention in Friday and Eid Khutbah
Ruling on the necessity of intention for the validity of the Friday and Eid sermons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-khutbah qa'imah maqam al-rak'atain' to determine when intention is required for the khutbah and identify the practical furu' from the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
The khutbah substitutes two rak'ahs; therefore, intention is required for its validity.

In the Hanafi madhhab, the Friday khutbah is not merely a sermon but legally stands in the place of two rak'ahs of Zuhr prayer. This substitutional role carries implications, most notably the requirement of intention (niyyah) for the khutbah to be valid. This lesson unpacks that ruling, its basis in the qawida, and its concrete applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Qawida
Locate the ruling maxim that governs this case: 'al-khutbah qa'imah maqam al-rak'atain' (the khutbah stands in the place of two rak'ahs). Understand that this is a dabt (sub-maxim) within the scope of Friday and Eid prayers.
This qawida directly links the khutbah to the status of prayer (salah).
2
Understand the Legal Reasoning (Ta'lil)
Since the khutbah is a substitute for two rak'ahs, it inherits the conditions of salah, including intention (niyyah). The passage cites Fath al-Qadir: 'Because it has been placed in the position of two rak'ahs, what is required for prayer is required for it.'
The argument is qiyas: the khutbah is analogized to prayer in its essential condition.
3
Apply to the First Furu' (Sneeze Case)
Consider the furu': a khatib sneezes after ascending the minbar and says 'Alhamdulillah' without intending it as part of the khutbah. Applying the qawida, the khutbah is invalid because the required intention is absent.
The utterance alone does not constitute khutbah; the intention is what makes it an act of worship.
4
Apply to the Eid Khutbah
The same ruling extends to the Eid khutbah because the Hanafis state that the conditions for Friday khutbah apply to Eid khutbah as well, except that the Eid khutbah comes after the prayer. Thus intention remains a condition.
The exception regarding sequence does not affect the requirement of intention.
5
Relate to the Maxim 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha'
The qawida here parallels the major maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions). The intention distinguishes a ritual act from a mere habit. This reinforces the ruling.
Both maxims together explain why intention is crucial for the khutbah's validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا النِّيَّةُ لِلْخُطْبَةِ فِي الْجُمُعَةِ فَشَرْطُ صِحَّتِهَا حَتَّى لَوْعَطَسَ بَعْدَ صُعُوْدِ الْمِنْبَرِ فَقَالَ الحَمْدُ لِلَّهِلِلْعُطَاسِ غَيْرَ قَاصِدٍ لَهَا لَمْ نَصِحُ كَمَا فِى فتح القَدِيرِ وَغَيْرِهِ وَخُطْبَةُ العِيْدَيْنِ كَذَالِكَ لِقَوْلِهِمْ يُشْتَرَطُ لَهَا مَايُشْتَرَطُ لِخُطْبَةِ الْجُمُعَةِ سِوى تَقْدِيمِ الْخُطْبَةِ. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال جمعہ کے خطبہ کے لئے نیت کرنا پس وہ اس کے [بیج؟] ہونے کی شرط ہے حتی کہ منبر پر چڑھنے کے بعد اگر چھینک آگئی پس اس نے خطبہ کا ارادہ کئے بغیر چھینک کی وجہ سے الحمد للہ کہا تو خطبہ درست نہ ہو گا فتح القدیر وغیرہ میں ایسا ہی ہے اور خطبہ عیدین کا حکم بھی یہی ہے اس لئے کہ فقہاء کا قول ہے جو شرائط اس کے لئے ہیں وہی شرائط خطبہ جمعہ کے لئے ہیں علاوہ خطبہ کے مقدم کرنے کے۔ تشریح: خطبہ جمعہ کی صحت کے لئے نیت شرط ہے یا نہیں اس کا دار ومدار اس پر ہے کہ خطبہ ظہر کی دورکعتوں کے قائم مقام ہے یا نہیں؟ جن کے نزدیک دورکعتوں کے قائم مقام ہے ان کے نزدیک صحت خطبہ جمعہ کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے اور جس کے نزدیک دورکعتوں کے قائم مقام نہیں ہے ان کے یہاں خطبہ جمعہ بدون نیت بھی صحیح ہو جائیگا لیکن شارح اشباہ نے عنایہ کے حوالہ سے نقل کیا ہے کہ اب سب کے نزدیک دور کعت کے قائم مقام ہے اس لئے نیت ضروری ہے۔ وفی فتح القدير لانها اقيمت مقام الركعتين يشترط لها ما اشترط للصلاة (فتح القديري ردم (۵۹) اس پر تفریح پیش کرتے ہیں کہ اگر خطیب نے منبر پر چڑھنے کے بعد چھینک آنے پر الحمد اللہ کہا اور خطبہ کی نیت
And as for intention for the Friday khutbah, it is a condition for its validity, so that if he sneezes after ascending the minbar and says 'Alhamdulillah' for the sneeze without intending the khutbah, it does not become valid, as in Fath al-Qadir and others. And the khutbah of the two Eids is similar, because they say that the conditions required for it are the same as those required for the Friday khutbah, except for preceding the khutbah. Explanation: The validity of the Friday khutbah depends on whether it stands in place of the two rak'ahs of Zuhr. For those who consider it standing in place of two rak'ahs, intention is necessary for the validity of the Friday khutbah. For those who do not consider it standing in place of two rak'ahs, the khutbah is valid without intention. But the author of Sharh al-Ashbah has narrated from al-Inayah that now everyone considers it standing in place of two rak'ahs, so intention is necessary. And in Fath al-Qadir: 'Because it has been placed in the position of two rak'ahs, what is required for prayer is required for it.' (Fath al-Qadir, vol. 5 p. 59). Based on this, they explain that if the khatib sneezes after ascending the minbar and says Alhamdulillah without intending khutbah...
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage discusses the requirement of intention for the Friday and Eid khutbahs. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that intention is a condition for the validity of the khutbah. The reasoning is that the khutbah stands in place of two rak'ahs of Zuhr prayer during Friday prayer. Therefore, since intention is required for prayer, it is also required for khutbah. The passage cites Fath al-Qadir and other authorities. It also notes that although there was a difference of opinion, the later scholars agreed that khutbah is a substitute for two rak'ahs, so intention is necessary. An example is given: if a khatib sneezes after ascending the minbar and says 'Alhamdulillah' without intending it as part of the khutbah, the khutbah is not valid.

Key Terms
خطبہ (khutbah): The sermon delivered during Friday or Eid prayer.
نیت (niyyah): Intention to perform the khutbah as part of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if a khatib sneezes after ascending the minbar and says 'Alhamdulillah' without intending the khutbah, what is the ruling?
A) The khutbah is valid because he said Alhamdulillah.
B) The khutbah becomes invalid.
C) The khutbah is valid but he should repeat it.
D) It depends on whether the followers heard.

Key Takeaway
Intention is a condition (shart) for the Friday and Eid khutbah because the khutbah is a legal substitute for two rak'ahs of prayer.
