Intention (Niyyah) for Sujood al-Sahw
Explains that niyyah is necessary for validity of sujood al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that intention is required for sujood al-sahw and identify the correct timing of that intention.

Core Idea
Intention is essential for sujood al-sahw, but it is required at prostration, not at salam.

This lesson examines the ruling that intention (niyyah) is necessary for the validity of sujood al-sahw, the prostration of forgetfulness. The author clarifies a common misunderstanding: intention must be present at the moment of performing the prostration, not at the salam that precedes it. This precision is crucial for correct practice and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Read the first sentence: intention is necessary for the validity of sujood al-sahw, just as for prayer.
This is a direct statement from the text.
2
Locate the sub-issue
The author then discusses a case: if a person says salam intending sujood al-sahw but had no intention at the moment of salam, does it affect the sujood?
The example clarifies timing.
3
Extract the correct timing
The text states that intention for sujood al-sahw is required at the time of performing the sujood, not at the salam.
This is the key distinction.
4
Refine the expression
The author corrects a previous formulation to avoid confusion: the better phrasing is 'la yadurru mureedu as-sujood niyyatu 'adam as-sujood waqt as-salam'.
This shows how precise language matters in legal texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا سجود السهو: جس طرح صحت صلوۃ کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے اسی طرح سجدۂ سہو کی صحت کے لئے بھی نیت ضروری ہے نیت کے بغیر سجدہ سہو درست نہ ہوگا۔ (الاشباہ مع الحموی ص ۳۶) ولا تضره نية عدمه وقت السلام : یہ بات ماقبل میں واذانوى قطعها لا يخرج عنها الا بمناف کے تحت گذر چکی ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص نماز کو قطع کرنے کی نیت کرے تو جب تک وہ منافی صلاۃ عمل نہ کرے اس وقت تک اس کی نماز منقطع نہ ہوگی یہ مسئلہ بھی اصلا اسی عبارت سے متعلق ہے چنانچہ اس مسئلہ کو اسی کے ساتھ ذکر کرنا چاہئے تھا۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ محض منافی صلاۃ عمل سے نیت کے بغیر آدمی نماز سے نکل جاتا ہے تو اب اگر کسی شخص نے سجدہ سہو کے لئے سلام پھیر اور بوقت سلام اس کی سجدہ سہو کی نیت نہیں تھی تو اس سے نہ سجدہ سہو میں کوئی فرق آئیگا اور نہ نماز نوٹے گی کیونکہ نیت سجدہ سہو کے لئے بوقت سلام ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ بوقت اداء سجدہ ضروری ہے اور یہاں نفس نیست موجود ہے اگر چہ بوقت سلام استحضار نیت نہیں ہے اس لئے عبارت یہ ہونی چاہئے تھی "لا نصر مريد السجود نية عدم السجود وقت السلام"
Similarly, sujood al-sahw: just as intention is necessary for the validity of prayer, similarly intention is necessary for the validity of sujood al-sahw. Without intention, sujood al-sahw will not be valid. (al-Ashbah ma'a al-Hamawi, p. 36). And the statement 'la tadurruhu niyyatu 'adamihi waqt al-salam': This matter has already passed under the topic of 'wa idha nawa qat'aha la yakhruju 'anha illa bimunaf' such that if a person intends to cut off prayer, as long as he does not perform an act contrary to prayer, his prayer is not cut off. This issue is also originally related to this statement, so it should have been mentioned with it. The issue is that a person exits prayer merely by performing an act contrary to prayer without intention. So now if a person performed salam for sujood al-sahw, and at the time of salam he did not have the intention of sujood al-sahw, then that will not affect sujood al-sahw nor will the prayer be invalid because intention for sujood al-sahw is not necessary at the time of salam, but rather at the time of performing the sujood. And here the act itself (nafs) of salam exists even if there was no presence of intention at the time of salam. Therefore the expression should have been: 'la yadurru mureedu as-sujood niyyatu 'adam as-sujood waqt as-salam'.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the requirement of intention (niyyah) for sujood al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). The author first states that, just like prayer itself, sujood al-sahw requires niyyah for validity; without it, the prostration is invalid. He then addresses a specific sub-issue: if a person performs the salam (salutation) intending to do sujood al-sahw, but at the moment of salam he had no intention of sujood al-sahw, does that affect the sujood? The answer is no, because the necessary intention for sujood al-sahw is required at the time of performing the sujood, not at the salam. The author criticizes the phrasing of a previous text, suggesting it should be corrected to 'la yadurru mureedu as-sujood niyyatu 'adam as-sujood waqt as-salam' (the one intending sujood is not harmed by the absence of intention for sujood at the time of salam).

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sajdah sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
نیت (niyyah): Intention; a necessary condition for the validity of acts of worship including sujood al-sahw.
سلام (salam): The salutation to end prayer; here it is the preceding act to sujood al-sahw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is intention (niyyah) necessary for sujood al-sahw according to this passage?
A) At the time of salam
B) At the time of performing the sujood
C) At the beginning of prayer
D) At the time of recitation

Key Takeaway
Intention is necessary for sujood al-sahw, and it must be present at the time of prostration, not at the salam.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Intention for Khutbah of Jumu'ah and Eid
Ruling on the requirement of intention for Jumu'ah and Eid khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on intention for Jumu'ah khutbah and evaluate the opposing view from al-Khaniyah.

Core Idea
Intention is required for the validity of Jumu'ah khutbah because it stands in place of two rak'ahs of Zuhr.

A critical issue in the fiqh of Jumu'ah is whether the khatib must intend the khutbah for it to be valid. This lesson examines the majority Hanafi position, the reasoning behind it, and a minority opposing view. You will learn the preferred ruling and how it applies in practice, including its extension to Eid khutbah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and the Example
Read the first part of the passage: intention is a condition for Jumu'ah khutbah. The example of sneezing and saying 'Alhamdulillah' without intention invalidates the khutbah.
The example is from Fath al-Qadir.
2
Understand the Basis: Standing in Place of Rak'ahs
The ruling rests on the view that the khutbah stands in place of two rak'ahs of Zuhr. Hence, it requires what prayer requires, including intention.
This is the foundational reasoning for the majority.
3
Recognize the Ikhtilaf from al-Khaniyah
The author of al-Khaniyah holds that the khutbah is a non-intended act of worship, so intention is not required for validity. Understand the basis: it does not stand in place of rak'ahs.
Al-Khaniyah's view would validate the khutbah even without intention.
4
Note the Tarjih (Preferred View)
The passage indicates that the majority, including Fath al-Qadir and Sharh al-Ashbah, adopt the view that intention is required. This is the operative position for fatwa.
The tarjih is based on the stronger proof that khutbah stands in place of rak'ahs.
5
Apply to Eid Khutbah and Note Differences
The same rule applies to Eid khutbah, with three differences: (1) khutbah is necessary for Jumu'ah, optional for Eid; (2) order relative to prayer; (3) degree of dislikedness of speaking during khutbah.
Eid khutbah follows the same conditions mutatis mutandis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

پر ہے کہ خطبہ ظہر کی دورکعتوں کے قائم مقام ہے یا نہیں؟ جن کے نزدیک دورکعتوں کے قائم مقام ہے ان کے نزدیک صحت خطبہ جمعہ کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے اور جس کے نزدیک دورکعتوں کے قائم مقام نہیں ہے ان کے یہاں خطبہ جمعہ بدون نیت بھی صحیح ہو جائیگا لیکن شارح اشباہ نے عنایہ کے حوالہ سے نقل کیا ہے کہ اب سب کے نزدیک دور کعت کے قائم مقام ہے اس لئے نیت ضروری ہے۔ وفی فتح القدير لانها اقيمت مقام الركعتين يشترط لها ما اشترط للصلاة (فتح القديري ردم (۵۹) اس پر تفریح پیش کرتے ہیں کہ اگر خطیب نے منبر پر چڑھنے کے بعد چھینک آنے پر الحمد اللہ کہا اور خطبہ کی نیت نہیں کی تو خطبہ نہیں ہوگا بلکہ خطبہ کے لئے خطبہ کی نیت سے کہنا ضروری ہے صاحب فتح القدیر صاحب عنا یہ نے اسی کو رائج قرار دیا ہے۔ (۲) صاحب خانیہ نے خطبہ جمعہ کو عبادة غير مقصودہ قرار دیا ہے اس لئے اگر خطیب نے ممبر پر چڑھنے کے بعد چھینک آنے پر بغیر خطبہ کے ارادے کے الحمد للہ کہا تو وہ خطبہ جمعہ کے قائم مقام ہوگا اسلئے کہ ان کے نزدیک خطبہ جمعہ ظہر کی دورکعتوں کے قائم مقام نہیں ہے اور جب ان کے قائم مقام نہیں ہے تو یہ خطبہ جمعہ عبادہ مقصود ہ بھی نہیں اور عبادہ غیر مقصودہ میں نیت بھی ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ نیت صرف اجر و ثواب کے لئے ہے۔ نیز خانیہ میں ہے کہ اگر چھینک کی وجہ سے الحمد للہ کہتے ہوئے جانور دبج کر دیا تو وہ ذبیح حلال نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ ذکر اللہ ذبح پر ہی شرط ہے اور ذکر اللہ بغیر قصد وارادہ کے متحقق نہیں ہوتا۔ و خطبة العيدين: خطبہ جمعہ اور خطبہ عیدین دونوں کی شرائط برابر ہیں پس جس طرح خطبہ جمعہ میں نیت شرط ہے اسی طرح خطبہ عیدین میں بھی نیت شرط ہے۔ البتہ خطبہ جمعہ و خطبہ عیدین میں چند بنیادی فرق ہے (۱) جواز جمعہ کے لئے خطبہ کا ہوناضروری ہے نماز عیدین کے لئے خطبہ ضروری نہیں (۲) جمعہ میں خطبہ نماز پر مقدم ہوتا ہے جبکہ عیدین میں بعد میں ہوتا ہے البتہ کسی نے اگر مقدم کر دیا تو اس کا اعادہ نہیں ہوگا (۳) خطبہ جمعہ کے دوران کلام کرے میں جو کراہت ہے اس درجہ کی کراہت عیدین کے خطبہ کے درمیان کلام کرنے میں نہیں ہے۔ (فتح القدیر پیروت ج ۲ ص ۷۸)
As for intention for the khutbah of Jumu'ah, it is a condition for its validity, such that if after ascending the minbar he sneezes and says 'alhamdulillah' for the sneeze without intending the khutbah, it is not valid, as in Fath al-Qadir and others. And the khutbah of the two Eids is likewise, because of their statement: 'The same conditions are required for it as for the khutbah of Jumu'ah except for the precedence of the khutbah.' Explanation: Whether intention is a condition for the validity of the Jumu'ah khutbah depends on whether the khutbah stands in place of the two rak'ahs of Zuhr. Those who hold that it does stand in place require intention; those who hold it does not consider the khutbah valid without intention. However, Sharh al-Ashbah narrates from al-Inayah that now all consider it to stand in place of the two rak'ahs, so intention is necessary. In Fath al-Qadir: 'Because it has been made to stand in place of two rak'ahs, it requires what is required for prayer.' He then elaborates: if the khatib, after ascending the minbar, sneezes and says 'alhamdulillah' without intending khutbah, the khutbah does not count; it is necessary to recite with the intention of khutbah. The author of al-Khaniyah considers the Jumu'ah khutbah as a non-intended act of worship, so if after ascending the minbar he says 'alhamdulillah' without intending khutbah, it suffices for the Jumu'ah khutbah, because in his view the khutbah does not stand in place of two rak'ahs, and when it does not stand in place, it is not an intended act of worship, and in non-intended acts of worship, intention is not necessary; intention is only for reward. Also in al-Khaniyah: if while saying 'alhamdulillah' due to sneeze he slaughters an animal, it is not halal because dhikr of Allah is a condition for slaughter and dhikr without intent is not realized. And the khutbah of the two Eids: the conditions of Jumu'ah and Eid khutbah are equal; just as intention is a condition in Jumu'ah khutbah, similarly intention is a condition in Eid khutbah. However, there are several basic differences: (1) For the validity of Jumu'ah, khutbah is necessary; for Eid prayer, khutbah is not necessary. (2) In Jumu'ah, khutbah precedes prayer; in Eid, it follows. But if someone precedes it, it is not repeated. (3) The dislikedness of speaking during Jumu'ah khutbah is not present to the same degree during Eid khutbah. (Fath al-Qadir, Beirut, vol. 2, p. 78)
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the requirement of intention for the khutbah of Jumu'ah and Eid. It begins by stating that intention is a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah khutbah, illustrating with an example: if the khatib sneezes after ascending the minbar and says 'alhamdulillah' without intending the khutbah, the khutbah is invalid. This is based on the view that the khutbah stands in place of two rak'ahs of Zuhr, and thus requires the same conditions as prayer. The passage then presents an ikhtilaf (dispute): the author of al-Khaniyah holds that the khutbah is not an intended act of worship, and therefore intention is not required for validity, only for reward. The passage then explains that the khutbah of the two Eids follows the same rules, with three differences: (1) khutbah is necessary for Jumu'ah but not for Eid, (2) order of presentation, and (3) degree of dislikedness of speech during khutbah.

Key Terms
خطبہ جمعہ (khutbah jumu'ah): The sermon delivered before the Jumu'ah prayer, considered a condition for its validity.
عبادہ غیر مقصودہ (ibadah ghayr maqsudah): An act of worship not intended for its own sake; intention is not required for validity.
قائم مقام (qa'im maqam): Standing in place of; the khutbah is considered to stand in the place of two rak'ahs of Zuhr for the purpose of fulfilling the Jumu'ah obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, is intention required for the validity of Jumu'ah khutbah?
A) Yes, because it stands in place of two rak'ahs
B) No, because it is a non-intended act
C) Only for Eid, not Jumu'ah
D) Only for reward, not validity

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi view requires intention for Jumu'ah and Eid khutbah because it stands in place of two rak'ahs of Zuhr.

Intention and the Validity of Adhan: A Hanafi Rasm al-Mufti Rule
Rasm al-mufti rule on intention for adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the role of intention in adhan and distinguish between conditions for validity and conditions for reward.

Core Idea
Intention is required for reward, not for validity — adhan without niyyah is valid but unrewarded.

The adhan is a communal sunnah, but does it require intention? This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair clarifies a common confusion: niyyah is a condition for thawab (reward), not for sihhah (validity). For the mufti, this distinction is crucial when answering questions about the adhan of someone who may have called absentmindedly.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
The passage begins by asserting that intention is not a condition for validity of adhan. Identify this clear statement.
Focus on the phrase 'la tushtrat li sihhatihi al-niyyah'.
2
Distinguish validity from reward
The passage then adds that niyyah is a condition for reward. Explain the difference between shurut al-sihhah (conditions for validity) and shurut al-thawab (conditions for reward).
This is a key Hanafi distinction in many acts of worship.
3
Define adhan
The passage provides both linguistic and terminological definitions. Understand the scope of what is being ruled upon.
Adhan is a specific announcement with known words.
4
Apply the ruling
Consider a scenario: a mu'adhdhin calls adhan without niyyah. The adhan is valid but no reward. Confirm the consequence.
The Sunnah is fulfilled even though the caller misses reward.
5
Relate to the qawida
This falls under the broader principle that acts of worship may have distinct conditions for validity and reward. Identify the relevant maxim (e.g., 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' applied to adhan).
Not all acts require intention for validity; adhan is a clear example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْآذَانُ فَلَا تُشْتَرَطُ لِصِحْتِهِ النِّيَّةُ وَإِنَّمَا هِيَ شَرْطٌ لِلثَّوَابِ عَلَيْهِ. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال اذ ان تو اس کی صحت کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ اس پر ثواب کے لئے شرط ہے۔ تشريح الاذان في اللغة الاعلام وفي الاصطلاح هو اعلام بوقت الصلوة بالفاظ معلومة ماثورة على صفة مخصوصة (عمدة الايضاح شرح نور الایضاح، ج مراض کرے ۲۷ ) مشہور قول کے مطابق اذان کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے نیت ضروری نہیں ہے اگر موذن نے بدون نیت اذان دی دی تو اذان کی سنت ادا ہو جائیگی البتہ مؤذن کو اس کی اذان کا ثواب نہیں ملے گا۔ (حاشیہ احمدی مع الا شباس (۳۷)
As for the adhan, intention is not a condition for its validity; rather it is a condition for reward upon it. Explanation: Adhan linguistically means announcement, and terminologically it is announcement of the time of prayer with known transmitted words in a specific manner. (Umdat al-Idah Sharh Nur al-Idah, vol. 2, p. 27) According to the well-known position, intention is not necessary for the validity of the adhan. If the mu'adhdhin gives the adhan without intention, the Sunnah of adhan is fulfilled, but the mu'adhdhin will not receive the reward for his adhan. (Hashiyah Ahmadi ma'a al-Ashbah, p. 37)
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on the role of intention (niyyah) in adhan. It states clearly that intention is not a condition for the validity (sihhah) of adhan; rather, it is a condition for receiving reward (thawab). This means that if a person calls the adhan without specifically intending it, the adhan is still legally valid and the Sunnah is fulfilled. However, the caller will not be rewarded for it. The passage further defines adhan both linguistically and terminologically, confirming the well-known Hanafi position.

Key Terms
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer, comprising specific phrases, used to announce the time of prayer.
نیت (niyyah): Intention; here it is distinguished between condition for validity and condition for reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on intention for the validity of adhan?
A) Intention is a condition for validity
B) Intention is not a condition for validity
C) Intention is only for the imam
D) Intention is fard

Key Takeaway
Intention is a condition for reward but not for validity in the Hanafi ruling on adhan.

Intention for Facing Qibla: Reconciling a Difference
Reconciliation of a difference on intention for qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the necessity of intention for facing the qibla and apply the contextual reconciliation to issue a fatwa.

Core Idea
Facing the qibla needs no separate intention; the prayer's intention covers it.

This passage from the Ashbah wa al-Nazair tradition presents a refined ruling on the role of intention (niyyah) in facing the qibla. Imam al-Jurjani held that intention is a condition for its validity, but the established Hanafi position—rooted in al-Mabsut—is that no separate intention is required. The scholars reconciled these views by contextualizing al-Jurjani's opinion to cases where the qibla is not obvious, such as in the open desert. Understanding this refinement is crucial for a mufti applying the correct fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting views
First, note the two positions: (1) Al-Jurjani's view that intention is required for facing qibla to be valid, (2) the 'sahih' (correct) view from al-Mabsut that intention is not required.
The sahih view is the authority of the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the sources of authority
The passage cites al-Mabsut for the sahih view and al-Binayah for the reconciliation. Al-Mabsut is a foundational text of Zahir al-Riwayah; al-Binayah is a later commentary that refines the ruling.
Understanding the hierarchy of sources helps in tarjih (preference).
3
Understand the contextual reconciliation
Some scholars interpreted al-Jurjani's condition to apply only when praying in the desert, where the qibla is not clearly marked. When praying towards a mihrab (prayer niche), the general rule applies—no separate intention.
This reconciliation shows how a seemingly conflicting rule is limited to exceptional circumstances.
4
Apply the fatwa hierarchy
For fatwa, the mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that intention for facing qibla is not required. The reconciliation tempers a potential over-application of al-Jurjani's view. Always default to the sahih position unless the case clearly falling under the exception (e.g., indeterminate qibla in the desert).
The common error is to treat al-Jurjani's view as general; the fatwa hierarchy shows it is marjuh (weaker).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا اِسْتِقْبَالُ الْقِبْلَةِ فَشَرَطَ الجُرْجَانِيُّ لِصِحَتِهِ النِّيَّةُ وَالصَّحِيحُ خِلَافُهُ كَمَا فِي الْمَبْسُوْطِ وَحَمَلَ بَعْضُهُمُ الْأَوَّلَ عَلَى مَا إِذَا كَانَ يُصَلِّي فِي الصِّحْرَاءِ وَالثَّانِي عَلَى مَا إذَا كَانَ يُصَلِّى إِلَى مِحْرَابِ كَذَا فِي الْبِنَايَةِ. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال استقبال قبلہ تو اس کی صحت کے لئے امام جرجانی نے نیت کو شرط قرار دیا ہے اور تا اس کے برخلاف ہے جیسا کہ مبسوط میں ہے اور بعض نے اول کو اس صورت پر محمول کیا ہے جب وہ صحراء میں نماز پڑھ رہا ہو اور دوسری صورت کو اس پر محمول کیا ہے جب وہ محراب کی طرف نماز پڑھ رہا ہو، بنا یہ میں ایساہی ہے۔
As for facing the qibla, al-Jurjani conditioned intention for its validity, but the correct [view] is the opposite, as in al-Mabsut. And some carried the first on the case when he prays in the desert, and the second on when he prays toward the mihrab. Such is in al-Binayah.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage addresses the requirement of intention for facing the qibla (istiqbal al-qiblah) in prayer. It mentions that Imam al-Jurjani considered intention a condition for its validity. However, the correct (sahih) position is that intention is not required, as stated in al-Mabsut. The passage then reconciles these views: some scholars restricted al-Jurjani's opinion to cases where the person prays in an open desert (where the qibla is not obvious), while the general ruling applies when praying towards the mihrab (a clearly designated prayer niche). This reconciliation is found in al-Binayah. Thus, the default ruling is that intention is not a condition for facing the qibla; intention is only needed for the act of prayer itself.

Key Terms
استقبال قبلہ (istiqbal al-qiblah): Facing the qibla during prayer; a condition for prayer's validity.
نِیَّة (niyyah): Intention; a mental resolve to perform an act of worship for the sake of Allah.
مِحْرَاب (mihrab): A niche in a mosque indicating the direction of the qibla.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reconciliation presented in the passage, when is intention required for facing the qibla?
A) Always, as per al-Jurjani
B) Only when praying in a desert without a clear marker
C) Only when praying toward a mihrab
D) It is never required, as per al-Mabsut

Key Takeaway
Facing the qibla does not require a separate intention except possibly when the qibla is not obvious, and even then the majority Hanafi position is lenient.

Intention in Worship: Validity vs. Reward — Four Applications
Applying the rule that intention is not required for validity to khutbah, adhan, istiqbal, and satr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim that intention is not required for validity except where stipulated to the four cases of khutbah, adhan, facing the qiblah, and covering the awrah, distinguishing between validity (sihhah) and reward (thawab).

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, intention (niyyah) is required for reward but not always for validity – the exception proves the rule.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi legal maxim: intention is not required for the validity of an act of worship unless the Lawgiver has explicitly stipulated it. The passage from Sharah al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair applies this maxim to four distinct acts: the Friday khutbah, the adhan, facing the qiblah, and covering the awrah. You will learn not only the rulings but also how the Hanafi school reasons about intention, especially in cases where an act is 'unintended' (ghayr maqsudah) for its own sake.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its classification
Determine whether the act is an 'intended worship' (ibadah maqsudah) or an 'unintended worship' (ibadah ghayr maqsudah). Unintended acts are means to an end, not ends in themselves.
Khutbah is considered by some as ghayr maqsudah, while adhan, istiqbal, and satr are typically classified as means.
2
Determine if intention is stipulated for validity
Check if there is a clear textual stipulation (nass) requiring intention for the act's validity. For example, wudu and salah explicitly require intention, but adhan does not.
The Hanafi principle: 'لا تُشْتَرَطُ النِّيَّةُ لِصِحَّةِ العِبَادَةِ إِلَّا حَيْثُ شُرِطَتْ'.
3
Apply the maxim: no intention needed for validity unless stipulated
If intention is not stipulated, the act is valid even without it. Record whether the act is still valid and what that means for the worshipper's obligation.
For adhan, istiqbal, and satr, the majority holds intention is not required for validity.
4
Check the reward implication
Even if valid, reward (thawab) is contingent on intention. Without intention, the act is valid but unrewarded. The exception is when the act is invalid due to an honest mistake, as in the case of praying without wudu' mistakenly.
The passage ends with: 'ولا تشترط للثواب صحة العبادة' – reward does not require validity.

نہیں کی تو خطبہ نہیں ہوگا بلکہ خطبہ کے لئے خطبہ کی نیت سے کہنا ضروری ہے صاحب فتح القدیر صاحب عنا یہ نے اسی کو رائج قرار دیا ہے۔
(۲) صاحب خانیہ نے خطبہ جمعہ کو عبادة غير مقصودہ قرار دیا ہے اس لئے اگر خطیب نے ممبر پر چڑھنے کے بعد چھینک آنے پر بغیر خطبہ کے ارادے کے الحمد للہ کہا تو وہ خطبہ جمعہ کے قائم مقام ہوگا اسلئے کہ ان کے نزدیک خطبہ جمعہ ظہر کی دورکعتوں کے قائم مقام نہیں ہے اور جب ان کے قائم مقام نہیں ہے تو یہ خطبہ جمعہ عبادہ مقصود ہ بھی نہیں اور عبادہ غیر مقصودہ میں نیت بھی ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ نیت صرف اجر و ثواب کے لئے ہے۔ نیز خانیہ میں ہے کہ اگر چھینک کی وجہ سے الحمد للہ کہتے ہوئے جانور دبج کر دیا تو وہ ذبیح حلال نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ ذکر اللہ ذبح پر ہی شرط ہے اور ذکر اللہ بغیر قصد وارادہ کے متحقق نہیں ہوتا۔
وخطبة العيدين: خطبہ جمعہ اور خطبہ عیدین دونوں کی شرائط برابر ہیں پس جس طرح خطبہ جمعہ میں نیت شرط ہے اسی طرح خطبہ عیدین میں بھی نیت شرط ہے۔ البتہ خطبہ جمعہ و خطبہ عیدین میں چند بنیادی فرق ہے (۱) جواز جمعہ کے لئے خطبہ کا ہوناضروری ہے نماز عیدین کے لئے خطبہ ضروری نہیں (۲) جمعہ میں خطبہ نماز پر مقدم ہوتا ہے جبکہ عیدین میں بعد میں ہوتا ہے البتہ کسی نے اگر مقدم کر دیا تو اس کا اعادہ نہیں ہوگا (۳) خطبہ جمعہ کے دوران کلام کرے میں جو کراہت ہے اس درجہ کی کراہت عیدین کے خطبہ کے درمیان کلام کرنے میں نہیں ہے۔ (فتح القدیر پیروت ج ۲ ص ۷۸) وَأَمَّا الْآذَانُ فَلَا تُشْتَرَطُ لِصِحْتِهِ النِّيَّةُ وَإِنَّمَا هِيَ شَرْطٌ لِلثَّوَابِ عَلَيْهِ.
ترجمہ: اور بہر حال اذ ان تو اس کی صحت کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ اس پر ثواب کے لئے شرط ہے۔ تشريح الاذان في اللغة الاعلام وفي الاصطلاح هو اعلام بوقت الصلوة بالفاظ معلومة ماثورة على صفة مخصوصة (عمدة الايضاح شرح نور الايضاح، ج مراض کرے ۲۷ )
مشہور قول کے مطابق اذان کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے نیت ضروری نہیں ہے اگر موذن نے بدون نیت اذان دیدی تو اذان کی سنت ادا ہو جائیگی البتہ مؤذن کو اس کی اذان کا ثواب نہیں ملے گا۔ (حاشیہ احمدی مع الا شباس (۳۷) وَأَمَّا اِسْتِقْبَالُ الْقِبْلَةِ فَشَرَطَ الجُرْجَانِيُّ لِصِحَتِهِ النِّيَّةُ وَالصَّحِيحُ خِلَافُهُ كَمَا فِي الْمَبْسُوْطِ وَحَمَلَ بَعْضُهُمُ الْأَوَّلَ عَلَى مَا إِذَا كَانَ يُصَلِّي فِي الصِّحْرَاءِ وَالثَّانِي عَلَى مَا إذَا كَانَ يُصَلِّى إِلَى مِحْرَابِ كَذَا فِي الْبِنَايَةِ.
ترجمہ: اور بہر حال استقبال قبلہ تو اس کی صحت کے لئے امام جرجانی نے نیت کو شرط قرار دیا ہے اور تا اس کے برخلاف ہے جیسا کہ مبسوط میں ہے اور بعض نے اول کو اس صورت پر محمول کیا ہے جب وہ صحراء میں نماز پڑھ رہا ہو اور دوسری صورت کو اس پر محمول کیا ہے جب وہ محراب کی طرف نماز پڑھ رہا ہو، بنا یہ میں ایساہی ہے۔

تشریح : استقبال قبلہ کے لئے نیت شرط ہے یا نہیں در اصل یہ مسئلہ ایک دوسرے مسئلہ پر موقوف ہے کہ مین کعبہ کو سامنے کرنا صحت صلاۃ کے لئے شرط ہے یا نہیں ۔ جمہور علماء کے نزدیک کی مشاہد کے لئے عین قبلہ کی طرف رخ کرنا ضروری ہے اور مکی غیر مشاہد کے لئے جت قبلہ سمت قبلہ ہی کافی ہے میں قبلہ کی طرف رخ کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
عبدالله جرجانی کے نزدیک عین قبلہ کا رخ کرنا ہر ایک کے لئے ضروری ہے مشاہد ہو یا غیر مشاہد یعنی قریب ہو یا بعید چونکہ بعید کو اس کا مکلف بنانے میں پریشانی ہے اس لئے انہوں نے نیت کو ضروری قرار دیکر عین قبلہ کا درجہ دیدیا پھر اس کے بعد دو قول ہو گئے ۔
(1) شیخ ابو بکرمحمد بن الفضل کے نزدیک کعبہ کا رخ کرنے کے بعد بھی نیت کعبہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ (۲) شیخ محمد بن حامد کے نزدیک شرط نہیں ہے اور جمہور کا مسلک بھی یہی ہے جیسا کہ صاحب ہدایہ تجنیس کے حوالہ سے نقل کرتے ہیں کہ صحیح قول کے مطابق نیت کعبہ مطلقا شرط نہیں ہے۔
بعض حضرات نے اول صورت کو اس پر محمول کیا ہے کہ جب جنگل وغیرہ میں نماز پڑھے اور دوسری صورت کو اس پر محمول کیا ہے جب محراب کی طرف یعنی آبادی میں نماز پڑھے۔ بہر حال فتقومی اس پر ہے کہ نیت نہ استقبال کے لئے شرط صحت ہے اور نہ استقبال کے بعد تعیین کعبہ کے لئے خواہ محراب میں نماز پڑھی جائے یا جنگل میں قبلہ متعارف ہو و متعین ہو یا غیر متعارف و غیر متعین ہو۔ وَأَمَّاسَتْرُ الْعَوْرَةِ فَلَا تُشْتَرَطُ لِصِحْتِهِ النِّيَّةُ وَلَمْ أرَفِيْهِ خِلَافًا وَلَا تُشْتَرَطُ لِلتَّوَابِ صِحَّةُ الْعِبَادَةِ بَلْ يُقَابُ عَلَى نِيَّتِهِ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ فَاسِدَةً بِغَيْرِ تَعَمُّدِهِ كَمَا لَوْصَلَّى مُحْدِثًا عَلَى ظَنِّ طَهَارَتِهِ وَسَيَاتِي تَحْقِیقه
ترجمہ: اور بہر حال ستر عورت تو اس کی صحت کے لئے نیت شرم نہیں اور میں نے اس میں کسی کا اختلاف نہیں دیکھا اور ثواب کے لئے عبادت کا صحیح ہونا شرط نہیں بلکہ اسے اس کی نیت پر تو اب دیا جائے گا اگر چہ وہ فاسد ہی ہو بغیر اس کے کہ اس کی طرف سے عمد ا ہو جیسا کہ کوئی محدث ہونے کی حالت میں اس گمان کے ساتھ نماز پڑھ لے کہ وہ ظاہر ہے اور اس کی تحقیق عنقریب آئے گی۔
تشریح: ستر عورت کے لئے کسی کپڑے کا استعمال کرے تو اسے استعمال کرتے وقت ستر عورت کی نیت نہ کرے تو بھی ستر عورت کا فریضہ ہو جائیگا اس کے لئے نبیت کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے، علامہ ابن نجیم مصری فرماتے ہیں اس مسئلہ میں کسی کا اختلاف میری نظر سے نہیں گذرا۔ ولا تشترط للنواب صحة العبادة : اخروی ثواب کے لئے عبادت کا صحیح ہونا شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ ثواب کا مدار فعل کے مقابلہ میں نیت پر زیادہ ہے اگر کسی آدمی نے عبادت شروع کی عبادت کی نیت سے تو اخروی ثواب اس
If he did not intend, the khutbah will not be valid; rather, for the khutbah, it is necessary to say it with the intention of khutbah. The authors of Fath al-Qadir and al-`Inayah have adopted this as the prevailing view.
(2) The author of al-Khaniyyah considered the Friday khutbah as an unintended act of worship (ibadah ghayr maqsudah). Therefore, if the khatib, after ascending the pulpit, sneezes and says "al-hamdu lillah" without intending the khutbah, it will suffice as the Friday khutbah, because according to him, the Friday khutbah is not a substitute for the two rak`ahs of Zuhr, and since it is not a substitute, the Friday khutbah is not an intended act of worship either. In an unintended act of worship, intention is not necessary; rather, intention is only for reward and merit. Also in al-Khaniyyah: if, due to a sneeze, while saying "al-hamdu lillah," he slaughters an animal, that slaughter will not be halal, because the mention of Allah is a condition for slaughter, and the mention of Allah is not realized without intent and will.
And the khutbah of the two Eids: The conditions of the Friday khutbah and the khutbah of the two Eids are equal. Just as intention is a condition in the Friday khutbah, so intention is a condition in the khutbah of the two Eids. However, there are several essential differences between the Friday khutbah and the khutbah of the two Eids: (1) For the validity of Friday, the khutbah is necessary; for the Eid prayer, the khutbah is not necessary. (2) In Friday, the khutbah precedes the prayer, while in the Eids, it comes after; however, if someone precedes it, it does not need to be repeated. (3) The degree of dislike (karahah) that exists in speaking during the Friday khutbah is not present in speaking during the khutbah of the Eids. (Fath al-Qadir, Beirut, vol. 2, p. 78) And as for the adhan, intention is not required for its validity; rather, it is a condition for reward upon it.
Translation: And as for the adhan, intention is not required for its validity; rather, it is a condition for reward upon it. Explanation of adhan: Linguistically, it means announcement; terminologically, it is an announcement of the time of prayer with known, transmitted words in a specific manner. (`Umdat al-Idah Sharh Nur al-Idah, vol.????? p. 27)
According to the well-known view, intention is not required for the validity of the adhan. If the mu'adhdhin gives the adhan without intention, the sunnah of adhan is fulfilled, but the mu'adhdhin will not receive the reward for his adhan. (Hashiyah Ahmadi with al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, p. 37) And as for facing the qiblah, al-Jurjani stipulated intention for its validity, but the correct view is contrary, as in al-Mabsut. Some scholars interpret the first view as when one prays in the open desert, and the second view as when one prays towards a mihrab; it is like this in al-Binayah.
Translation: And as for facing the qiblah, Imam al-Jurjani considered intention a condition for its validity, but the correct view is contrary, as in al-Mabsut. Some scholars interpreted the first [view] as when one is praying in the desert, and the second [view] as when one is praying towards a mihrab; it is like this in al-Binayah.
Explanation: Whether intention is required for facing the qiblah or not; in reality, this issue depends on another issue: whether facing the Ka`bah is a condition for the validity of prayer or not. According to the majority of scholars, for one who sees the Ka`bah (mushahid), turning towards the exact qiblah is necessary; for one who does not see (ghair mushahid), facing the direction of the qiblah is sufficient; turning towards the exact qiblah is not necessary.
According to `Abdullah al-Jurjani, turning towards the exact qiblah is necessary for everyone, whether mushahid or ghair mushahid, i.e., near or far. Since obligating this for the distant person involves difficulty, he made intention necessary and gave it the status of facing the exact qiblah. Then there were two opinions:
(1) According to Shaykh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl, after facing the Ka`bah, intending the Ka`bah is also a condition.
(2) According to Shaykh Muhammad ibn Hamid, it is not a condition, and this is the position of the majority, as the author of al-Hidayah narrates from al-Tajnis that according to the correct view, intending the Ka`bah is absolutely not a condition.
Some scholars interpreted the first view as when one prays in the jungle etc., and the second view as when one prays towards the mihrab, i.e., in a populated area. In any case, the fatwa is that intention is neither a condition for the validity of facing the qiblah nor for specifying the Ka`bah after facing it, whether prayer is offered in a mihrab or in the jungle, whether the qiblah is known and determined or unknown and undetermined. And as for covering the `awrah, intention is not required for its validity, and I have not seen any disagreement regarding it. Nor is the validity of the act of worship required for reward; rather, he will be rewarded based on his intention, even if it is invalid without his deliberate fault, as when one prays in a state of impurity while thinking he is pure; its verification will come soon.
Translation: And as for covering the `awrah, intention is not required for its validity, and I have not seen any disagreement regarding it. And for reward, the validity of the worship is not required; rather, he will be rewarded based on his intention, even if it is invalid without his deliberate fault, as when one prays in a state of impurity while thinking he is pure; its verification will come soon.
Explanation: If one uses a cloth to cover the `awrah without intending to cover the `awrah, the obligation of covering the `awrah is still fulfilled; there is no need for intention. `Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says: I have not seen any disagreement in this issue. And the validity of worship is not a condition for reward: For the reward in the Hereafter, the validity of the worship is not a condition; rather, the basis of reward depends more on intention than on the action. If a person begins an act of worship with the intention of worship, he will receive the reward in the Hereafter.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the legal maxim regarding intention (niyyah) in acts of worship. It discusses four specific acts—khutbah, adhan, facing the qiblah, and covering the `awrah—and examines whether intention is required for their validity or only for reward.

The text begins by presenting a disagreement among Hanafi scholars about the Friday khutbah. Some, like the authors of Fath al-Qadir and al-`Inayah, hold that intention is necessary for the khutbah to be valid. Others, like the author of al-Khaniyyah, consider the Friday khutbah as an unintended act of worship (`ibadah ghayr maqsudah), meaning it is not a substitute for the Zuhr prayer, and thus intention is not required for its validity; intention is only for reward. This is illustrated by an example: if the khatib sneezes and says 'al-hamdu lillah' without intending the khutbah, it suffices. The author then notes the difference in slaughter: if one says 'al-hamdu lillah' due to sneezing while slaughtering, the slaughter is not halal because the remembrance of Allah (dhikr) must be intended.

Next, the khutbah of the two Eids is discussed. The conditions are similar to Friday, but there are key differences: (1) Khutbah is essential for Friday but not for Eid prayer; (2) In Friday, khutbah precedes prayer, while in Eid, it follows; (3) Speaking during Friday khutbah is more disliked than during Eid khutbah.

The passage then moves to the adhan (call to prayer). The established ruling is that intention is not a condition for the validity of adhan; it is only a condition for reward. The mu'adhdhin fulfills the sunnah even without intention, but does not earn the reward.

For facing the qiblah (istiqbal al-qiblah), there is a known difference. Imam al-Jurjani required intention for its validity, but the correct view in the Hanafi madhhab is that intention is not required. Some scholars reconciled these views by distinguishing between praying in the open desert (where intention might be needed to face the exact qiblah) and praying towards a mihrab (where the direction is clear). Ultimately, the relied-upon position (fatwa) is that intention is required neither for facing the qiblah nor for specifying the Ka'bah after facing it, regardless of circumstances.

Finally, covering the `awrah (satr al-`awrah) is addressed. There is no disagreement: intention is not required for its validity. The act is valid even without intention. The text then concludes with a general principle: reward (thawab) does not require the act to be valid; rather, reward is given based on intention, even if the act is invalid due to an honest mistake (e.g., praying without wudu' while believing one is pure).

Throughout, the commentary emphasizes that intention is primarily about reward, while validity often does not require it, except where explicitly stipulated.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; the conscious purpose or aim in performing an act of worship.
صحة (sihhah): Validity; the act's compliance with legal requirements such that it fulfills the obligation or sunnah.
ثواب (thawab): Reward; recompense from Allah for an act done with the right intention.
عبادة غير مقصودہ (ibadah ghayr maqsudah): An act of worship that is not intended for its own sake but as a means to something else (e.g., khutbah as a condition for Friday prayer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is required for the adhan to be valid?
A) Intention is required for both validity and reward.
B) Intention is required for validity but not for reward.
C) Intention is required for reward but not for validity.
D) Intention is not required at all.

Key Takeaway
Intention (niyyah) is primarily about reward; many acts of worship are valid without it, except where the Law explicitly requires it.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Intention Required for Zakat Payment
Ruling on intention for zakat with critical refinement of a minority view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that zakat requires the owner's intention and evaluate the validity of forced collection in light of the Hanafi mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Zakat is an act of worship; without the owner's intention, even the imam's forced collection does not fulfill it.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair establishes a critical principle: zakat, like other acts of worship, requires intention (niyyah). It then refines a contrary view attributed to al-Qadi al-Isbijabi, declaring it weak, and confirms the mu‘tamad (relied-upon) position that forcible taking by the imam does not count as valid zakat. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct fatwa application, especially when dealing with recalcitrant payers.

Guided Path
1
State the base principle
Identify the foundational rule: 'Zakat payment is not valid except with intention.' This is the axiom from which the rest follows.
Intention here means the owner's deliberate intent to fulfill the zakat obligation.
2
Identify the challenging opinion
Recognize the view of al-Qadi al-Isbijabi: if a person refuses to pay, the imam may forcibly take the zakat and distribute it, and this suffices because the imam has authority to take it.
This opinion relies on the imam's wilāyah (authority) as a substitute for the owner's consent.
3
Analyze the refinement
Understand why the author declares this view 'weak' and presents the mu‘tamad: the imam's taking cannot replace the owner's intention, which is a necessary condition for the validity of zakat.
The authority of the imam extends to enforcement, but not to the personal act of worship.
4
Apply the refined rule to practical scenarios
Conclude that if the imam forcibly takes money from a refuser, that payment does not discharge the zakat obligation. The collector should instead apply pressure (e.g., imprisonment) to induce voluntary payment with intention.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical consequence of the dispute.
5
Connect to broader legal maxim
Link this ruling to the qawida: 'Al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions). Intention is central to acts of worship, and actions without it are invalid.
This maxim governs many ibādāt, not just zakat.

وَأَمَّا الزَّكوة فَلَا يَصِحُ أَدَاءُ هَا إِلَّا بِالنِّيَّةِ وَعَلَى هَذَا فَمَا ذَكَرَ الْقَاضِي الإِسْبِيْجَابِي أَنَّ مَنِ امْتَنَعَ عَنْ أَدَائِهَا أَخَذَهَا الْإِمَامُ كَرْهَا وَوَضَعَهَا فِي أَهْلِهَا وَتَجْزِيْهِ لِإِنَّ لِلْإِمَامِ وَلَا يَةَ أَخْذِهَا فَقَامَ أَخْذُهُ مَقَامَ دَفْعِ الْمَالِكِ بِاخْتِيَارِهِ ضَعِيفٌ وَالْمُعْتَمَدُ فِي الْمَذْهَبِ عَدَمُ الْاجْزَاءِ كَرْهاً قَالَ فِي الْمُحِيْطِ وَمَنِ امْتَنَعَ عَنْ أَدَاءِ الزَّكوةِ فَالسَّاعِيْ لَا يَأْخُذُ عَنْهُ الزَّكَوةَ كَرْهاً وَلَوْ أَخَذَ لَا يَقَعُ عَنِ الزَّكونَةِ لِكَوْنِهَا بِلَا اخْتِيَارِ وَلَكِنْ يُجْرُهُ بِالْخَيْسِ ليُؤدى بنفسه انتهى. ترجمه: اور بہر حال زکوۃ بدون نیت اس کی ادائیگی صحیح نہیں ہے اور اسی بنیاد پر جو قاضی اسیجائی نے ذکر کیا کہ جو اس کی ادائیگی سے رک گیا تو امام اس کوز بر دستی لیکر مصرف میں دیدے اور اس کے لئے کافی ہے اس لئے کہ امام کو اس کو لینے کی ولایت حاصل ہے اس کا لینا مالک کے اپنے اختیار سے دینے کے قائم مقام ہو جائے گا یہ ضعیف ؟ اور مذہب میں قابل اعتماد جبراً کافی نہ ہونا ہے محیط میں کہا جو ز کوۃ کی ادائیگی سے رک گیا تو عامل اس سے زبردستی کوڈ نہ لے اور اگر ل لی تو زکوۃ کی طرف سے واقع نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہ بلا اختیار ہے لیکن وہ اس کو قید کر کے مجبور کر یگا تا کہ خود بخو دادا کر دے، محیط کا کلام پورا ہوا۔ تشريح: الزكوة لغةً النمو وفی الشريعة تملیک مال مخصوص لشخص مخصوص (عمدة الايضاح شرح نور الايضاح ج ۲ ص ۳۷۳)
And as for zakat, its payment is not valid except with intention. Based on this, what al-Qadi al-Isbijabi mentioned that if someone refrains from paying it, the imam should take it by force and distribute it to its recipients, and it will suffice for him because the imam has authority to take it, so his taking stands in place of the owner's voluntary payment—this is weak. The relied-upon position in the madhhab is that it is not sufficient if taken by force. In al-Muhit, it is stated: If someone refrains from paying zakat, the collector should not take zakat from him by force. Even if he takes it, it will not count as zakat because it is without the owner's choice. Rather, he should imprison him to force him to pay it himself. End of al-Muhit. Translation: And in any case, zakat is not valid without intention. On this basis, what al-Qadi al-Isbijabi mentioned that if someone refuses to pay, the imam should take it by force and distribute it to the deserving, and it will suffice for him because the imam has authority to take it, so his taking is equivalent to the owner's voluntary payment—this is weak. The reliable view in the madhhab is that it is not sufficient if taken by force. In al-Muhit, it is said: If someone refrains from paying zakat, the collector should not take zakat from him by force. If he takes it, it will not count as zakat because it is without his choice. Rather, he should imprison him to force him to pay himself. End of al-Muhit. Explanation: Zakat linguistically means growth; in Shariah, it is the transfer of specific wealth to a specific person.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage establishes a critical rule for zakat: intention is essential for its validity. The text then critiques a contrary view of al-Qadi al-Isbijabi, who argued that if a person refuses to pay zakat, the imam may forcibly take it and that suffices. This opinion is declared weak (da‘if). The relied-upon (mu‘tamad) position, as recorded in al-Muhit, is that forced collection does not discharge the zakat obligation because it lacks the owner's consent and intention. Instead, the collector should apply pressure, such as imprisonment, to compel the person to pay voluntarily. The passage ends with a concise technical definition of zakat: linguistically 'growth' and legally 'transfer of specified wealth to a specified person'. This ruling underscores that zakat is an act of worship contingent on volition and sincerity, distinguishing it from mere financial obligations.

Key Terms
زكاة (zakāh): Linguistically 'growth'; in Shariah, transfer of specified wealth to a specified person (obligatory charity).
نية (niyyah): Intention; essential for zakat to be valid.
إمام (imām): The Muslim ruler or his appointed representative with authority over zakat collection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mu‘tamad), if the imam forcibly takes zakat from someone who refuses to pay, is the obligation discharged?
A) Yes, because the imam has authority
B) No, because intention is lacking
C) Yes, if the imam distributes it correctly
D) No, unless the owner later agrees

Key Takeaway
Zakat payment is valid only with the owner's intention; forcible collection by the imam does not fulfill the obligation.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
beginner
6 min
The Requirement of Intention in Zakat and Its Conditions
Ruling on the necessity of intention for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that intention is a condition for zakat and apply the condition of contiguity (muqaranah) to determine whether zakat is fulfilled.

Core Idea
Zakat's validity hinges on intention; without it, the obligation remains unfulfilled.

Intention (niyyah) is the heart of worship. In this lesson, we examine how the Hanafi school applies the legal maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to zakat, establishing that intention is not merely recommended but a condition for its validity. We also explore the concept of contiguity (muqaranah) — how the intention must be linked to the act of payment, either actually or legally.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the statement in the text that intention is necessary for zakat, just like prayer.
2
Define contiguity (muqaranah)
Explain the two types: actual contiguity (intention at time of payment) and legal contiguity (intention while wealth still in poor's possession).
Legal contiguity extends the window for intention.
3
Apply to a scenario
Given that someone sets aside zakat money but does not intend until later, determine if it is acceptable per the text.
The text explicitly allows intention after setting aside.

نماز کی طرح زکوۃ بھی عبادۃ مقصودہ ہے اس کی ادائیگی کی صحت کے لئے نیت ہو نا ضروری ہے بدون نیت زکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ ادا نہ ہو گی خواہ وہ نیت زکوۃ دیتے وقت کرے یا مال زکوۃ کو علیحدہ کرتے وقت کرے اس کو مقارنت یہ کہتے ہیں اور خواہ مقارنت حکمیہ ہو جیسے بدون نیت فقیر کو کو دیدی اور مال ابھی فقیر کے قبضہ میں ہے اس وقت بھی اگر نیت کر لی جائے تو کافی ہے بہر حال نیت کا ادائیگی سے اتصال اور مقارن ہونا ضروری ہے خواہ مقارنت قیقیہ ہو یا حکمیہ۔
وعلى هذا فما ذكره القاضی اموال زکوۃ کی دو قسمیں ہیں: (۱) اموال ظاہرہ جیسے گائے بیل مویشی کمیتی و غیر (۲) اموال باطنہ جیسے درا ہم ود تا نیر وغیرہ ۔ اگر کوئی زکوۃ ادا نہ کرے تو اموال ظاہرہ میں حکومت جبر ا ز کوۃ وصول کر سکتی ہے جبکہ اموال باطنہ میں زکوۃ کی ادائیگی کی ذمہ داری حکومت پر نہیں بلکہ خود صاحب مال پر ہے اموال باطنہ میں حکومت جبر کر کے زکوۃ وصول نہیں کر سکتی جبکہ قاضی اسیجانی فرماتے ہیں کہ اموال ظاہرہ ہو یا اموال باطنہ ہر ایک کے سلسلے میں حکومت جبر کر کے زکوۃ وصول کر سکتی ہے اور حکومت کا جبر از کوۃ وصول کرنا ایسا ہی ہے جیسے مالک نے زکوۃ خود اپنے اختیار سے دی ہو لہذا ما لک کی طرف سے زکوۃ ادا ہو جائیگی اگر چہ حکومت نے جبر از کوۃ وصول کی ہو۔ علامہ ابن نجیم المصری علیہ الرحمہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اموال ظاہرہ میں جبرا حکومت کا زکوۃ وصول کرتا اور مالک کی طرف سے زکوۃ کا ادا ہونا جمہور علماء کے نزدیک بھی سیج اور درست ہے جبکہ اموال باطنہ میں جبر از کوۃ وصول کر کے حکومت کا اس کے مصرف میں خرچ کر دیتا اور مالک کی طرف سے زکوۃ کا ادا ہونا یہ قول ضعیف ہے کیونکہ اموال ظاہرہ کے زکوۃ کی وصولی کی ذمہ داری حکومت کی ہے لیکن اموال باطنہ کی زکوۃ کی وصولی کی ذمہ داری حکومت کی نہیں ہے بلکہ خود صاحب مال کی ہے اس لئے اگر حکومت نے جبراً اموال باطنہ کی زکوۃ وصول کی تو مالک کی طرف سے زکوۃ عدم نیت کی وجہ سے ادا نہ ہوگی۔ وفي رد المختار ان الساعى لو اخذها منه كرها لا يسقط الفرض عنه في الاموال الباطنة بخلاف الظاهرة هو المفتی به (شامی زکریا ج ۳ ص (۱۸۷) قال في المحيط اگر صاحب زکوۃ اموال باطنہ کی زکوۃ ادانہ کرے تو ارباب حکومت زبر دستی اس سے زکوۃ اصول نہیں کریں گے اگر ز بر دستی اموال باطنہ میں زکوۃ ارباب حکومت نے وصول کر لی تو اختیار نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے صاحب مال کی زکوۃ ادا نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اموال باطنہ کی زکوۃ کی ادائیگی کی ذمہ داری خود صاحب مال پر ہے اور نیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے زکوۃ ادانہ ہوگی بخلاف اموال ظاہرہ کے کہ ان کی وصولی کی ذمہ داری ارباب حکومت پر ہے اس لئے اگر بدون نیت مالک کی اجازت کے بغیر زکوۃ وصول کر کے اس کے مصرف میں دیدی تو زکوۃ ادا ہو جائینگی۔ لیکن اموال باطنہ کی زکوۃ ادا نہ کرنے کی صورت میں ارباب حکومت صاحب مال کو قید کر لیں گے تا کہ وہ خود ہی زکوۃ اموال باطنہ کی ادائیگی پر مجبور ہو جائے اور اس کے قصد و اختیار کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اس کی زکوۃ بھی ادا ہو جائے ۔
زکوۃ کے واجب ہو جانے کے بعد زکوۃ کی ادائیگی علی التراخی واجب ہے یا علی الفور علامہ حموی نے ظہیر یہ کے حوالہ سے نقل کیا ہے کہ ہمارے اصحاب میں سے ابن شجاع علیہ الرحمہ کی روایت کے بموجب زکوۃ علی التراخی واجب ہے جب بھی ادا کرے گا تو ادا ہی کہلائے گی۔ امام محمد کی روایت یہ ہے کہ وجوب زکوۃ کے بعد اس کی ادائیگی علی الفور واجب ہے اگر حولان حول کے بعد زکو ادا نہ کی تو وہ گنہگار ہوگا اور اس کی شہادت قابل قبول نہ ہوگی اور جب امام کو اس کے بارے میں معلوم ہو کہ اس نے زکوۃ ادا نہیں کی ہے تو تعزیر کرے اس کو قید کرے اور زکوۃ کی ادائیگی کا مطالبہ کرے۔
علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ تعزیر قید کرنا اموال ظاہرہ کی زکوۃ ادا نہ کرنے کی صورت میں ہے اموال باطنہ میں نہیں ہے کیونکہ اموال باطنہ میں زکوۃ کی ادائیگی فقراء وغیرہ کو یہ خود صاحب مال کی ذمہ داری ہے امام کو اموال باطنہ کے سلسلہ میں مطالبہ کا حق نہیں ہے۔ وَخَرَجَ عَنْ اشْتِرَاطِهَا لَهَامَا إِذَا تَصَدَّقَ بِجَمِيعِ النصابِ بِلَانِيَّةٍ فَإِنَّ الْفَرْضَ يَسْقُطُ عَنْهُ وَاخْتَلَفُوا فِي سُقُوْطِ زَكَوةِ الْبَعْضِ إِذَا تَصَدَّقَ بِهِ.
ترجمه: اور نیت کے شرط ہونے سے وہ صورت خارج ہو گئی جب پور انصاب بدون نیت صدقہ کر دیا کیونکہ فرض اس سے ساقط ہو جائے گا اور بعض کی زکوۃ کے ساقط ہونے کے سلسلہ میں فقہاء نے اختلاف کیا ہے جبکہ وہ اس کو صدقہ کر دے۔
تشریح: جس شخص پر زکوۃ واجب تھی اس نے جملہ مال صدقہ کر دیا بدون نیت زکوۃ تو زکوۃ اس سے ساقط" جائے گی کیونکہ مال کے جس حصہ کی زکوۃ کی ادائیگی ضروری تھی وہ اس کا ایک جز تھا اور رمانسیت کا مسئلہ تو وہ مزاحمت کو دور کرنے کے لئے تھی جب اس نے کل مال ہی صدقہ کر لیا تو مزاحمت باقی نہ رہی اور عدم مزاحمت کی وجہ سے نیت کا ضرورت باقی نہیں رہی ہاں نفس عبادت یعنی صدقہ کی نیت موجود ہے جو نیت فرض کے لئے کافی ہے۔ واختلفوا : اگر کسی نے بعض نصاب صدقہ کیا تو کیا اس صورت میں بھی زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی اما محمد کے نزد کہانی زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی انہوں نے جزء کو کل کے درجہ میں اتارا ہے۔
امام یوسف کے نزدیک زکوۃ ساقط نہ ہو گی کیونکہ واجب متعین نہیں ہے لہذا جو حصہ صدقہ میں گیا ہے تو وہ جو مال کا وہ حصہ نہیں ہے جس کی بطور ز کوۃ ادا ئیگی واجب ہے۔
Just like prayer, zakat is also a worship intended for its own sake. For the validity of its payment, intention is necessary. Without intention, giving zakat will not fulfill the obligation, whether one makes the intention at the time of giving zakat or at the time of setting aside the zakat wealth — this is called contiguity (muqaranah). And even if the contiguity is legal (hukmiyyah), such as giving to the poor without intention while the wealth is still in the poor's possession, then if intention is made at that time, it suffices. In any case, the connection and contiguity of intention to payment is necessary, whether actual or legal. Upon this basis, what the Qadi mentioned: Zakat wealth is of two types: (1) Apparent wealth like cattle, livestock, measured items, etc.; (2) Hidden wealth like dirhams and dinars, etc. If someone does not pay zakat, for apparent wealth the government can collect zakat forcibly, whereas for hidden wealth, the responsibility of paying zakat is not on the government but on the owner himself. The government cannot forcibly collect zakat for hidden wealth. However, Qadi Isfijani says that whether apparent or hidden, the government can forcibly collect zakat for both, and the government's forcible collection is just as if the owner gave zakat voluntarily, so the zakat will be fulfilled on behalf of the owner even if the government collected it forcibly. Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says that for apparent wealth, the government's forcible collection and the zakat being fulfilled on behalf of the owner is correct according to the majority of scholars, whereas for hidden wealth, the government forcibly collects and spends it in its prescribed channels, but [the claim that] the zakat is fulfilled on behalf of the owner is a weak view, because the responsibility of collecting zakat for apparent wealth lies with the government, but for hidden wealth, the responsibility of collection does not lie with the government; rather it lies with the owner. Therefore, if the government forcibly collects zakat on hidden wealth, the zakat will not be fulfilled on behalf of the owner due to lack of intention. In Radd al-Mukhtar: 'If the collector takes it from him by force, the obligation does not drop from him regarding hidden wealth, unlike apparent wealth; this is the fatwa.' (Shamiyya, Zakariyya vol. 3 p. 187) It is said in al-Muhit: If the owner of hidden wealth does not pay zakat, the authorities will not forcibly take zakat from him. If they forcibly collect zakat on hidden wealth, then due to lack of choice, the zakat will not be fulfilled for the owner, because the responsibility of paying zakat on hidden wealth is on the owner himself, and due to lack of intention, zakat will not be fulfilled. Unlike apparent wealth, where the responsibility of collection is on the authorities; therefore, if without intention and without the owner's permission, they collect zakat and spend it in its prescribed channels, the zakat is fulfilled. But if zakat on hidden wealth is not paid, the authorities will imprison the owner so that he himself is compelled to pay the zakat on hidden wealth, and due to the presence of his intent and choice, his zakat will be fulfilled. After zakat becomes obligatory, is its payment obligatory at leisure (on delay) or immediately? Allamah al-Hamawi narrated from al-Zahiriyyah that according to a report from Ibn Shuja', zakat is obligatory on delay, and whenever he pays, it counts as payment. According to a report from Imam Muhammad, after obligation, paying zakat immediately is obligatory; if he does not pay after the year's passage, he becomes sinful, his testimony is unacceptable, and when the ruler knows that he has not paid, he should administer ta'zir, imprison him, and demand payment. Allamah al-Hamawi says that this ta'zir and imprisonment is for the case of not paying zakat on apparent wealth, not for hidden wealth, because for hidden wealth, paying zakat to the poor etc. is the owner's own responsibility; the ruler has no right to demand it. 'And there is an exception from its condition [of intention] for the case when one gives all the nisab as charity without intention, for the obligation drops from him, and they differed regarding the dropping of zakat for part if he gives it as charity.' Translation: And the case when he gives the entire nisab in charity without intention is excluded from the condition of intention, because the obligation drops from him. And the scholars differed regarding the dropping of zakat on part when he gives it as charity. Explanation: A person on whom zakat was obligatory gave all his wealth in charity without intention of zakat, then zakat drops from him, because the portion for which zakat payment was necessary was a part of it, and the issue of intention was for removing impediment. When he gave all the wealth in charity, no impediment remains, and due to the absence of impediment, the need for intention does not remain. Rather, the intention of the worship itself, i.e., charity, exists, which suffices as intention for the obligation. 'And they differed': If someone gave part of the nisab in charity, does zakat drop in this case too? According to Imam Muhammad, zakat drops; he treated the part as equivalent to the whole. According to Imam Yusuf, zakat does not drop, because the obligation is not specified; therefore the portion given in charity is not the same portion whose payment as zakat was obligatory.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is an application of the legal maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions) specifically to the obligation of zakat in Hanafi fiqh. It first establishes the general rule: intention (niyyah) is necessary for the validity of zakat, just as for prayer. The intention must be connected to the act of payment, either actually or legally. The passage then discusses the distinction between apparent and hidden wealth regarding the government's role in forcible collection. The relied-upon Hanafi position (as per Radd al-Mukhtar) is that for apparent wealth like livestock and crops, the state can collect forcibly even without the owner's intention, and the obligation is discharged because the state acts as the agent of collection. For hidden wealth like cash, the state cannot collect forcibly; if it does, the obligation is not discharged due to lack of intention. Instead, the state may detain the owner to compel voluntary payment. The passage then addresses the timing of zakat payment: the preferred view (Ibn Shuja') is that it is due on delay (tarakhi), but Imam Muhammad held it is immediate (fawr), with consequences for sin and testimony. Finally, an exception to the intention requirement is presented: if a person gives all the nisab as voluntary charity without intending zakat, the zakat obligation drops because the wealth is exhausted and no impediment remains. However, if only part of the nisab is given, the Hanafi school is split: Imam Muhammad says the obligation drops (treating the part as the whole), while Imam Yusuf says it does not because the zakat obligation is not attached to a specific portion.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention required for the validity of zakat; must be connected to the act of payment
مقارنت (muqaranah): Contiguity; the connection of intention to the act of payment, either actual or legal

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about the requirement of intention (niyyah) for zakat?
A) Intention is not required; only the act of giving matters.
B) Intention is required and must be present exactly at the moment of payment.
C) Intention is required and can be made at the time of setting aside the zakat wealth or at the time of payment, and even after payment if the wealth is still in the recipient's possession.
D) Intention is required only if the zakat is given to a specific category of recipients.

Key Takeaway
Intention is a condition for zakat, and Hanafi fiqh allows flexibility in its timing through actual or legal contiguity.

Government Collection of Zakat: Apparent vs Hidden Wealth
Distinction between apparent and hidden wealth in zakat collection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between apparent and hidden wealth regarding government forcible collection of zakat and apply the Hanafi rule that intention is dropped for apparent wealth when the state collects.

Core Idea
For apparent wealth, state collection discharges the obligation even without owner's intention; for hidden wealth, it does not.

This lesson explores a crucial distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the difference between apparent wealth (amwal zahirah) and hidden wealth (amwal batinah) in relation to zakat. The passage explains that the government can forcibly collect zakat on apparent wealth, and this fulfills the obligation even without the owner's intention. However, for hidden wealth, forcible collection does not discharge the obligation, and the owner must pay with intention. This distinction is derived from the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' but modified by the role of the state as agent.

Guided Path
1
Define the two types of wealth
Identify apparent wealth (livestock, crops) and hidden wealth (cash, gold) as defined in the passage.
These categories determine state involvement.
2
State the ruling for each type
For apparent wealth, state can collect forcibly and obligation drops even without owner's intention. For hidden wealth, state cannot collect forcibly; if it does, obligation remains.
Exception: Some scholars like Qadi Isfijani hold that state can collect both, but the mufta bihi is the majority view.
3
Analyze the basis
Why does intention matter? For hidden wealth, the owner is responsible; for apparent, the state acts as agent.
The maxim applies: the state's intention serves as the owner's intention for apparent wealth.

علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ تعزیر قید کرنا اموال ظاہرہ کی زکوۃ ادا نہ کرنے کی صورت میں ہے اموال باطنہ میں نہیں ہے کیونکہ اموال باطنہ میں زکوۃ کی ادائیگی فقراء وغیرہ کو یہ خود صاحب مال کی ذمہ داری ہے امام کو اموال باطنہ کے سلسلہ میں مطالبہ کا حق نہیں ہے۔ وَخَرَجَ عَنْ اشْتِرَاطِهَا لَهَامَا إِذَا تَصَدَّقَ بِجَمِيعِ النصابِ بِلَانِيَّةٍ فَإِنَّ الْفَرْضَ يَسْقُطُ عَنْهُ وَاخْتَلَفُوا فِي سُقُوْطِ زَكَوةِ الْبَعْضِ إِذَا تَصَدَّقَ بِهِ.
ترجمه: اور نیت کے شرط ہونے سے وہ صورت خارج ہو گئی جب پور انصاب بدون نیت صدقہ کر دیا کیونکہ فرض اس سے ساقط ہو جائے گا اور بعض کی زکوۃ کے ساقط ہونے کے سلسلہ میں فقہاء نے اختلاف کیا ہے جبکہ وہ اس کو صدقہ کر دے۔
تشریح: جس شخص پر زکوۃ واجب تھی اس نے جملہ مال صدقہ کر دیا بدون نیت زکوۃ تو زکوۃ اس سے ساقط" جائے گی کیونکہ مال کے جس حصہ کی زکوۃ کی ادائیگی ضروری تھی وہ اس کا ایک جز تھا اور رمانسیت کا مسئلہ تو وہ مزاحمت کو دور کرنے کے لئے تھی جب اس نے کل مال ہی صدقہ کر لیا تو مزاحمت باقی نہ رہی اور عدم مزاحمت کی وجہ سے نیت کا ضرورت باقی نہیں رہی ہاں نفس عبادت یعنی صدقہ کی نیت موجود ہے جو نیت فرض کے لئے کافی ہے۔ واختلفوا : اگر کسی نے بعض نصاب صدقہ کیا تو کیا اس صورت میں بھی زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی اما محمد کے نزد کہانی زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی انہوں نے جزء کو کل کے درجہ میں اتارا ہے۔
امام یوسف کے نزدیک زکوۃ ساقط نہ ہو گی کیونکہ واجب متعین نہیں ہے لہذا جو حصہ صدقہ میں گیا ہے تو وہ جو مال کا وہ حصہ نہیں ہے جس کی بطور ز کوۃ ادا ئیگی واجب ہے۔
Just like prayer, zakat is also a worship intended for its own sake. For the validity of its payment, intention is necessary. Without intention, giving zakat will not fulfill the obligation, whether one makes the intention at the time of giving zakat or at the time of setting aside the zakat wealth — this is called contiguity (muqaranah). And even if the contiguity is legal (hukmiyyah), such as giving to the poor without intention while the wealth is still in the poor's possession, then if intention is made at that time, it suffices. In any case, the connection and contiguity of intention to payment is necessary, whether actual or legal. Upon this basis, what the Qadi mentioned: Zakat wealth is of two types: (1) Apparent wealth like cattle, livestock, measured items, etc.; (2) Hidden wealth like dirhams and dinars, etc. If someone does not pay zakat, for apparent wealth the government can collect zakat forcibly, whereas for hidden wealth, the responsibility of paying zakat is not on the government but on the owner himself. The government cannot forcibly collect zakat for hidden wealth. However, Qadi Isfijani says that whether apparent or hidden, the government can forcibly collect zakat for both, and the government's forcible collection is just as if the owner gave zakat voluntarily, so the zakat will be fulfilled on behalf of the owner even if the government collected it forcibly. Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says that for apparent wealth, the government's forcible collection and the zakat being fulfilled on behalf of the owner is correct according to the majority of scholars, whereas for hidden wealth, the government forcibly collects and spends it in its prescribed channels, but [the claim that] the zakat is fulfilled on behalf of the owner is a weak view, because the responsibility of collecting zakat for apparent wealth lies with the government, but for hidden wealth, the responsibility of collection does not lie with the government; rather it lies with the owner. Therefore, if the government forcibly collects zakat on hidden wealth, the zakat will not be fulfilled on behalf of the owner due to lack of intention. In Radd al-Mukhtar: 'If the collector takes it from him by force, the obligation does not drop from him regarding hidden wealth, unlike apparent wealth; this is the fatwa.' (Shamiyya, Zakariyya vol. 3 p. 187) It is said in al-Muhit: If the owner of hidden wealth does not pay zakat, the authorities will not forcibly take zakat from him. If they forcibly collect zakat on hidden wealth, then due to lack of choice, the zakat will not be fulfilled for the owner, because the responsibility of paying zakat on hidden wealth is on the owner himself, and due to lack of intention, zakat will not be fulfilled. Unlike apparent wealth, where the responsibility of collection is on the authorities; therefore, if without intention and without the owner's permission, they collect zakat and spend it in its prescribed channels, the zakat is fulfilled. But if zakat on hidden wealth is not paid, the authorities will imprison the owner so that he himself is compelled to pay the zakat on hidden wealth, and due to the presence of his intent and choice, his zakat will be fulfilled. After zakat becomes obligatory, is its payment obligatory at leisure (on delay) or immediately? Allamah al-Hamawi narrated from al-Zahiriyyah that according to a report from Ibn Shuja', zakat is obligatory on delay, and whenever he pays, it counts as payment. According to a report from Imam Muhammad, after obligation, paying zakat immediately is obligatory; if he does not pay after the year's passage, he becomes sinful, his testimony is unacceptable, and when the ruler knows that he has not paid, he should administer ta'zir, imprison him, and demand payment. Allamah al-Hamawi says that this ta'zir and imprisonment is for the case of not paying zakat on apparent wealth, not for hidden wealth, because for hidden wealth, paying zakat to the poor etc. is the owner's own responsibility; the ruler has no right to demand it. 'And there is an exception from its condition [of intention] for the case when one gives all the nisab as charity without intention, for the obligation drops from him, and they differed regarding the dropping of zakat for part if he gives it as charity.' Translation: And the case when he gives the entire nisab in charity without intention is excluded from the condition of intention, because the obligation drops from him. And the scholars differed regarding the dropping of zakat on part when he gives it as charity. Explanation: A person on whom zakat was obligatory gave all his wealth in charity without intention of zakat, then zakat drops from him, because the portion for which zakat payment was necessary was a part of it, and the issue of intention was for removing impediment. When he gave all the wealth in charity, no impediment remains, and due to the absence of impediment, the need for intention does not remain. Rather, the intention of the worship itself, i.e., charity, exists, which suffices as intention for the obligation. 'And they differed': If someone gave part of the nisab in charity, does zakat drop in this case too? According to Imam Muhammad, zakat drops; he treated the part as equivalent to the whole. According to Imam Yusuf, zakat does not drop, because the obligation is not specified; therefore the portion given in charity is not the same portion whose payment as zakat was obligatory.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is an application of the legal maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions) specifically to the obligation of zakat in Hanafi fiqh. It first establishes the general rule: intention (niyyah) is necessary for the validity of zakat, just as for prayer. The intention must be connected to the act of payment, either actually or legally. The passage then discusses the distinction between apparent and hidden wealth regarding the government's role in forcible collection. The relied-upon Hanafi position (as per Radd al-Mukhtar) is that for apparent wealth like livestock and crops, the state can collect forcibly even without the owner's intention, and the obligation is discharged because the state acts as the agent of collection. For hidden wealth like cash, the state cannot collect forcibly; if it does, the obligation is not discharged due to lack of intention. Instead, the state may detain the owner to compel voluntary payment. The passage then addresses the timing of zakat payment: the preferred view (Ibn Shuja') is that it is due on delay (tarakhi), but Imam Muhammad held it is immediate (fawr), with consequences for sin and testimony. Finally, an exception to the intention requirement is presented: if a person gives all the nisab as voluntary charity without intending zakat, the zakat obligation drops because the wealth is exhausted and no impediment remains. However, if only part of the nisab is given, the Hanafi school is split: Imam Muhammad says the obligation drops (treating the part as the whole), while Imam Yusuf says it does not because the zakat obligation is not attached to a specific portion.

Key Terms
اموال ظاہرہ (amwal zahirah): Apparent wealth such as cattle, livestock, and measured crops; visible and subject to state collection
اموال باطنہ (amwal batinah): Hidden wealth such as cash (dirhams and dinars); not subject to state collection

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does forcible government collection of zakat on hidden wealth not fulfill the owner's obligation?
A) Because hidden wealth is not subject to zakat.
B) Because the government does not have the authority to collect zakat at all.
C) Because the owner's intention is lacking and the state is not the agent for hidden wealth.
D) Because hidden wealth must be given to the poor directly by the owner.

Key Takeaway
The discharge of zakat through state collection depends on the type of wealth: apparent wealth suffices without owner's intention; hidden wealth requires the owner's intention.

Exception to Intention: When All Nisab is Given as Charity and the Internal Hanafi Dispute
Exception to intention requirement when all nisab is given as sadaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exception to the intention requirement when all nisab is given as charity and explain the internal Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Yusuf on giving part of the nisab.

Core Idea
Giving all nisab as sadaqah without zakat intention drops the obligation; but if only part is given, the obligation may or may not drop, depending on the Hanafi imam.

This lesson presents a fascinating exception to the requirement of intention (niyyah) in zakat. If a person gives away all of their zakatable wealth (nisab) as voluntary charity (sadaqah) without specifically intending zakat, the zakat obligation is discharged because the 'impediment' of the obligation is removed. However, if only part of the nisab is given, the Hanafi school splits: Imam Muhammad holds that the part takes the ruling of the whole, so the obligation drops, while Imam Yusuf holds that it does not, because the zakat obligation is not fixed to a specific portion. This ikhtilaf illustrates the principle of legal reasoning (talil) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the exception
Identify the exception: giving all nisab in sadaqah without intention drops the fard.
Reason: no impediment remains; the worship of sadaqah substitutes.
2
Analyze the reasoning
Why does intention become unnecessary? Because the purpose of intention (distinguishing worship) is fulfilled by the act of charity itself.
This is a direct application of the maxim: the act's intention (sadaqah) suffices.
3
Present the internal ikhtilaf
If only part is given, Imam Muhammad says obligation drops (part = whole), Imam Yusuf says it does not (obligation is unspecified).
The relied-upon view is likely Imam Yusuf's (as per later authorities).
4
Determine the thamarah
Practical difference: if someone gives half nisab in sadaqah without intention, under Muhammad's view, no zakat is due on remaining half; under Yusuf's, zakat is still due on entire nisab.
This affects whether the person must still pay zakat.
