The Qawida: The Vowed (Act) is Like Fard – Applications in Nadhr and Qada'
Explaining the maxim 'al-mandhoor ka al-fard' and its applications to vows and make-up.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-mandhoor ka al-fard' to determine the validity and requirements of vows and make-up acts.

Core Idea
A vowed act requires intention like fard, but the vow only holds if the act is not already obligatory.

This lesson explores a key maxim from the Hanafi legal tradition: the vowed act (mandhoor) is like fard in its obligation to fulfill. However, this maxim has specific conditions and exceptions. We will examine when a vow is valid, when it fails, and how intention and specification operate in make-up acts (qada'). The passage also clarifies the Hanafi position on the nature of vow as wajib, not fard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim and Its Literal Meaning
The author states 'wa al-mandhoor ka al-fard'. State clearly that the vowed act is comparable to fard in requiring intention and specification.
This is the central qawida of the lesson.
2
Analyze the Nature of a Vow (Wajib vs Fard)
The passage notes a difference: some say a vow is fard, others say wajib. Ibn Nujaym holds it is wajib. Understand that the Hanafi mufta bihi is wajib, which affects how strictly it is applied.
The distinction impacts whether a missed vow requires a sacrifice (dam) like a missed fard or not.
3
Apply the Condition: The Vowed Act Must Not Be Already Obligatory
If someone vows an act already obligatory (e.g., fard Hajj for one who hasn't performed it), the vow is invalid because the condition is missing. The original obligation remains alone.
This is the key exception to the maxim.
4
Extend the Maxim to Qada' (Make-up Acts)
The passage states that intention is required for qada' just as for ada'. For Ramadan qada', specification of the missed day is a condition, unlike ada' where specification is not required.
This shows how the maxim operates across different chapters of fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمنذور كالفرض : منذور فرض کے مانند ہے جس طرح فرض کی صحت اور تعیین کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے اس طرح نذر کی صحت اور تعیین کے لئے بھی نیت ضروری ہے۔ یہ تشبیہ دراصل اس بات پر مبنی ہے کہ نذر فرض ہے یا واجب ہے۔ بعض وجوب کے قائل ہیں اور بعض فرضیت کے قائل ہیں علامہ ابن نجیم مصری بھی نذر کے وجوب کے قائل ہیں۔ نذر کہتے ہیں کہ بندہ کسی غیر لازم چیز کو اپنے اوپر لازم کر لے حکم اس کا یہ ہے کہ یہ فرض کے قائم مقام ہے اس کو پورا کرنا ضروری ہے بشرطیکہ وہ کسی معصیت کی نذر نہ ہو یا کسی ایسی عبادت کی نذر نہ ہو جو بذاتہ مقصود نہ ہو اور وہ ایسی طاعت پر مشتمل ہو جس کی جنس از قبیل واجبات مقصودہ ہو ۔
ولونذ رحجة الاسلام: اگر کسی شخص نے نذر مانی کہ اگر میرا افلاں کام ہو گیا تو میں حج فرض ادا کروں گا تو اس پر حج فرض ہی فرض ہوگا اس پر نذر کی وجہ سے حج فرض نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ شرائط نذر میں سے یہ بھی ہے کہ منذور واجب نہ ہو چونکہ یہاں منذور پہلے ہی سے واجب ہے اس لئے شرط مفقود ہونے کی وجہ سے نذرتیح نہیں ہوئی جس کی وجہ سے صرف اصل فرض اس پر رہ گیا۔ ی ایسا ہی ہے جیسے کسی نے ایام نحر میں قربانی کی نذر مانی حال یہ ہے کہ اس پر قربانی پہلے سے واجب ہے تو اس کی نذر کی وجہ سے اس پر قربانی واجب نہ ہوگی صرف پہلے سے واجب شدہ قربانی واجب ہوگی۔ والقضاء فی الکل : جس طرح ادا کی صحت اور تعیین کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے ہی طرح قضا کی صحت و تعین کے لیئے بھی نیت ضروری ہے البتہ رمضان کی ادا اور قضا میں کچھ فرق ہے کہ رمضان کی قضا میں تعیین شرط ہے جبکہ اس کی ادا میں تعیین شرط نہیں ہے۔
And the vowed (act) is like fard: the vowed act is like fard. Just as intention is necessary for the validity and specification of fard, similarly intention is necessary for the validity and specification of a vow. This analogy is based on whether a vow is fard or wajib. Some hold it is wajib, some hold it is fard. Ibn Nujaym al-Misri holds that a vow is wajib. A vow is defined as a person making a non-obligatory thing obligatory on himself. Its ruling is that it stands in place of fard; fulfilling it is necessary provided it is not a vow of sin or a vow of a worship that is not intended for itself, and it comprises an act of obedience that belongs to the category of intended obligatory acts. 'And if one vows the Hajj of Islam': if a person makes a vow that if a certain thing happens, he will perform the obligatory Hajj, then upon him only the fard Hajj is obligatory; the vow does not make the Hajj fard (again) because among the conditions of a vow is that the vowed act is not already obligatory. Since here the vowed act is already obligatory, the condition is missing, so the vow is not valid, and only the original fard remains. It is like if someone vows a sacrifice during the days of sacrifice while a sacrifice is already obligatory on him, then the vow does not make it obligatory; only the originally obligatory sacrifice is due. 'And qada' in all cases': Just as intention is necessary for the validity and specification of ada', similarly intention is necessary for the validity and specification of qada'. However, there is a difference between ada' and qada' of Ramadan: in qada' of Ramadan, specification (ta'yin) is a condition, whereas in its ada', specification is not a condition.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage discusses two topics: vows (nadhr) and make-up (qada'). First, regarding vows: The author states that a vowed act is like fard in requiring intention. That is, if someone vows to perform an act of worship, he must have the intention to fulfill that specific vow. The passage explains that a vow is a commitment to do something that is not originally obligatory. The Hanafi position is that a vow becomes wajib (obligatory) to fulfill, provided the vowed act is from the category of intended acts of worship and is not sinful. However, if someone vows an act that is already obligatory (like the fard Hajj for someone who has not performed it), the vow is not effective because the condition of the vow (that the act is not already wajib) is missing. The example given is if someone vows to perform the obligatory Hajj, he already owes the fard Hajj, so the vow does not add another obligation. Similarly, if one vows a sacrifice during the sacrificial days while a sacrifice is already obligatory, the vow is redundant. Second, regarding qada': The passage says that qada' (making up missed acts) requires intention just like ada' (performing on time). However, for the qada' of Ramadan fasts, one must specify the day (e.g., 'I intend to make up the missed fast of such and such day'), whereas for the ada' of Ramadan, specifying the day is not required because the fast is already specified by the month itself.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow to make a non-obligatory act obligatory on oneself.
قضاء (qada'): The make-up of a missed obligatory act of worship.
تعیین (ta'yin): Specification of the particular act or day intended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a person who has never performed Hajj vows to perform the obligatory Hajj, what happens?
A) He must perform two Hajj.
B) He only owes the original fard Hajj.
C) The vow becomes invalid because it is impossible.
D) He must perform the Hajj as a vow plus the fard.

Key Takeaway
For vows to be valid, the vowed act must not already be obligatory, and intention is required for both fulfilling a vow and making up missed acts, with specification needed for Ramadan qada'.

Applying the Qawida of Dhaman to Unauthorized Slaughter in Udhiyah
Tafri' applying dhaman qawida to udhiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida of dhaman to determine ownership and validity of udhiyah in cases of unauthorized slaughter.

Core Idea
If the slaughterer is held liable, his sacrifice counts—dhaman retroactively transfers ownership.

This passage explores a subtle but powerful application of a Hanafi legal maxim. You will see how the qawida 'the one who pays compensation becomes owner retroactively' resolves a seeming contradiction when an animal bought for sacrifice is slaughtered by someone else without permission. The key is whether the buyer holds the slaughterer liable—a choice that determines whose sacrifice is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling on intention
Note that the Hanafi position allows intention for udhiyah to be made at the time of purchase, not necessarily at slaughter, analogous to zakat.
This is the foundation for the tafri' (derived case).
2
Understand the two scenarios of the tafri'
If someone buys an animal with intention, and another slaughters it without permission: (1) buyer takes the animal without holding liable → sacrifice is for buyer; (2) buyer holds slaughterer liable → sacrifice is for slaughterer.
The second scenario seems contradictory because the buyer had already intended sacrifice.
3
Recognize the apparent contradiction
Rationally, since the buyer intended sacrifice at purchase, and the animal was in his ownership at slaughter, imposing liability on the slaughterer seems unfair.
This is the 'perceived contradiction' that the qawida resolves.
4
Apply the qawida of dhaman
The qawida: 'The one who pays compensation becomes owner of the compensated thing from the time compensation became obligatory.' Thus, when the slaughterer is held liable, he retroactively owns the animal from the moment of usurpation (i.e., the moment he slaughtered).
Therefore, at the moment of slaughter, the animal was his, and his sacrifice is valid.

تشريح : بذل الحمود میں اس میں چار افات لکھتے ہیں اضحیه (بضم الهمزه) إضحيه ( بكسر الهمزه) اس کی اضاحی ہے ضحیۃ اس کی جمع ضحایا ہے اور اضحاۃ اس کی جمع اضحا ہے۔و فی الدر المختار: الأضحية لغةً إسم لما يذبح أيام الأضحى من تسمية الشئ بإسم وقته. وقال الكرخي: وهي ما يذبح يوم العيد تقرباً إلى الله تعالى وسميت بذالك لأنها تفعل لأضحى. قربانی بھی عبادت مقصود ہے اس لئے اسکی صحت کیلئے نیت ضروری ہے۔ لیکن عند الشراء لاعند الذبیح اس سے اگر چہ ی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ نیت خریدنے کے وقت ضروری ہے ذبح کے وقت نہیں حالانکہ اصل یہ ہے کہ ذبح کے وقت نیت ضروری ھے اور اگر خریدنے کے وقت بھی نیت کر لی تو وہ نیت بھی کافی ہے جیسے زکوۃ دیتے وقت نیت ضروری ہے لیکن اگر مال زکوۃ کو علاحدہ کرتے وقت نیت کرلی اور دیتے وقت زکوۃ کی نیت نہ کرے تو کافی ہے۔
علامہ ابن نجیم تفریع پیش کرتے ہوئے تحریر کرتے ہیں۔ کہ اگر کسی نے جانور کو خریدتے وقت قربانی کی نیت کی پھر کسی دوسرے آدمی نے مالک کی دلالہ یا صراحہ اجازت کے بغیر اسکو اپنی طرف سے ذبح کر دیا تو اب دو صورتیں ہیں کہ خریدنے والا ذبح کئے ہوئے جانور کو لے لے اور اسے ضامن نہ بنائے ۔ دوسری صورت میں اس مذبوحہ جانور کو نہ لے اور اسے ضامن بنالے، پہلی صورت میں قربانی جانور خریدنے والے کی طرف سے ہوگی اور دوسری صورت میں خود ذائج کی طرف سے قربانی ہو جائیگی۔ لیکن اگر ذابح نے جانور خود مالک ہی کی طرف سے ذبح کیا ہے تو اس صورت میں ذابح پر تاوان نہ ہوگا ۔ چونکہ ان مسائل میں قربانی کی نیت جانور کے خریدتے وقت ہی کر لی گئی تھی وہی کافی ہو جاتی ہے بوقت ذبح نیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہوتا۔
لكن عند الشراء: جانوروں کے خریدنے کے وقت نیت کا اعتبار ہے۔ اس کا ثمرہ اس صورت میں ظاہر ہوگا کہ جب کسی نے قربانی کی نیت سے کوئی جانور خریدا پھر اس نے یا کسی اور نے مالک کی اجازت کے بغیر اسے بغیر نیت ذبح کے ذبح کر ڈالا تو اس جانور کی قربانی درست ہو جائے گی اور خرید نے کے وقت کی نیت کافی ہوگی لیکن اگر خریدتے وقت قربانی کی نیت نہیں کی پھر اسی نے یا کسی اور نے بغیر ذبح کی نیت کے ذبح کر ڈالا تو قربانی درست نہ ہوگی۔
تفریح میں جو دوسری صورت ہے اور اس میں ذائع کو ضامن بنایا گیا ہے عقلاً اس کو ضامن بنانا درست نہیں ہونا چاہئے تھا کیونکہ جب بوقت شراء جانور کے مالک نے قربانی کی نیت سے جانور خریدا اور کسی دوسرے نے بغیر مالک جانور کے جانور ذبح کر ڈالا تو جس وقت اس غیر نے جانور کو ذبح کیا ہے اس وقت تو مالک جانور کی ملکیت میں وہ جانور مذبوح ہوا اور بوقت شراء قربانی کی نیت پائی ہی گئی جو قربانی کے لئے کافی ہے تو اس غیر پر تاوان کو لازم کرنا درست نہیں ہونا چاہئے تھا۔
اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ فقہ کا قاعدہ ہے کہ ضمان دینے سے ضامن شئی مضمونہ کا مالک ہو جاتا ہے اور یہ ملکیت اسی وقت سے تعلیم کی جاتی ہے جس وقت سے ضمان واجب ہوا تھا تو ظاہر ہے کہ جس وقت اس نے جانور کو غصب کیا تھا اسی وقت سے اس ضامن کو اس جانور کا مالک سمجھا جائے گا تو جس وقت اس نے جانور ذبح کیا ہے وہ ذائج کی ملکیت میں ہی تھا اس لئے اس سے تاوان لینا بھی درست ہوا اور قربانی ذائع ہی کی طرف سے سمجھی جائے گی۔
Tashrih: In Badhl al-Mahmud, it writes four words for udhiyah: udhiyah (with dhamma on hamza), idhiyah (with kasra on hamza), its plural is adahi; dhiyah, its plural is dhahaya; and adhah, its plural is adha. And in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: al-udhiyah linguistically is a name for what is slaughtered on the days of Adha, naming the thing by the name of its time. And al-Karkhi said: It is what is slaughtered on the day of Eid as a means of nearness to Allah, and it is called that because it is done for Adha. Sacrifice is also an intended worship, so intention is necessary for its validity. But the intention is at the time of purchase, not at the time of slaughter, from which it seems that intention is necessary at the time of purchase, not at the time of slaughter, even though the principle is that intention is necessary at the time of slaughter; but if one also makes intention at the time of purchase, that intention is sufficient. Just as in zakat, intention is necessary at the time of payment, but if one separates the zakat wealth and makes intention at that time and does not make intention at the time of payment, it is sufficient.
Allamah Ibn Nujaym, while presenting a tafri', writes: If someone bought an animal with the intention of sacrifice, then another person slaughtered it without the owner's permission, whether implicitly or explicitly, and he slaughtered it on his own behalf; then there are two scenarios: that the buyer takes the slaughtered animal and does not hold him liable; the second scenario: he does not take that slaughtered animal and holds him liable. In the first scenario, the sacrifice is on behalf of the buyer; in the second scenario, the sacrifice is on behalf of the slaughterer himself. But if the slaughterer slaughtered the animal himself on behalf of the owner, then in that case there is no penalty on the slaughterer. Since in these issues the intention for sacrifice was already made at the time of buying the animal, that is sufficient; it is not necessary to make intention at the time of slaughter.
However, when purchased: consideration is given to the intention at the time of buying the animal. Its fruit appears in this scenario: when someone bought an animal with the intention of sacrifice, then he or someone else slaughtered it without the owner's permission and without intention of slaughter, then that animal's sacrifice will be valid and the intention at the time of purchase will be sufficient. But if at the time of purchase he did not make intention for sacrifice, then later he or someone else slaughtered it without intention of slaughter, then the sacrifice will not be valid.
In the tafri', the second scenario is where the slaughterer is made liable; rationally, making him liable should not be correct because when at the time of purchase the owner bought the animal with intention of sacrifice, and someone else slaughtered it without the owner's permission, then at the time that other person slaughtered the animal, the animal was in the ownership of the owner – it was slaughtered – and at the time of purchase the intention of sacrifice was already present, which is sufficient for sacrifice, so imposing compensation on that other person should not be correct.
The answer is that the legal maxim is: the one who pays compensation becomes the owner of the compensated thing from the time the compensation became obligatory. So it is clear that from the time he usurped (ghasb) the animal, from that time the compensator is considered the owner of that animal. So when he slaughtered the animal, it was in the ownership of the slaughterer; therefore, taking compensation from him is correct, and the sacrifice will be considered on behalf of the slaughterer.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the qawida (legal maxim) concerning dhaman (compensation) and its application in the context of udhiyah (sacrificial animal). The author first establishes that intention (niyyah) for udhiyah is valid at the time of purchase, not necessarily at slaughter, analogous to zakat. Then Ibn Nujaym presents a tafri' (derived case): if someone buys an animal with intention of sacrifice, and another person slaughters it without permission, two scenarios arise. The ruling depends on whether the buyer takes the slaughtered animal or holds the slaughterer liable. The apparent contradiction — why should the slaughterer be liable if the buyer already had intention? — is resolved by the qawida: the one who pays compensation (dhaman) becomes owner retroactively from the time of the wrongful act (ghasb). Thus, when the slaughterer usurped the animal (by unauthorized slaughter), he became liable; upon paying compensation, he becomes owner from that moment, so his slaughter is on his own behalf. This application demonstrates the power of the qawida in resolving apparent anomalies.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Deliberate intention required for validity of worship; for udhiyah, can be made at time of purchase and suffices even if not renewed at slaughter.
اضحیہ (udhiyah): Sacrificial animal slaughtered on the days of Eid al-Adha for taqarrub.
ضمان (dhaman): Financial liability or compensation; here, the obligation to pay the value of a usurped property.
غصب (ghasp): Wrongful taking of property without owner's consent, creating liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a person buys an animal with intention of sacrifice, and another person slaughters it without permission and is held liable, whose sacrifice is valid according to the Hanafi qawida of dhaman?
A) The buyer's
B) The slaughterer's
C) Neither
D) Both

Key Takeaway
The qawida of dhaman (retroactive ownership upon liability) resolves the apparent contradiction between valid intention at purchase and liability for unauthorized slaughter.

Maxim: Guarantor Becomes Owner from Time of Guarantee
Applying the qawida of daman to a case of ghasb and udhiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal maxim that a guarantor becomes owner from the time the guarantee becomes obligatory, and evaluate its application in cases of usurpation (ghasb) and sacrifice (udhiyah).

Core Idea
A guarantor owns the guaranteed item retroactively from the moment liability arose, not from the contract date.

This lesson presents a key Hanafi legal maxim (qawida) concerning guarantees (daman). The maxim states that when a person gives a guarantee for a specific item, the guarantor becomes its owner, and this ownership is retroactively effective from the time the guarantee became obligatory. We will explore this maxim through a concrete case involving usurpation (ghasb) and sacrifice (udhiyah), showing how the maxim resolves the legal status of the animal.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Begin by stating the qawida in Arabic and English. The maxim is: 'By giving a guarantee, the guarantor becomes the owner of the guaranteed thing.' This establishes the general principle.
2
Identify the retroactive effect
Understand that ownership is assigned from the time the guarantee became wajib (obligatory), not from the time of the contract or delivery. This retroactive assignment is crucial for resolving disputes about acts that occurred before the guarantee.
The passage explicitly says 'ownership is established from the time the guarantee became obligatory.'
3
Apply to the case of ghasb and udhiyah
Take the furu: a person usurps an animal, later becomes a guarantor for it, then slaughters it as udhiyah. According to the maxim, the guarantor is considered owner from the moment of usurpation. Therefore, at the time of slaughter, the animal was owned by the slaughterer, making the sacrifice valid. The original owner must be compensated for the usurpation.
The compensation (tawan) is due because the usurpation was a wrongful act, but the ownership is valid for the sacrifice.
4
Note the scope and istithna'at
Recognize that this maxim applies specifically to daman of a specific item (ayn), not to guarantees of debts or general obligations. The source does not list exceptions, but in Hanafi fiqh, there are nuances where ownership does not retroact (e.g., if the guarantor is not the usurper).
This maxim is a sughra (minor) qawida and is restricted by other principles.
5
Synthesize the ruling
Conclude that the udhiyah is valid on behalf of the guarantor, and compensation is required from him to the original owner. This resolves the apparent conflict between the wrongful usurpation and the religious act of sacrifice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ فقہ کا قاعدہ ہے کہ ضمان دینے سے ضامن شئی مضمونہ کا مالک ہو جاتا ہے اور یہ ملکیت اسی وقت سے تعلیم کی جاتی ہے جس وقت سے ضمان واجب ہوا تھا تو ظاہر ہے کہ جس وقت اس نے جانور کو غصب کیا تھا اسی وقت سے اس ضامن کو اس جانور کا مالک سمجھا جائے گا تو جس وقت اس نے جانور ذبح کیا ہے وہ ذائج کی ملکیت میں ہی تھا اس لئے اس سے تاوان لینا بھی درست ہوا اور قربانی ذائع ہی کی طرف سے سمجھی جائے گی۔
The answer to this is that the legal maxim of fiqh is that by giving a guarantee, the guarantor becomes the owner of the guaranteed thing, and this ownership is established from the time the guarantee became obligatory. So it is clear that from the time he usurped the animal, from that time the guarantor is considered the owner of that animal. So at the time he slaughtered the animal, it was in the ownership of the one who slaughtered, therefore taking compensation from him is correct, and the sacrifice is considered to be on behalf of the one who slaughtered.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage presents a qawida (legal maxim) of the Hanafi school: when a person gives a guarantee (daman) for a specific item, the guarantor becomes the owner of that item, and this ownership is retroactively effective from the moment the guarantee became wajib (obligatory). The passage then applies this maxim to a case: a person usurps (ghasb) an animal, and later becomes a guarantor for that animal (or perhaps the animal is subject to a guarantee). According to the maxim, the guarantor is considered the owner from the time of usurpation. Therefore, if he slaughters the animal as udhiyah (sacrifice), it is valid on his behalf, and he must compensate the original owner for the usurpation. This shows how a qawida can resolve complex transactions.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): A guarantee that transfers ownership of the guaranteed item to the guarantor from the time the guarantee becomes obligatory.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; wrongful taking of property without consent.
قربانی (udhiyah): Sacrificial animal slaughtered on Eid al-Adha; requires valid ownership at time of slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi maxim on daman, when does the guarantor become owner of the guaranteed item?
A) From the time of the contract of guarantee.
B) From the time the guarantee became obligatory (wajib).
C) From the time the guarantor actually hands over the item.
D) From the time the original owner loses ownership.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim of daman establishes retroactive ownership from the time of liability, resolving cases of ghasb and udhiyah by validating the guarantor's acts while requiring compensation.

Specification of Udhiyah by Intention: The Sahih View
Ruling with ikhtilaf: specification by intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on specification of udhiyah by intention and identify the mufta bihi position regarding the rich.

Core Idea
Intention alone specifies the udhiyah animal for both rich and poor — the sahih view overrides financial status.

In Hanafi fiqh, the udhiyah sacrifice carries specific rulings regarding the animal's legal status once purchased with intention. The earlier view (qaalu) distinguished between a poor and rich person: for the poor, intention creates a binding specification (like a vow); for the rich, it does not. The sahih (correct) view, however, holds that the animal becomes specified absolutely, regardless of the buyer's wealth. This lesson unpacks that dispute and its practical consequences for fatwa, focusing on how a mufti navigates between these opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Locate in the matn the statement 'qaalu' (they said) and the subsequent distinction: for a poor person, the animal is specified; for a rich person, it is not. Then note the corrective 'al-sahih' (the correct view) that it is specified absolutely.
The matn uses 'qaalu' to refer to earlier Hanafi scholars, and 'al-sahih' to indicate the preferred view.
2
Understand the illa for the poor
Recognise that for the poor, the purchase with intention is analogous to a nadhr (vow). Even without verbal utterance, intention suffices to make the animal specified, as held by the majority of scholars.
This analogy is the key dalil for specification in the poor case.
3
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
Examine the practical consequence: if the animal is lost or dies, under the earlier view the poor is not obliged to replace it, but the rich is. Under the sahih view, both must replace if they intend to fulfill the sacrifice. Also, if the lost animal is found, the poor sacrifices both, the rich only one.
This shows how the ikhtilaf plays out in real-world fatwa.
4
Apply the sahih view
According to the sahih view, the animal is specified for both. However, the rich person is permitted to substitute another animal during the days of sacrifice (as in al-Bada'i). After the days, if unsacrificed, the animal must be given in charity alive.
The substitution does not negate specification; it is a separate permission.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The sahih position (absolute specification) is the relied-upon view for fatwa. This means the mufti should advise that a rich person’s intended udhiyah animal becomes specified and cannot be sold, though it can be replaced.
This tarjih is based on the principle that intention creates obligation, not financial status.

Source Text

وَهَلْ تَتَعَيَّنُ الأَضْحِيَّةُ بِالنِّيَّةِ قَالُوْا إِنْ كَانَ فَقِيْراً وَقَدْ إِشْتَرَاهَا بِنِيَّتِهَا تَعَيَّنَتْ فَلَيْسَ لَهُ بَيْعُهَا وَإِنْ كَانَ غَنِياً لَمْ تَتَعَيَّنَ وَالصَّحِيحُ أَنَّهَا تَتَعَيَّنُ مُطْلَقاً فَيَتَصَدَّقُ بِهَا الْغَنِيُّ بَعْدَ أَيَّامِهَا حَيَّةٌ وَلَكِنْ لَهُ أَنْ يُقِيْمَ غَيْرَهَا مَقَامَهَا كَمَا فِي الْبَدَائِعِ مِنَ الْأضْحِيَّةِ قَالُوْا قربانی کے لئے متعین نہیں ہوگا۔ ثمرہ اختلاف اس صورت میں ظاہر ہوگا کہ اگر غریب کا جانور گم ہو گیا یا مر گیا تو اس پر دوسرا جانور خرید کر اس کی قربانی ضروری نہیں ہے جب کہ مالدار پر دوسرا جانور خرید کر الاسلام زمینیہ منگور میں اس متعین اونٹ کو بطور صدقہ نہیں دے گا اس وقت تک وہ نذر سے بری نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر اس نے اشاعت الاسلام زمینیہ میں اس متعین اونٹ کے بجائے جامعہ عربیہ مدرستہ المؤمنین قصبہ منگور الماری میں زکوۃ کی نیت سے الگ رکھا ہوا ہے وہ متعین رہے گا’ و الصحيح أنها تتعین“ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جب تک وہ کسی دوسرے جانور کی قربانی نہ کردے اس وقت تک وہ جانور قربانی کے لئے متعین رہے گا۔ فيتصدق الخ: اگر ایام قربانی گذر جائیں اور کسی وجہ سے مال دار قربانی نہ کرے تو اس کے لئے حکم یہ ہے کہ زندہ جانور کو صدقہ کر دے کیونکہ اصل تو صدقہ ہی ہے اگر چہ ایام قربانی میں احراق الدم افضل ہے لیکن جب ایام نحر تا کہ اعتراض واقع نہ ہو کہ ایام نخر گذر نے پر زندہ جانور کو صدقہ کرنا یا گم ہو جانے یا مر جانے پر دوسرے جانور کی قربانی ضروری ہے۔ تو کہنا درست نہیں ہے جو جواز پر دلالت کرتا ہے وجوب پر نہیں۔ نیز او ر کہا والصحيح انها تتعین اور بعد میں کہا کہ مال دار جانور کو بدل سکتا ہے تو مصنف کی عبارت میں بظاہر تضاد ہے تو اس کا جواب لہ سے دیا ہے کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ مصنف کی مراد اس سے وہ ہو جس کو ہم نے اس سے پہلے دوسری کو ہدی کہا جاتا ہے۔
Translation of the Arabic matn: 'And is the udhiyah specified by intention? They said: If he is poor and bought it with its intention, it becomes specified, so he cannot sell it. If he is rich, it is not specified. The correct view is that it is specified absolutely, so the rich person gives it in charity alive after its days, but he may replace it with another, as in al-Bada'i'. They said: The hadaya are like the udhiyah.' The Urdu sharh explains: 'Translation: And does the animal for sacrifice become specified by intention? The jurists say that if he is poor and bought it with the intention of sacrifice, it becomes specified, so selling it is not correct for him. And if he is rich, it is not specified. And according to the correct opinion, it becomes specified absolutely. So after the days of sacrifice, the rich person will give the animal in charity alive, but he is permitted to substitute another in its place, as in al-Bada'i' from the Book of Udhiyah. The jurists say that the hadaya are like the udhiyahs.' Commentary: In this passage, discussing intention, it is said that if one buys an animal with the intention of sacrifice, does it become specified or not? The jurists clarified the difference between rich and poor: if the buyer is poor, the animal becomes specified for sacrifice and he cannot sell it, because for the poor it is like a vow (nadhr), and a vowed item becomes specified even if some scholars require verbal utterance—the majority hold that mere intention suffices. If the buyer is rich, the animal is not specified. The practical consequence (thamarah) of this difference is that if the poor person's animal is lost or dies, he is not obliged to buy another; the rich person is obliged. Then if the lost animal is found and he has bought another, the poor person must sacrifice both, while the rich person only needs to sacrifice one without specification, though it is better to sacrifice both. 'The correct view: it becomes specified absolutely': the correct view is that the animal becomes specified whether the buyer is poor or rich, but there is a slight difference in specification. An example: a man says: 'If my such-and-such work is done, I will give a specific camel in charity to Madrasa Isha'at al-Islam in Mangalore.' Then if his work is done, he is not free from the vow until he gives that specific camel. But if instead of that specific camel, he gives a different camel to another school, his vow is fulfilled. Similarly, if someone sets aside a specific 1000-rupee note for zakat, then gives a different 1000-rupee note (or two 500s) as zakat, his zakat is fulfilled, but the specific note remains set aside until he pays the amount. 'And the correct view: it becomes specified' means that until he sacrifices another animal, that animal remains specified for sacrifice. 'Then he gives it in charity': if the days of sacrifice pass and the rich person has not sacrificed for any reason, his ruling is that he must give the animal in charity alive because the original act is charity; though slaughter and distribution during the days is better, if the days pass, the ruling returns to its original form, so the rich person must give it in charity alive, and the same applies to the poor. 'But he may replace it': the word 'la' (in 'lakin') is for prevention of a misunderstanding—one might think that after the days pass, giving alive or replacing is obligatory; the text indicates permissibility, not obligation. Also, the apparent contradiction between 'the correct view: it becomes specified' and the later statement 'the rich can replace it' is resolved by explaining that the replacement is like the example previously given. 'And the hadaya are like the udhiyahs': just as general sacrifice rulings apply, similarly the rulings for the sacrifice of Hajj are the same, the only difference being the name: one is called udhiyah and the other hadi.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (rasm) from the fiqh of udhiyah (sacrifice) addressing whether an animal purchased with the intention of sacrifice becomes legally specified (ta'ayyun) for that purpose. The matn presents two positions: the earlier view (qaalu) distinguishes between a poor person (faqir) and a rich person (ghani) — for the poor, intention alone specifies the animal (like a vow), so he cannot sell it; for the rich, it does not become specified. The sahih (correct) view, however, is that it becomes specified absolutely for both. The commentary elaborates: for the poor, the purchase with intention is treated as a nadhr (vow) — even without verbal utterance, the majority hold that intention suffices to create a binding specification. The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence of the disagreement) is that if the animal is lost or dies, the poor person is not obliged to replace it (since it was not obligatory upon him in the first place?), whereas the rich person must buy another. If the lost animal is found, the poor person must sacrifice both (since both are now specified), while the rich person need only sacrifice one (due to non-specification). After the days of sacrifice, if the animal survives, it must be given in charity alive (since the time for sacrifice is past). The rich person may substitute another animal during the days, but that does not negate specification. The hadaya (Hajj sacrifices) follow the same rules as udhiyah, differing only in nomenclature. This passage illustrates how intention interacts with legal classification and the importance of financial status in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
الأضحية (al-udhiyah): The animal sacrificed on the days of Eid al-Adha.
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow that makes a specified thing obligatory upon the person.
التعيين (al-ta'ayyun): Specification of a particular animal for the sacrifice such that it cannot be replaced or sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the sahih (correct) view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on an udhiyah animal purchased with intention by a rich person?
A) It does not become specified; he can sell it.
B) It becomes specified, so he cannot sell it, but he can replace it with another.
C) It becomes specified and cannot be replaced.
D) It becomes specified only if he verbally declares a vow.

Key Takeaway
Intention alone specifies the udhiyah animal for both rich and poor; the sahih view is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications

The Maxim 'والهدايا كالضحايا' and Its Applications in Specification and Substitution
Commentary on specifications of vowed and sacrificial animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'والهدايا كالضحايا' to cases of specification and substitution in vows (nazr) and sacrificial animals (udhiya/hadi), and identify the operative ruling for fatwa.

Core Idea
A specified animal remains earmarked but substitution fulfills the vow or sacrifice.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi maxim that sacrificial animals for Hajj (hadi) follow the same rulings as those for Eid (udhiya). The commentary illustrates key furuat on specification and substitution, including when time for sacrifice expires. Understanding this maxim is essential for muftis to issue correct fatwas on vows and sacrifices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
State the English meaning of 'والهدايا كالضحايا' and note that it applies to the chapters of udhiya and hadi.
The maxim is a sughra (minor) and nathr (miscellaneous) type.
2
Analyze the ruling on specification (ta'ayyun)
From the nazr and zakat examples, extract that once an animal or asset is specified, it remains specified until the obligation is fulfilled or substituted.
The commentator affirms 'و الصحيح أنها تتعين' as the relied-upon view.
3
Understand substitution (tabdeel)
Note that substitution is permissible; the vow is fulfilled by giving a different animal, but the original remains earmarked.
The resolution of the apparent contradiction between specification and substitution is that the latter is a permission, not an obligation.
4
Apply the ruling after the days of sacrifice
If the days of sacrifice pass, a wealthy person must give the living animal in charity because the original purpose (charity) returns.
The ruling for the poor is the same: charity is obligatory.
5
Extend the maxim to further cases
Using the qawida, apply the same principles to hadi (Hajj sacrifice) as to udhiya, noting only the linguistic difference.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf in terminology, not in ruling.

I will give a specific camel as charity at Madrasa Ishaat al-Islam, Zaminia, Mangalore. If his work is done, he will not be free from the vow until he gives that specified camel as charity at Madrasa Ishaat al-Islam, Zaminia, Mangalore. But if instead of that specified camel, he gives a different camel in charity at Jami'ah Arabiyya Madrasat al-Mu'minin, Kasba Mangore, District Haridwar, Uttarakhand, then his vow will be fulfilled. For example, someone set aside a thousand-rupee note in an almirah for zakat, and then he gave a different thousand-rupee note or two five-hundred notes as zakat instead; his vow will be fulfilled, but the note in the almirah remains specified until he gives a thousand rupees as zakat. 'And the correct view is that it becomes specified' means that until he sacrifices another animal, that animal remains specified for sacrifice. 'So he gives charity etc.': If the days of sacrifice pass and a wealthy person does not sacrifice for some reason, the ruling is that he should give the living animal as charity, because the origin is charity, although during the days of sacrifice burning the blood is better; but when the days of sacrifice have passed and he could not sacrifice, the ruling returns to its origin, i.e., charity. Therefore, for a wealthy person, giving that living animal in charity is obligatory, and the same ruling applies to a poor person. 'But he may substitute' – the word 'li' means 'upon' so that an objection does not arise: saying that after the days of sacrifice have passed, giving the living animal in charity or sacrificing another animal if it is lost or dead is obligatory is not correct, because the expression indicates permissibility, not obligation. Also, he said 'and the correct view is that it becomes specified' and later he said that a wealthy person may substitute the animal; so there is an apparent contradiction in the author's text. The answer to this is provided by 'li' that it is possible that the author meant by that what we explained earlier under 'but he may substitute someone else'. 'And the sacrificial animals (for Hajj) are like the sacrificial animals (for 'Eid)': Just as the rulings for general sacrifice apply, similarly the rulings for the Hajj sacrifice apply; the only difference is that one is linguistically called udhiya and the other hadi.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the maxim 'والهدايا كالضحايا' (sacrificial animals for Hajj are like those for 'Eid). It begins by illustrating rulings on vows (nazr) and specification. The commentator explains that when a person vows to give a specific animal in charity, that animal becomes specified (متعين) and the vow is not fulfilled until that particular animal is given. However, substitution is effective: if the person gives a different animal or equivalent value, the vow is fulfilled, though the original animal remains specified until the vow is discharged. Another example concerns zakat: setting aside a specific note does not prevent substitution; however, the specified note remains allocated until the zakat is paid. The phrase 'و الصحيح أنها تتعين' (the correct view is that it becomes specified) is explained: a sacrificial animal becomes specified and remains so until sacrificed or substituted. After the days of sacrifice, a wealthy person must give the living animal as charity because the original purpose was charity (blood sacrifice being better but time-bound). The commentator also resolves an apparent contradiction: the statement that the animal is specified and the later statement that a wealthy person may substitute it are reconciled by interpreting the latter as permissibility, not obligation. Finally, the maxim is stated: sacrificial animals for Hajj (hadi) follow the same rulings as for 'Eid (udhiya), differing only in name.

Key Terms
نذر (nazr): A vow to perform an act of worship if a condition is met.
متعين (mutta'ayyin): A specific item designated for a purpose; it cannot be replaced without affecting the obligation.
هدايا (hadaya): Sacrificial animals offered during Hajj.
ضحايا (dahaya): Sacrificial animals offered during Eid al-Adha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, after the days of sacrifice have passed, what must a wealthy person do with the specified sacrificial animal?
A) Keep it for the next year's sacrifice.
B) Sacrifice it anyway, even if the days have passed.
C) Give the living animal in charity.
D) Sell it and give the money in charity.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'والهدايا كالضحايا' unifies rulings on specification and substitution for all sacrificial animals, with the key nuance that substitution is permissible but the original remains allocated until the obligation is discharged.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications

Emancipation as Qurba: The Maxim and Its Applications
Explaining the legal nature of 'itq, waqf, jihad, and wasiyyah regarding niyyah and reward

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-‘itq laysa bi‘bādah wad‘an' to determine when intention is required for validity vs. reward in acts like emancipation, waqf, and wasiyyah.

Core Idea
Emancipation is not worship; it is valid without intention but reward requires it.

This lesson explores a foundational Hanafi legal maxim: emancipation is not worship by original disposition. The passage distinguishes between 'ibada (worship requiring intention for validity) and qurba (acts of drawing near, valid without intention but reward depends on intention). Understanding this maxim helps you correctly apply rulings to emancipation, waqf, bequests, and jihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim and Its Proof
Extract the core maxim from the text: emancipation is not worship by original disposition. Note the proof: it is valid from a disbeliever, whereas worship is not.
This proof is a logical inference (dalil aqli).
2
Distinguish Between Qurba and 'Ibada
Understand the Hanafi distinction: 'ibada requires intention (niyyah) for validity; qurba requires intention only for reward, not validity.
Examples: salah is 'ibada; freeing a slave is qurba.
3
Apply the Maxim to Furuat (Scenarios)
Work through the given scenarios: explicit words without intention → valid, no reward; allusive words → not valid without intention; emancipation for idols or creatures → valid but sinful or makruh depending on intention.
Each scenario tests the boundary of the maxim.
4
Recognize the Exception: Jihad
Note that jihad is classified as 'ibada, not qurba, because it is among the greatest acts of worship and thus requires sincerity for validity.
This is an istithna' (exception) from the general principle.
5
Apply the Related Maxim 'La thawab illa bi al-niyya'
Connect to the companion rule: reward is only with intention. Even though emancipation is valid without intention, no reward is given without it.
This maxim ensures that acts of qurba become worship when accompanied by sincere intention.

ترجمہ: اور رہی آزادی تو وہ وضع کے اعتبار سے ہمارے نزدیک عبادت نہیں ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ کافر کی طرف سے صحیح ہے حالانکہ اسکے لئے عبادت نہیں پس اگر اللہ کی رضا کی نیت کی تو آزادی عبادت ہوگی اسپر ثواب ہوگا اور اگر بدون نیت آزاد کیا تو صحیح ہے اور ثواب نہیں اگر چہ آزادی صریح ہو ۔ اور بہر حال کنایات تو ان کے لئے نبیت ضروری ہے پس اگر بہت کیلئے یا شیطان کیلئے آزاد کیا تو آزادی صحیح ہے اور وہ گناہ گار ہوگا اور اگر کسی مخلوق کیلئے آزاد کیا تو صحیح ہے اور وہ مباح ہے نہ تو اب ہے اور نہ گناہ اور مناسب ہیکہ بت کیلئے آزاد کرنے کو مخصوص کیا جائے جبکہ آزاد کرنے والا کافر ہو ہر حال مسلمان جب بت کیلئے آزاد کرے بت کی تعظیم کے ارادہ سے تو اس نے کفر کیا جب کرد مناسب ہے کسی مخلوق کیلئے آزاد کرنا مکروہ ہوا اور مدبر اور مکاتب بنانا آزاد کرنے کی ہی طرح ہے۔ تشريح العتق في اللغة القوة وفى الشريعة هي قوة حكمية يصير المكلف اهلا للتصرفات الشرعية.
آزاد کرنا اصلا عبادت نہیں ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ آزادی کا فر کی طرف سے بھی صحیح ہو جاتی ہے، حالانکہ یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ کافر کی عبادت صحیح نہیں ہوتی اس لئے فقہاء نے کہا ہے آزادی قربت ہے اور قربت کی صحت کے لئے نیت ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ عبادت کی صحت کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے۔ قربت و عبادت میں فرق عبادت نام ہے اس کا جس کے ذریعہ بشرط نیست معبود کو پہچانتے ہوئے عبادت کی جائے اور قربت نام ہے اس عمل کا جسکے ذریعہ متقرب الیہ کو پہچان کر اس کی قربت حاصل کی جائے اس لئے امام رافعی نے اسپر نقل کیا ہے کہ محقق متقربات میں سے ہے۔
جب یہ بات متحقق ہوئی کہ محق منتظر بات میں سے ہے عبادت نہیں ہے تو اس کو عبادت بنانے کے لئے نین ضروری ہے تا کہ عبادت اور عادت میں امتیاز ہو جائے اس پر تفریح پیش کرتے ہوئے علامہ ابن نجیم مصری فرمانے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی مسلمان محض رضاء الہی کی خاطر غلام آزاد کرے گا تو وہ آزاد کرنا عبادت ہو گا اس کو اجر و ثواب ملے گا نوٹی کی ضمیر کا مرجع معتق مسلم ہے کافر کو اگر مرجع قرار دیا تو مسئلہ صحیح نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ کافر بہت غیر معتبر ہے وان اعتقی ۔ اگر کسی نے بدون نبت الفاظ صریحہ سے غلام کو آزاد کر دیا تو غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا اس میں نیت کی ضرورت نہیں
لیکن ثواب بدون نیت نہ ملے گا جیسا کہ قاعدہ مشہور ہے لا ثواب الابا لنية. واما الکنایات : الفاظ کنائی کے ذریعہ آزاد کرنے کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے بدون نیت الفاظ کنائی سے غلام کی آزادی کا تحقق نہ ہوگا مثلا لا ملک علیک او خرجت عن ملکی وغیرہ۔
فان اعتق للصنم او للشيطان
غلام کو آزاد کرنے کی چند صورتیں ہیں (۱) بت یا شیطان کے چڑھاوے کے لئے غلام آزاد کیا تو آزادی صحیح ؟ البتہ معتق گناہگار ہوگا ۔ آزادی اس لئے صحیح ہے کہ آزادی کا رکن جو رقیت کے ازالہ میں مؤثر ہوتا ہے وہ موجود ؟
(۲) اللہ کی رضاء کے لئے آر او کرنا (۳) کسی مخلوق کے لئے آزاد کرتا ۔
مسلمان کا بت کے لئے غلام آزاد کرنا موجب کفر ہے اور کسی مخلوق کے نام پر آزاد کرنا مکروہ ہے اگر ہی عمان نے بت کے لئے کسی غلام کو آزاد کیا تو اس کا یہ عمل موجب کفر ہوگا اور اگر کسی مخلوق کے نام پر آزاد کیا تو اس کا عمل بھی کفر ہوگا بشرطیکہ اس سے اس کی تعظیم کی نیت کی ہو ۔
وينبغي ان يكون بت کے لیئے آزادی کو کافر معتق کی طرف منسوب کرنا مناس اس لئے کہ سے یہ بعید از قیاس ہے۔ اور اگر بتوں کی تعظیم کی خاطر کسی مسلمان نے بت کے نام پر آزادی کا ارتکاب کیا تو کافر جائے گا جیسا کہ اوپر گذرا ہے۔
سوال: کسی مخلوق کے نام پر آزاد کرنے کو ایک جگہ مبان اور دوسرے جگہ مکروہ۔ جواب: اس کا یہ ہے کہ اباحت اور کراہیت دونوں ایک ساتھ جمع ہو سکتے ہیں اس لئے کہ کرا بیت واباحت کا دونوں جواز ہی کے فرد ہیں۔ والتدبير والكتابة: اگر آقا اپنے غلام سے یوں کہ دے کہ میرے مرنے کے بعد تو آزاد ہے تو اس غلام کو ھ ہے کہا جائے گا اور آقا کے مرنے کے بعد وہ غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ مکاتب جس کو آقا بدل کتابت ادا کرنے کا حکم دیدے اس کو مکاتب کہتے ہیں۔ لہذا آزادی کے بعد جس طرح اس کے ساتھ وہ تمام تصرفات ممنوع ہو جاتے ہیں جو اس کے غلام کے ہوتے ہوئے درست تھے نہیں علم تو یہ اور کتابت کا بھی ہے۔ وَأَمَّا الْجِهَادُ فَمِنْ أَعْظَمِ الْعِبَادَاتِ فَلَا بُدَّ لَهُ مِنْ خُلُوصِ النِّيَّةِ وَأَمَّا الْوَصِيَّةُ فَكا العتق إن فَصَدَ التَّقَرُّبَ فَلَهُ الثَّوَابُ وَإِلَّا فَهيَ صَحِيحَة فَقَط وَأَمَّا الْوَقْفُ فَلَيْسَ بِعِبَادَةِ وَضْعاً بِدَلِيْلِ صِحْتِهِ مِنَ الْكَافِرِ فَإِنْ نَوَى الْقُرْبَةَ فَلَهُ الثَّوَابُ وَإِلَّا فَلَا.
ترجمہ: اور رہا جہاد تو و ہ بری عبادتوں میں سے ہے تو اس کے لئے خلوص نیت ضروری ہے اور بہر حال وصیت تو وہ مثل آزادی کے ہے اگر تقرب کا ارادہ کیا تو اس کے لئے ثواب ہے ور نہ تو وہ صحیح ہے فقط اور بہر حال وقف تو اصل کے اعتبار سے عبادت نہیں ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے کہ وہ کافر کی جانب سے صحیح ہے پس اگر قربت کی نیت کی تو اس کے لئے ثواب ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ تشریح: ملاعلی قاری لکھتے ہیں الجهاد لغة المشقة وشرعاً بذل المجهود في قتال الكفار اشرة او معاونة بالمال او بالرای او بتكثير السواد اوغیر ذلک(الدر المنضود ج ۲ ص / ۴۸۳) جہاد کا شمار بڑی عبادتوں میں ہوتا ہے لہذا حصول ثواب کے لئے اخلاص نیت ضروری ہے صحت جہادا خلاص نیت
Translation: As for emancipation, according to original disposition, it is not worship in our view. The proof is that it is valid from the disbeliever, even though for him it is not worship. So if one intends the pleasure of Allah, then emancipation becomes worship and he will have reward. If he emancipates without intention, it is valid but no reward, even if the emancipation is explicit. As for allusions, intention is necessary for them. So if he emancipates for an idol or for Satan, the emancipation is valid and he is sinful. If he emancipates for a creature, it is valid and permissible, neither reward nor sin. And it is appropriate that emancipation for an idol be specified when the emancipator is a disbeliever. However, when a Muslim emancipates for an idol with the intention of honoring it, he commits disbelief. It is appropriate that emancipation for a creature is disliked. And making a mudabbar or mukatab is like emancipation. Explanation: al-‘itq linguistically means strength, and in Shariah it is a legal strength by which the legally responsible person becomes eligible for legal dispositions. Emancipation is originally not worship. The proof is that emancipation is valid from the disbeliever, whereas it is agreed that the worship of a disbeliever is not valid. Therefore the jurists said: emancipation is a qurbah (act of drawing near), and for the validity of qurbah, intention is not necessary; rather, for the validity of worship, intention is necessary. The difference between qurbah and worship: worship is that by which, with the condition of intention, one worships the worshipped; qurbah is an act by which one seeks closeness to the one to whom one draws near, recognizing him. So Imam Rafi‘i narrated that it is among the verified means of drawing near. When it is established that it is among the means of drawing near and not worship, then to make it worship, intention is necessary so that worship and habit may be distinguished. Expanding on this, Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says: If a Muslim emancipates a slave solely for the pleasure of Allah, then that emancipation will be worship and he will receive reward (note: the pronoun refers to the Muslim emancipator; if one refers it to the disbeliever, the issue would not be correct because the disbeliever is not reliable). If one emancipates with explicit words without intention, the slave is emancipated and intention is not necessary for validity, but reward is not given without intention, as per the famous rule: 'No reward except with intention.' As for allusions: for emancipation through allusive words, intention is necessary; without intention, emancipation does not occur, e.g., 'You have no ownership over me' or 'You have left my ownership,' etc. If he emancipates for an idol or for Satan: There are several forms of emancipation: (1) If he emancipates a slave as an offering for an idol or Satan, the emancipation is valid, but the emancipator is sinful. The emancipation is valid because the pillar of emancipation, which is effective in removing slave status, is present. (2) Emancipation for the pleasure of Allah. (3) Emancipation for a creature. A Muslim emancipating for an idol causes disbelief; emancipating in the name of a creature is disliked. If a Muslim emancipates a slave for an idol, this act causes disbelief. And if he emancipates in the name of a creature, his act is also disbelief provided he intends veneration. And it is appropriate that emancipation for an idol be attributed to a disbeliever emancipator, because for a Muslim it is far-fetched. If a Muslim commits emancipation in the name of an idol for the veneration of idols, he becomes a disbeliever as previously mentioned. Question: Emancipation in the name of a creature is described in one place as permissible and in another as disliked. Answer: Permissibility and dislike can coexist because both are under the category of permissibility. As for tadbir and kitabah: If a master says to his slave, 'You are free after my death,' that slave is called mudabbar, and after the master's death he becomes free. A mukatab is one to whom the master has given the command to pay a written contract. Therefore, just as after emancipation, all those dispositions that were valid during his slavery become prohibited, the same applies to tadbir and kitabah. As for jihad, it is among the greatest acts of worship, so sincerity of intention is necessary for it. As for wasiyyah (bequest), it is like emancipation: if he intends seeking nearness, he gets reward; otherwise, it is merely valid. As for waqf, it is not worship by original disposition, as evidenced by its validity from a disbeliever. So if he intends qurbah, he gets reward; otherwise, no. Translation: As for jihad, it is among the greatest acts of worship, so sincerity of intention is necessary. As for wasiyyah, it is like emancipation: if he intends seeking nearness, he gets reward; otherwise, it is merely valid. As for waqf, it is not worship by original disposition due to the evidence of its validity from a disbeliever; so if he intends qurbah, he gets reward; otherwise, no. Explanation: Mulla ‘Ali al-Qari writes: Jihad linguistically means hardship, and in Shariah it is expending utmost effort in fighting the disbelievers, either personally or by assisting with wealth, opinion, increasing numbers, etc. (al-Durr al-Manḍūd, vol. 2, p. 483). Jihad is counted among the great acts of worship, so sincerity of intention is necessary for obtaining reward; validity of jihad requires sincerity of intention.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the legal category of emancipation ('itq) and similar acts. The author begins by establishing a key principle: emancipation is not worship by original disposition (wad'an) in the Hanafi school. The proof is that it is valid from a disbeliever, whereas true worship is not valid from a disbeliever. Therefore, emancipation is classified as a qurba (act of drawing near to Allah) rather than 'ibada. The distinction: 'ibada requires niyya for validity, while qurba does not. However, to receive reward, niyya is necessary even for qurba. The passage then applies this to various scenarios: if a Muslim emancipates with intention for Allah's pleasure, it becomes worship and he gets reward. If he emancipates without any intention (using explicit words like 'anta hurr'), the emancipation is valid but no reward. For allusive words (kinayat), intention is necessary for the emancipation to take effect. The author then discusses cases where emancipation is performed for an idol or Satan: the emancipation is valid (because the rukn—removal of slavery—is present) but the emancipator is sinful. For a Muslim to emancipate for an idol with the intention of veneration constitutes kufr. Emancipation for a creature is permissible (mubah) but makruh if done for veneration. The passage reconciles an apparent contradiction by stating that permissibility and dislike can coexist. Next, it covers tadbir (emancipation after death) and kitabah (contractual emancipation), which follow the same rulings. The author then shifts to jihad, which is among the greatest acts of worship and therefore requires sincerity of intention (ikhlas). Similarly, wasiyyah (bequest) is like emancipation: valid even without intention of qurba, but reward requires it. Finally, waqf is like emancipation: not worship by original disposition (valid from a disbeliever), but if one intends qurba, reward accrues; otherwise it is merely valid. Throughout, the commentary uses Hanafi sources like Imam Rafi'i and Ibn Nujaym and cites the rule 'la thawab illa bi al-niyya'.

Key Terms
عتق (‘itq): Emancipation; legally it is the removal of slavery, making the slave free. It is considered a qurba (act of drawing near) not 'ibada by original disposition.
قربت (qurbah): An act by which one seeks closeness to Allah, not requiring intention for validity but requiring it for reward.
کنایات (kināyāt): Allusive words that imply emancipation but are not explicit, e.g., 'la mulka 'alayka' or 'kharajta min mulki'. For these, intention is necessary for the emancipation to take effect.
عبادت (‘ibādah): Worship that by its original nature (wad') requires intention for validity; e.g., salah, sawm, jihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a Muslim emancipates a slave using explicit words (e.g., 'anta hurr') without any intention, what is the ruling?
A) The emancipation is invalid because intention is required for any act of worship.
B) The emancipation is valid but no reward is given.
C) The emancipation is valid and reward is given automatically.
D) The emancipation is invalid because it is not for the sake of Allah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'al-‘itq laysa bi‘bādah wad‘an' distinguishes between acts that are worship by nature and those that are not, affecting the role of intention in validity and reward.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
The Coexistence of Ibaha and Karahah: Freeing Slaves for Creatures
Ruling on freeing slaves for idols (kufr) and creatures (makruh) with maxim on ibaha and karahah coexistence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-ibahah wa al-karahah yajtami'an' to distinguish between valid but disliked actions and invalid actions, and to identify when intention transforms permissibility into kufr.

Core Idea
A makruh action remains legally valid (ja'iz) because ibaha and karahah can coexist within jawaz.

This passage addresses freeing slaves in the name of idols (kufr) versus creatures (makruh). A seeming contradiction arises: why is the act called mubah in one place and makruh in another? The answer lies in a key Hanafi qawida: permissibility and dislike can coexist, as both are subsets of jawaz. Understanding this principle prevents the error of equating 'disliked' with 'invalid'.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its rank
Identify the qawida: 'al-ibahah wa al-karahah yajtami'an' (Permissibility and dislike can coexist). Rank it as a wusta (intermediate) maxim and note its type (dabt fiqhi).
This maxim governs cases where an action is legally permissible but undesirable.
2
Identify the scope of the maxim
Determine which fiqh chapters this maxim applies to. It applies broadly to acts of worship and transactions where an action may be valid but disliked.
The scope is all chapters; the key is that karahah does not negate jawaz.
3
Work through the furuat
Apply the maxim to the case given: freeing a slave in the name of a creature without veneration. The act is makruh but valid (ja'iz), not invalid.
The maxim explains why the same act can be described as both mubah and makruh in different contexts.
4
Identify the istithna' (exception)
Check if there are exceptions where karahah invalidates the act. Here, if the intention is veneration of the creature, the act becomes kufr (invalid). This exception is governed by the related qawida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
The exception shows that when karahah is coupled with kufr intention, it is no longer within the jawaz category.
5
Note related qawaid
The maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' parallels this one: intention can elevate or lower the ruling but does not change the essential permissibility of the act itself.
Understanding the relationship between these maxims helps in fatwa application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) اللہ کی رضاء کے لئے آر او کرنا (۳) کسی مخلوق کے لئے آزاد کرتا ۔
مسلمان کا بت کے لئے غلام آزاد کرنا موجب کفر ہے اور کسی مخلوق کے نام پر آزاد کرنا مکروہ ہے اگر ہی عمان نے بت کے لئے کسی غلام کو آزاد کیا تو اس کا یہ عمل موجب کفر ہوگا اور اگر کسی مخلوق کے نام پر آزاد کیا تو اس کا عمل بھی کفر ہوگا بشرطیکہ اس سے اس کی تعظیم کی نیت کی ہو ۔
وينبغي ان يكون بت کے لیئے آزادی کو کافر معتق کی طرف منسوب کرنا مناس اس لئے کہ سے یہ بعید از قیاس ہے۔ اور اگر بتوں کی تعظیم کی خاطر کسی مسلمان نے بت کے نام پر آزادی کا ارتکاب کیا تو کافر جائے گا جیسا کہ اوپر گذرا ہے۔
سوال: کسی مخلوق کے نام پر آزاد کرنے کو ایک جگہ مباح اور دوسرے جگہ مکروہ۔ جواب: اس کا یہ ہے کہ اباحت اور کراہیت دونوں ایک ساتھ جمع ہو سکتے ہیں اس لئے کہ کراہت واباحت دونوں جواز ہی کے فرد ہیں۔
(2) To do it for the pleasure of Allah. (3) To free for a creature. A Muslim freeing a slave for an idol is kufr, and freeing in the name of a creature is makruh. If a Muslim freed a slave for an idol, this action would be kufr. And if he freed in the name of a creature, his action would also be kufr, provided he intended veneration thereby. And it should be that attributing the freeing for an idol to the kafir emancipator is appropriate because this is far from analogy. And if a Muslim, for the sake of venerating idols, committed freeing in the name of an idol, he will become a kafir, as passed above. Question: In one place, freeing in the name of a creature is called mubah, and in another place makruh. Answer: The answer is that ibaha and karahah can both come together, because karahah and ibaha are both types of permissibility (jawaz).
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on freeing slaves and then clarifies a seeming contradiction. It first states two categories: freeing for Allah's pleasure and freeing for a creature. The focus is on freeing for an idol: a Muslim doing so becomes a kafir. Freeing in the name of a creature (e.g., a saint) is makruh but if done intending veneration, it becomes kufr as well. The text notes that ascribing such freeing to a kafir is appropriate because the act is far from qiyas. Then a question arises: why is freeing for a creature called mubah in one place and makruh in another? The answer is that ibaha (permissibility) and karahah (dislike) can coexist because both are subcategories of jawaz. This illustrates the Hanafi qawida that permissibility and dislike are not mutually exclusive. In Hanafi usul, a thing can be permissible in itself (ja'iz) but disliked due to an external reason. Thus, the ruling is that the act is valid (jā'iz) but disliked (makruh).

Key Terms
مباح (mubāḥ): An action that is permissible; legally indifferent, neither commanded nor prohibited.
مکروہ (makrūh): An action that is disliked but not forbidden; it is blameworthy but not sinful.
جواز (jawāz): Permissibility; an action that is valid and legally allowed, encompassing mubah and makruh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Muslim frees a slave in the name of a saint without intending veneration, what is the ruling?
A) The emancipation is invalid.
B) The emancipation is valid but makruh.
C) The emancipation is haram.
D) The emancipation is valid and rewarded.

Key Takeaway
A makruh tanzihan action remains legally valid; permissibility (jawaz) includes both mubah and makruh.

Jihad: Intention, Types, and the Principle of Reward
Ruling on jihad: intention for validity vs reward, types, and the maxim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-ajr biqadr al-mashaqqah' to distinguish between haqiqi and majazi jihad and identify the role of ikhlas in obtaining reward.

Core Idea
Reward for jihad requires sincerity; validity only needs basic intention. Greater hardship yields greater reward.

This passage from Ashbah wa al-Nazair discusses jihad in the context of intention and reward. It clarifies a common confusion: while jihad is a great act of worship, its validity does not depend on sincerity (ikhlas) — only the original intention to fight suffices for it to be valid. However, for reward (thawab), ikhlas is essential. The passage then distinguishes between two types of jihad (haqiqi and majazi) and introduces the fundamental qawida: 'al-ajr biqadr al-mashaqqah' — reward is proportional to hardship. This lesson will unpack these rulings and show how this maxim operates in the Hanafi legal tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on jihad's validity and reward
Read the passage carefully. It states that jihad requires original intention (aslah niyyat) for validity, but ikhlas is needed for reward. Recognize that this is analogous to the example of prayer: a prayer performed for show is valid but yields no reward.
The distinction between sihhah (validity) and thawab (reward) is a key Hanafi theme.
2
Classify the two types of jihad
The passage lists haqiqi (physical fighting for Allah) and majazi (spiritual struggle against the self and desires). Note the difference in hardship: haqiqi involves risking life and leaving family, while majazi is internal struggle.
The classification is based on the nature of the effort.
3
Apply the qawida al-ajr biqadr al-mashaqqah
The maxim 'reward is proportional to hardship' is directly applied: because haqiqi jihad involves greater hardship, its reward is greater. This is an explicit example of the maxim's operation.
The maxim appears at the end of the passage as the underlying principle.
4
Extract the broader principle and conditions
The maxim is not absolute: it only applies to valid acts performed with sincere intention. If the act is invalid (e.g., without proper authority) or lacks ikhlas, the hardship does not yield reward. Understand the scope and exceptions.
This connects to the earlier point about ikhlas being a condition for reward.

Source Text

ترجمہ: اور رہا جہاد تو و ہ بری عبادتوں میں سے ہے تو اس کے لئے خلوص نیت ضروری ہے اور بہر حال وصیت تو وہ مثل آزادی کے ہے اگر تقرب کا ارادہ کیا تو اس کے لئے ثواب ہے ور نہ تو وہ صحیح ہے فقط اور بہر حال وقف تو اصل کے اعتبار سے عبادت نہیں ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے کہ وہ کافر کی جانب سے صحیح ہے پس اگر قربت کی نیت کی تو اس کے لئے ثواب ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ تشریح: ملاعلی قاری لکھتے ہیں الجهاد لغة المشقة وشرعاً بذل المجهود في قتال الكفار اشرة او معاونة بالمال او بالرای او بتكثير السواد اوغیر ذلک(الدر المنضود ج ۲ ص / ۴۸۳) جہاد کا شمار بڑی عبادتوں میں ہوتا ہے لہذا حصول ثواب کے لئے اخلاص نیت ضروری ہے صحت جہادا خلاص نیت پر موقوف نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے اصل نیست کافی ہے مثلاً کسی نے دکھلاوے کے لئے نماز پر میں تو انار صحیح ہو جائے گی لیکن ثواب نہ ملے گا کیونکہ حصول ثواب وجود عزیمت پر موقوف ہے جس کو اخلاص کہتے ہیں ایسے ہی جہاد ہے کہ نفس جہاد کی صحت کے لئے اصل نیست شرط ہے لیکن اگر اصل نیت کے ساتھ اخلاص نہیں ہے تو ثواب کا حصول نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ حدیث میں صراحت کے ساتھ ریا کا مجاہد کے لئے بجائے تو اب کے وعید منقول ہے۔
جبار کی دو قسمیں ہیں: (۱) حقیقی (۲) مجازی فضائل کثیر و ہیں اور اس کو حقیقی جہاد کہتے ہیں ۔ اول معنی کا اطلاق ایک جنگ پر ہوتا ہے جو اعلاء کلمتہ اللہ کے لئے دشمنوں سے لڑی جائے اس کے احادیث میں (۲) مجازی معنی کے اعتبار سے جہاد مجاہد و ریاضت اور نفسانی خواہشات کو دباتا لیکن یہ حقیقی جہاد نہیں ہے اس جہاد کے اندر طلبہ امر بالمعروف کرنے والے اور دیگر افراد بھی شامل ہیں جہاد کی دونوں قسموں میں آسمان وزمین کا فرق ہے کیونکہ جہاد حقیقی میں بندہ اپنی جان ہتھیلی پر رکھ کر اللہ کی خاطر بیوی ، بچوں کو تنہا چھوڑ کر میدان جنگ کی طرف نکل پڑتا ہے وہ مشقت کسی طالب علم یا جماعت میں جانے والے کو نہیں ہوسکتی۔ اور اصول یہ ہے گا الاجر بقدر المشقة.
As for jihad, it is among the greatest acts of worship, so sincerity of intention is necessary for it. ... Commentary: Mulla Ali Qari writes: Jihad linguistically is hardship, and legally it is expending effort in fighting the disbelievers, directly or with wealth or opinion or increasing numbers or otherwise. Jihad is counted among the great acts of worship, so for obtaining reward, ikhlas of intention is necessary. The validity of jihad is not dependent on ikhlas; rather for its validity, the original intention is sufficient. For example, if someone prays for show, the prayer is valid but no reward, because obtaining reward depends on existence of 'azimah, which is ikhlas. Similarly, jihad: for validity, original intention is conditional, but if there is no ikhlas with the original intention, reward will not be obtained, as in hadith warning against riya for the mujahid. Jihad is of two types: (1) real (haqiqi), (2) metaphorical (majazi). Both have many virtues; real jihad is fighting enemies for the elevation of Allah's word. Metaphorical jihad is struggling against the self and desires. The difference is vast. The principle is: reward is according to hardship (al-ajr biqadr al-mashaqqah).

Commentary
This passage discusses jihad in the context of intention. It begins with the Arabic text stating that jihad is among the greatest acts of worship and requires sincerity of intention. The Urdu commentary expands: quoting Mulla Ali Qari's definition of jihad (linguistic: hardship; legal: effort in fighting disbelievers). It explains that for jihad to be valid, only the intention to fight (aslah niyyat) is needed; ikhlas (sincerity) is not required for validity but for reward. An analogy with prayer is given: prayer performed for show is valid but has no reward. Similarly, a mujahid who fights for show gains no reward. The passage then distinguishes two types of jihad: haqiqi (actual fighting for Allah) and majazi (spiritual struggle against the self). It emphasizes the vast difference between them, as haqiqi involves risking life. Finally, it states the principle: al-ajr biqadr al-mashaqqah (reward is proportional to hardship), which is a major qawida. This clarifies that while validity of jihad does not require ikhlas, the reward is tied to sincerity and the level of hardship.

Key Terms
جهاد (jihād): Exerting effort in fighting the disbelievers, either directly or through assistance with wealth, opinion, or numbers.
اخلاص (ikhlāṣ): Sincerity; performing an action solely for Allah's pleasure, without any worldly motive.
الاجر بقدر المشقة (al-ajr biqadr al-mashaqqah): The reward is proportional to the hardship endured in performing the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Intention for Validity vs Reward in Non-Ibadat Acts
Explains that for non-ibadat acts, validity requires only asl niyyah, reward requires ikhlas; includes the qawida 'al-ajr biqadr al-mashaqqah' and definitions of wasiyyah and waqf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the role of basic intention (asl niyyah) for validity and sincere intention (ikhlas) for reward in acts like prayer, jihad, will, and endowment, and apply the Hanafi qawida 'al-ajr biqadr al-mashaqqah' to compare reward levels.

Core Idea
For all acts, validity requires only basic intention; reward requires sincerity.

This passage tackles a critical nuance in Hanafi fiqh: an act can be legally valid even if done without sincere intent—only reward depends on ikhlas. We will explore the examples given (prayer, jihad, wasiyyah, waqf) and the underlying qawida that reward is proportional to hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling category
Read the passage and note that it discusses acts that are not pure worship (ghayr ibadat) as well as acts of worship like prayer. The common thread: in all cases, validity requires only the basic intention (asl niyyah), not sincerity.
Even prayer, a pure ibadat, does not require ikhlas for validity; ikhlas is for reward.
2
State the qawida and its scope
The passage introduces the qawida 'al-ajr biqadr al-mashaqqah' (reward is according to hardship) to explain why real jihad gets more reward than metaphorical jihad. Identify where this qawida appears and note its application.
The qawida is used to compare the hardship and reward of different jihad types.
3
Apply the qawida to the examples
For each example (prayer for show, jihad for show, wasiyyah without intention of nearness, waqf without intention of nearness), determine the ruling: the act is valid (sahih) but reward is lost when sincerity is absent.
Use the principle: asl niyyah → validity; ikhlas → reward.
4
Analyze the definitions of wasiyyah and waqf
The passage defines wasiyyah (will) as a deferred transfer for up to one-third, and waqf (endowment) according to the two Hanafi views (Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn). Note how these definitions fit the overall rule: they are valid even without intention, but reward depends on intention.
The intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on waqf (revocable vs irrevocable) is noted but does not affect the validity-reward distinction.
5
Synthesize the fatwa hierarchy
From the passage, extract the mufta bihi (operative) position: for non-ibadat acts and even for ibadat like prayer, validity does not require sincerity; the mufta bihi for waqf follows the Sahibayn (irrevocable) in later fatwa.
This distinction is crucial for muftis when issuing fatwas on the validity of an act.

Source Text

پر موقوف نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے اصل نیست کافی ہے مثلاً کسی نے دکھلاوے کے لئے نماز پر میں تو انار صحیح ہو جائے گی لیکن ثواب نہ ملے گا کیونکہ حصول ثواب وجود عزیمت پر موقوف ہے جس کو اخلاص کہتے ہیں ایسے ہی جہاد ہے کہ نفس جہاد کی صحت کے لئے اصل نیست شرط ہے لیکن اگر اصل نیت کے ساتھ اخلاص نہیں ہے تو ثواب کا حصول نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ حدیث میں صراحت کے ساتھ ریا کا مجاہد کے لئے بجائے تو اب کے وعید منقول ہے۔
جبار کی دو قسمیں ہیں: (۱) حقیقی (۲) مجازی
فضائل کثیر و ہیں اور اس کو حقیقی جہاد کہتے ہیں ۔ اول معنی کا اطلاق ایک جنگ پر ہوتا ہے جو اعلاء کلمتہ اللہ کے لئے دشمنوں سے لڑی جائے اس کے احادیث میں
(۲) مجازی معنی کے اعتبار سے جہاد مجاہد و ریاضت اور نفسانی خواہشات کو دباتا لیکن یہ حقیقی جہاد نہیں ہے اس جہاد کے اندر طلبہ امر بالمعروف کرنے والے اور دیگر افراد بھی شامل ہیں جہاد کی دونوں قسموں میں آسمان وزمین کا فرق ہے کیونکہ جہاد حقیقی میں بندہ اپنی جان ہتھیلی پر رکھ کر اللہ کی خاطر بیوی ، بچوں کو تنہا چھوڑ کر میدان جنگ کی طرف نکل پڑتا ہے وہ مشقت کسی طالب علم یا جماعت میں جانے والے کو نہیں ہوسکتی۔ اور اصول یہ ہے گا
الاجر بقدر المشقة. وأما الوصية : هی تملیک مضاف الى ما بعد الموت ومحل نفاذه الثلث. وصیت بھی محقق کی طرح عبادت نہیں بلکہ متقربات میں سے ہے اگر وصیت سے حصول ثواب اور تقرب منصوبہ تو اس کے لئے نیست ضروری ہے اگر وصیت سے تقرب اور ثواب کا حصول مقصود ہو تو ثواب ملے گا ورنہ نہیں اگرچہ وصیت بدون نیت صحیح ہو جائے گی۔
وأما الوقف الوقف في اللغة الحبس وفي الشريعة حبس العين على ملك الواقف والتصدق بالمنفعة عند ابي حنيفة فيجوز رجوعه وعندهما حبس العين عن التمليك مع التصدق بمنفعتها فتكون العين زائلة الى ملك الله تعالى من وجه. وقف فی نفسہ عبادت نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر یہ عبادت ہوتا تب کا فر کی طرف سے صحیح نہیں ہوتا جب وقف فی قصہ عبادت نہیں رہا تو اگر کوئی مسلمان وقف کرتے وقت قربت کی نیت کرے گا تبھی اسے ثواب ملے گا ورنہ نہیں اگرچہ وقف بدون نیت بھی کیسی ہو جاتا ہے۔
It is not dependent [on reward intention] but for its validity the mere intention is sufficient. For example, if someone prays for show, his prayer will be valid but he will get no reward, because attainment of reward depends on the existence of determination, which is called sincerity. Similarly with jihad: for the validity of jihad itself, the mere intention is a condition, but if with the mere intention there is no sincerity, then reward will not be obtained, as is narrated in hadith with clarity about the threat of punishment for a mujahid for show. Jihad has two types: (1) real, (2) metaphorical. There are many virtues, and it is called real jihad. First meaning applies to a battle fought for the exaltation of Allah's word against enemies, according to hadith. (2) In the metaphorical sense, jihad is struggling against one's lower self and suppressing desires, but this is not real jihad; this jihad includes seekers of knowledge, enjoining good, and others. Between the two types of jihad there is the difference of heaven and earth, because in real jihad a person places his life in his palm and leaves his wife and children alone for Allah's sake and goes to the battlefield; such hardship cannot be for a student or one going to a congregation. The principle is: reward is according to hardship. As for will: it is a transfer of ownership attached to after death, and its place of execution is one-third. A will is not worship like [other acts] but is among means of drawing near. If obtaining reward and nearness is intended through the will, then intention is necessary for it; if nearness and reward are intended, reward will be obtained, otherwise not, though the will will be valid without intention. As for endowment: endowment linguistically means detention; in Shariah, according to Abu Hanifa, it is detention of the substance under the ownership of the endower and giving away the benefit as charity, so he may revoke it; according to the two companions, it is detention of the substance from transfer of ownership along with giving away its benefit as charity, so the substance passes to the ownership of Allah Most High in a sense. In itself, endowment is not worship, because if it were worship, it would not be valid from an unbeliever. Since endowment is not worship, if a Muslim endows with the intention of drawing near, only then will he get reward; otherwise not, even though endowment is valid without intention.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage establishes a key principle in Hanafi fiqh: for acts that are not pure worship (ibadat), validity does not depend on sincerity (ikhlas) or the intention of reward. Rather, the mere intention to perform the act (asl niyyah) is sufficient for its legal validity. However, reward (thawab) is conditional upon sincerity and the intention of seeking nearness to Allah. The author provides examples: prayer, jihad, will (wasiyyah), and endowment (waqf). For each, he emphasizes that the act is valid even if done without sincere intention (e.g., for show or without seeking reward), but reward is only given when the doer intends obedience and closeness to Allah. The passage also defines two types of jihad: actual (military) and metaphorical (spiritual or social struggle), and provides the legal definitions of wasiyyah and waqf according to the Hanafi school, noting the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the nature of waqf. The underlying qawida is that in mu'amalat (transactions and other worldly acts), the act itself is valid without intention, but reward depends on intention. This is a practical rule for muftis: when issuing fatwas, they must distinguish between the validity of an act and the attainment of reward.

Key Terms
اصل نیست (asl niyyah): The basic intention to perform an act, without regard to sincerity or seeking reward.
جہاد حقیقی (jihad haqiqi): Actual military struggle against enemies to exalt Allah's word.
جہاد مجازی (jihad majazi): Metaphorical struggle against one's ego, seeking knowledge, or enjoining good.
وصیت (wasiyyah): A will that transfers ownership of up to one-third of the estate after death.
وقف (waqf): Endowment; detention of a property to give its benefit as charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sincere intention to seek reward
B) Mere intention to perform the act of waqf
C) Both A and B
D) The permission of the endower's heirs

Key Takeaway
For all acts, legal validity requires only the basic intention (asl niyyah); sincere intention (ikhlas) is necessary only for divine reward.
