The Rule: Marriage is Closer to Worship than Seclusion
Explaining why marriage is closer to worship than seclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that marriage in a state of moderation is a confirmed sunnah superior to seclusion for voluntary worship, identify the four proofs from Hanafi sources, and apply the rule with awareness of its condition of i'tidal.

Core Idea
Marriage in moderation is sunnah mu'akkadah and superior to nafl worship seclusion, based on prophetic practice and legal reasoning.

This passage from Sharah al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair explains an important subsidiary rule for muftis: that marriage, when one is able to fulfill its duties, is not merely permissible but a confirmed sunnah that outranks solitary worship. The author clarifies that this rule applies only under conditions of 'i'tidal' (moderation) and supports it with four proofs from the Bada'i' of Imam al-Ayni. Understanding this rule helps muftis prioritize marriage over seclusion in advising the community.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the rule: 'Engaging in marriage (in a state of moderation) is closer to worship and better than seclusion for pure worship.' This is the core ruling being explained.
The rule is not absolute; it depends on the condition of i'tidal.
2
Understand the condition of i'tidal
Note that the superiority applies only when the person is able to fulfill the rights of marriage (mahr, nafaqah, etc.) without falling into injustice or neglecting obligatory duties. This is the state of moderation.
I'tidal is defined in the commentary of Kanz as having the means and not fearing oppression.
3
Classify the ruling level
The ruling for marriage in this state is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah), not fard or wajib. This is according to the correct view (sahih qawl).
Sunnah mu'akkadah is superior to nafl, which is why marriage is better than seclusion for nafl worship.
4
Walk through the four proofs
The author cites four proofs from Badr al-Din al-Ayni: (1) Sunnah is superior to nafl. (2) Leaving sunnah incurs threat, leaving nafl does not. (3) The Prophet consistently married and did not adopt seclusion. (4) Marriage brings multiple benefits: offspring, chastity, provision for wife.
Proof (3) is further strengthened by the principle that the Prophet's practice (sunnah fi'liyya) indicates desirability for his ummah.
5
Address the objection about Prophet Jesus
Recognize that the praise of Jesus for not marrying is specific to his shariah. In our shariah, marriage is superior, so that objection does not apply.
This shows that rulings are shariah-specific; general principles are derived from the Prophet's practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ : اور رہا نکاح تو انہوں نے کہا کہ وہ عبادات کے بہت قریب ہے حتی کہ اس میں مشغول ہونا محض عبادت کے لئے تخلیہ سے بہتر ہے اور وہ حالت اعتدال میں سنت موکدہ ہے صحیح قول کے بموجب چنانچہ تحصیل ثواب کے لئے نیت کی ضرورت پیش آئیگی اور وہ یہ کہ ارادہ کرے اپنے نفس کی عفت اور اس کی پاکدامنی کا اور اولاد حاصل کرنے کا اور کنز کی شرح شرح کبیر میں ہم نے اعتدال کی تفسیر کر دی ہے۔ تشريح النكاح هو فى اللغة الضم والجمع و فى الشريعة هو عقد يرد على تمليك منفعة البضع قصداً والمراد بالنكاح هنا الوطى المترتب على العقد الصحيح. نکاح من جد عبادت ہے اور من وجہ معاملہ ہے لیکن عبادت کے زیادہ قریب ہے چونکہ مسلمانوں کی کثرت کا باعث ہونے کے ساتھ ساتھ سبب عفت اور پاکدامنی کا ذریعہ بھی ہے۔ حتى ان الاشتغال به: ازدواجی زندگی میں مشغول رہ کر زندگی گذار نا خلوت میں رہ کر عبادت کرنے کے مقابلہ میں کئی اعتبار سے بڑھا ہوا اور بہتر ہے جیسا کہ صاحب بدائع نے چند طرق سے استدلال کیا ہے۔ (1) نکاح کرنا سنت ہے جبکہ محض عبادت کے لئے خلوت اختیار کرنا نفل ہے اور سنت نفل سے بڑھکر ہے۔ (۲) ترک سنت پر وعید ہے اور ترک نفل پر وعید نہیں۔ (۳) آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے نکاح کئے اور اس پر مواظبت فرمائی اور آپ نے نکاح سے تخلیہ نہیں فرمایا بلکہ دوسروں کے مقابلہ میں اور زیادہ نکاح کئے ، جب آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے حق میں نکاح کی افضلیت ثابت ہوگئی تو آپ کی امت کے حق میں بھی یہی افضل ہوگا اس لئے کہ اصل شرائع میں عموم ہے اور خصوص دلیل پر موقوف ہے۔ (۴) یہ نکاح نوافل سے افضل ہے کیونکہ اولاد کے حصول کا سبب ہے اپنے نفس کو بے حیائی اور اپنی بیوی کو نفقہ، سکتی اور لباس دیکر بے حیائی سے بچانا ہے۔ ان امور مذکورہ کی وجہ سے نکاح کو نفلی عبادت کے لئے خلوت اختیار کرنے پر افضلیت حاصل ہے۔ اور حضرت عیسیٰ علیہ السلام کی ترک نکاح پر جو تعریف قرآن شریف میں مذکور ہے تو وہ ان کی شریعت کے اعتبار سے ہے ہماری شریعت میں یہ افضلیت کا باعث نہیں ہے۔ (حاشيه الحموي مع الاشباه ص ۸۳)
Translation: And as for marriage, they said that it is very close to acts of worship, such that engaging in it is better than seclusion purely for worship, and it is a confirmed sunnah in a state of moderation according to the correct view. Hence, intention is needed to attain reward, and that is to intend the chastity of one's soul and its purity, and to obtain offspring, and we have explained moderation in the commentary of Kanz in the great commentary. Explanation: Nikah linguistically means joining and gathering, and in shariah it is a contract that effects ownership of the benefit of the vulva intentionally, and by nikah here is meant the intercourse resulting from a valid contract. Nikah is worship in one respect and transaction in another, but it is closer to worship because it causes increase of Muslims and also becomes a means of chastity and purity. So much so that engaging in married life and passing life is better in several respects than remaining in seclusion for worship. As the author of Bada'i has argued through several ways: (1) Nikah is sunnah, while seclusion purely for worship is nafl, and sunnah is superior to nafl. (2) There is a threat for leaving sunnah, but no threat for leaving nafl. (3) The Prophet ﷺ performed marriage and adhered to it, and he did not adopt seclusion from marriage; rather he performed more marriages than others. When superiority of marriage is established for the Prophet, it will also be superior for his ummah, because the original in shariahs is generality and is dependent on a specific proof. (4) This marriage is superior to voluntary prayers because it is a means of obtaining offspring, protecting oneself from lewdness, and providing maintenance, dwelling, and clothing to one's wife, thus protecting her from lewdness. Due to these mentioned matters, marriage has superiority over adopting seclusion for voluntary worship. And the praise of Jesus عليه السلام mentioned in the Noble Qur'an for abandoning marriage is according to his shariah, but in our shariah it is not a cause of superiority. (Hashiyah al-Hamawi with al-Ashbah, p. 83)
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage begins by establishing that marriage is an act of worship, but not purely so; it also has elements of transaction. However, it is closer to worship because of its spiritual and social benefits. The author then clarifies that the default ruling for marriage is sunnah mu'akkadah, but this applies only in a state of moderation (i'tidal). He then offers four rational proofs from the work of Imam Badr al-Din al-Ayni (author of Bada'i') to demonstrate that marriage is superior to seclusion for voluntary worship: (1) the superior rank of sunnah over nafl, (2) the threat of punishment for leaving sunnah, (3) the prophetic practice of marrying and not abandoning it, (4) the worldly and otherworldly benefits of marriage. The passage concludes by addressing a potential objection based on the praise of Prophet Jesus for remaining unmarried, explaining that this was specific to his shariah and not applicable to the ummah of Prophet Muhammad.

Key Terms
نكاح (nikah): Legally, a contract that effects ownership of the benefit of the vulva (tamlik manfa'at al-bud') intentionally; here it refers to the sexual intercourse resulting from a valid contract.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah, which is a recommended act that the Prophet regularly performed and emphasized, leaving it without excuse is blameworthy.
اعتدال (i'tidal): A state of moderation where one is able to fulfill the rights of marriage (mahr, nafaqah) without falling into injustice or neglecting obligatory duties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the proofs offered for the superiority of marriage over seclusion?
A) Sunnah is superior to nafl.
B) Leaving sunnah incurs a threat of punishment.
C) The Prophet married and did not seclude.
D) Marriage is a financial transaction.

Key Takeaway
Marriage in a state of i'tidal is a confirmed sunnah and closer to worship than seclusion for nafl acts, based on prophetic practice, legal hierarchy, and tangible benefits.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

Five Categories of Marriage and Conditions for Sunnah Mu'akkadah
Classifying marriage rulings from fard to haram and clarifying role of intention and moderation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five rulings of marriage according to personal circumstance and apply the conditions that determine whether it is fard, wajib, sunnah mu'akkadah, makruh, or haram.

Core Idea
Marriage is sunnah mu'akkadah only when one can afford rights and avoid injustice; otherwise it shifts to wajib, fard, makruh, or haram.

The default ruling of marriage for a person in moderation is sunnah mu'akkadah. However, this ruling is not fixed; it changes based on one's ability to fulfill marital rights and the risk of sin. In this lesson, we will dissect the five-category classification and the conditions that determine each ruling, as well as the role of intention and the meaning of 'moderation' (i'tidal).

Guided Path
1
Grasp the classification framework
Recognize that the ruling of marriage depends on personal circumstances. There are five categories: fard, wajib, sunnah mu'akkadah, makruh, and haram.
The passage lists them in order of decreasing obligation.
2
Identify the conditions for each category
For each category, note the key evidential threshold: certainty of zina (fard), strong likelihood but not certainty (wajib), ability to afford rights and no fear of injustice (sunnah), fear of injustice (makruh), certainty of injustice (haram).
The thresholds are based on subjective fear/certainty, not fixed.
3
Apply the conditions for sunnah mu'akkadah
Sunnah mu'akkadah requires three conditions: ability to afford mahr and nafaqah, no fear of falling into injustice (zulm), and no fear of neglecting obligatory duties or sunnahs.
If any condition is missing, the sunnah ruling drops.
4
Understand the role of intention (niyyah)
Intention is not a condition for the validity of the marriage contract; a marriage without pious intention is valid. However, for reward (thawab), one must intend chastity, protecting one's spouse, and seeking lawful offspring.
Mere lust as intention is prohibited.
5
Define moderation (i'tidal)
Moderation is defined by later Hanafi scholars as the state where one is able to afford maintenance, free from fear of injustice or neglect of duties. This is the baseline for sunnah mu'akkadah.
The passage cites Allamah Muyyi, Hasakfi, and Shami for this definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو عند الاعتدال سنة مؤكدة : نكاح کی حکم کے اعتبار سے پانچ قسمیں ہیں۔ (۱) فرض : جبکہ زنا میں مبتلا ہونے کا کامل اور پختہ یقین ہو اور یہ یقین ہو کہ نکاح کے ذریعہ ہی وہ زنا سے محفوظ رہ سکتا ہے تو فرض ہے۔ (۲) واجب ہے جبکہ زنا میں پڑ جانے کا خوف تو نہ ہو لیکن نفس کو بد نظری یا استمنا بالکلف سے بچانا ممکن نہ ہو ۔ (۳) سنت مؤکدہ ہے جبکہ نائح وطی ، مہر اور بیوی کے نفقہ پر بھی قادر ہو اس طرح کہ فرض کے ترک سنتوں سے اعراض اور ظلم میں پڑ جانے کا اندیشہ نہ ہو۔ اگر ان میں سے کسی ایک پر بھی نالح قادر نہ ہو تو صاحب بحر کی تصریح کے مطابق اس کے حق میں نکاح سنت مؤکدہ نہ ہوگا۔ (۴) مکروہ ہے جبکہ ظلم میں پڑ جانے کا خوف ہو۔ (۵) جب ظلم میں پڑ جانے کا پختہ یقین ہو تو پھر حرام ہو جائے گا۔ فيحتاج إلى النية لتحصيل الثواب ، نکاح بذات خود عبادت نہیں ہے کہ عبادت کے قریب ہے نہ جان لئے صحت نکاح کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں ہے البتہ حصول ثواب کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے اور نیت کی وجہ سے کان عبادت ہو جائے گا اگر نکاح کا مقصد محض اتباع شریعت ہے اور امتثال امر نبوی ہے تو بھی ثواب ملے گا۔ وهو ان يقصد الاعفاف: بوقت نکاح بد نیت ہو کہ خود بھی بدنگاہی اور بدکاری سے محفوظ ر ہیں گے اور بیوی کو بھی حرام سے بچانے کی نیت ہو ۔ اسی طرح جائز طریقہ سے اولاد کے حصول کی نیت ہو اگر محض شہوت پورا کرنے کی نیت ہو تو یہ ممنوع ہے۔ وفسرنا الاعتدال: بقول علامہ مویی، علامہ حصکفی اور علامہ شامی نے اعتدال کی تفسیر یہ بیان کی ہے کہ بلی مرور نفقہ پر قادر ہو ظلم میں مبتلا ہونے کا اندیشہ نہ ہو اس طرح فرائض و سنن کے ترک کا بھی خوف نہ ہو۔ اگر ان میں سے کسی ایک بات بھی مقصود ہوگئی تو پھر معتدل حالت باقی نہیں رہے گی لہذا پھر ایسے شخص کے حق میں نکاح سنت بھی نہ ہوگا۔ قوله في الشرح الكبير وصف الشرح بكونه كبيرا للكشف وبيان الواقع لا للاحتراز فانه ليس له شرح صغير المراد من الشرح الكبير هو البحر الرائق للعلامه زين الدين ابن نجيم المصرى المتوفى ٩٧٠ وهو شرح معروف بين العلماء والمفتيين.
And it is at moderation a confirmed sunnah. Marriage has five types in terms of ruling: (1) Fard: when one has complete and firm certainty of falling into zina and is certain that only through marriage can he be protected from zina, then it is fard. (2) Wajib: when there is no fear of falling into zina but it is not possible to protect the soul from evil glances or masturbation. (3) Sunnah mu'akkadah: when one is able to afford spending, mahr, and wife's maintenance in such a way that there is no fear of neglecting obligations, abandoning sunnah, or falling into injustice. If one is not able to afford even one of these, then according to the specification of the author of al-Bahr, marriage will not be sunnah mu'akkadah for him. (4) Makruh: when there is fear of falling into injustice. (5) When there is firm certainty of falling into injustice, then it becomes haram. So intention is needed for attaining reward; marriage in itself is not worship such that it is close to worship. Intention is not a condition for the validity of marriage; however, for attaining reward, intention is necessary, and because of intention, it becomes worship. If the purpose of marriage is merely following the sharia and obeying the Prophet's command, then also reward will be given. That is, to intend chastity: at the time of marriage, one should have the intention that he himself will be protected from evil glances and lewdness and also intend to protect his wife from the haram. Similarly, to intend to obtain offspring through a permissible way. If the intention is merely to satisfy lust, then it is prohibited. And we have explained moderation: according to the statement of Allamah Muyyi, Allamah Hasakfi, and Allamah Shami have explained moderation as being able to afford maintenance, not having fear of falling into injustice, and also not having fear of abandoning obligations and sunnah. If any one of these matters is compromised, then the moderate state will no longer remain; hence, for such a person, marriage will not even be a sunnah. His statement 'in the great commentary': describing the commentary as 'great' is for elaboration and explanation of the reality, not for distinction, for he did not have a small commentary. What is meant by 'the great commentary' is al-Bahr al-Ra'iq by Allamah Zayn al-Din Ibn Nujaym al-Misri (d. 970), which is a well-known commentary among scholars and muftis.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed classification of the legal ruling of marriage according to personal circumstance. It lists five categories from fard to haram, which is a classic Hanafi schematic. The default ruling for a person in a state of moderation is sunnah mu'akkadah, but this changes if conditions are not met. The author then clarifies a key point: intention is not a condition for the validity of the marriage contract itself; a marriage performed even without a pious intention is legally valid. However, to gain spiritual reward, one must have the correct intention of seeking chastity, protecting one's spouse, and obtaining lawful offspring. A mere intention to satisfy lust is blameworthy. Finally, the passage defines 'moderation' (i'tidal) as the ability to provide maintenance (mahr and nafaqah) without fear of injustice or neglect of religious duties. If any of these conditions are missing, the state of moderation is not achieved, and marriage is no longer sunnah mu'akkadah for that individual. The passage also identifies the reference to 'al-sharh al-kabir' as al-Bahr al-Ra'iq by Ibn Nujaym.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): An obligatory act with certainty; marriage becomes fard when one is certain of falling into zina without it.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act; here applies when there is strong likelihood of sin through glances or masturbation, but not certain zina.
سنت مؤکدہ (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah; the default ruling for marriage when one is in a state of moderation and able to fulfill rights.
نیت (niyyah): Intention; not a condition for validity of marriage but required for reward. Correct intention: seeking chastity, protecting spouse, lawful offspring.
اعتدال (i'tidal): Moderation; state where one can afford maintenance, no fear of injustice or neglecting duties. This is the baseline for sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does marriage become fard?
A) When one can afford mahr and nafaqah.
B) When one has complete certainty of falling into zina without it.
C) When one fears falling into injustice.
D) When one is unable to control lust through other means.

Key Takeaway
The ruling of marriage changes from fard to haram based on personal circumstance; intention is needed for reward, not validity.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

Intention in Marriage and Other Acts of Worship
Explaining the role of intention in marriage and extending the principle to all acts of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim that intention is not required for contract validity but is required for reward, and distinguish between situations where intention affects reward versus validity, including exceptions for allusive words and acts of worship.

Core Idea
Intention is not needed for marriage's validity; it is needed for reward — a key distinction between mu'amalat and qurubat.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair explores a crucial distinction in Hanafi law: intention (niyyah) affects reward, not validity, in marriage. However, this rule extends to all acts of worship and has important exceptions. Understanding this maxim sharpens a mufti's ability to distinguish when intention matters for the contract itself versus when it only affects the spiritual outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim
What is the precise rule stated in the passage? The maxim is that intention is not a condition for the validity of marriage (or contracts) but is required for reward.
The Arabic: لا تحتاج النية في صحة العقد بل في الثواب
2
Apply to the furu' case: marriage in jest
Apply the maxim: since intention is not needed for validity, a marriage pronounced jokingly is valid as long as external conditions are met. The hadith of three things being serious and in jest supports this.
The key evidence: ثلاث جدهن جد وهزلهن جد: النكاح والطلاق والرجعة
3
Apply to the furu' case: unknown words
If a person uses words of unknown meaning but knows that such words effect marriage, the marriage is valid according to the mufta bih (relied-upon fatwa). The witnesses' knowledge is not required for validity, though understanding by witnesses is the correct view.
Fatwa is on validity even if witnesses do not understand, per al-Bazzaziyyah.
4
Analyze the exception for kinayah words
For clear (sarih) words, no intention is needed. But for allusive (kinayah) words, intention becomes necessary to determine the intended meaning. This is governed by the maxim 'Acts are judged by intentions.'
Exception to the rule: intention is needed for determining the meaning, not for validity per se.
5
Extend the principle to all qurubat
The same rule applies to all acts of worship (qurubat) like teaching, giving fatwa, and writing: they are valid without intention, but reward depends on sincere intention to draw near to Allah. The passage quotes a hadith warning against seeking knowledge for worldly purposes.
Thus, intention affects reward only, not validity, for these actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پڑ جانے کا پختہ یقین ہو تو پھر حرام ہو جائے گا۔
فيحتاج إلى النية لتحصيل النواب ، نکات بذات خود عمارت نہیں ہے کہ عبادت کے قریب نہ جان لئے صحت نکاح کے لئے نیست شرط نہیں ہے البتہ حصول ثواب کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے اور نیت کی وجہ سے کان عبادت ہو جائے گا اگر نکاح کا مقصد محض اتباع شریعت ہے اور امتثال امر نبوی ہے تو بھی ثواب ملے گا۔ وهو ان يقصد الاعفاف: بوقت نکاح بد نیت ہو کہ خود بھی بدنگاہی اور بدکاری سے محفوظ ر ہیں گے اور یونیکو بھی حرام سے بچانے کی نیت ہو ۔ اسی طرح جائز طریقہ سے اولاد کے حصول کی نیت ہوا اگر محض شہوت پورا کرنے کی نیت ہو تو یہ ممنوع ہے۔
وفسرنا الاعتدال: بقول علامہ موئی، علامہ حصکفی اور علامہ شامی نے اعتدال کی تفسیر یہ بیان کی ہے کہ بلی مرور نفقہ پر قادر ہو ظلم میں مبتلا ہونے کا اندیشہ نہ ہو اس طرح فرائض و سنن کے ترک کا بھی خوف نہ ہو۔ اگر ان میں سے کیا ایک بات بھی مقصود ہوگئی تو پھر معتدل حالت باقی نہیں رہے گی لہذا پھر ایسے شخص کے حق میں نکاح سنت بھی نہ ہوگا۔ قوله في الشرح الكبير وصف الشرح بكونه كبيرا للكشف وبيان الواقع لا للاحتراز فانه ليس له شرح صغير المراد من الشرح الكبير هو البحر الرائق للعلامه زين الدين ابن نجيم المصرى المتولى ٩٧٠ وهو شرح معروف بين العلماء والمفتيين.
ولما تكن اليه فيه شرط صحتِهِ قَالُوا يَصحُ النِّكَاحَ مَعَ الْهَزْلِ لَكِنْ قَالُوا لَوْ عَقَدَ بِلَفْظٍ لا يُعْرَفُ مَعْنَاهُ فَفِيهِ خِلافٌ وَالْفَتْوَى عَلَى صِحْتِهِ عَلِمَ الشُّهُودُ أوْ لَا كَمَا فِي الْبَزَّازِيَةِ. ترجمه: اور جبکہ نکاح میں نیت اس کے صحیح ہونے کی شرط نہیں ہے فقہاء نے کہا کہ نکاح مذاق کے ساتھ کی درست ہے لیکن انہوں نے کہا کہ اگر ایسے لفظ سے عقد کیا جس کے معنی معلوم نہ ہو تو اس میں اختلاف ہے اور خونی ان کی صحت پر ہے گواہوں کو معلوم ہو یا نہ ہو جیسا کہ بزاز یہ میں ہے۔ تشریح جبکہ آپ کو یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ نکاح کی صحت کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں ہے تو فقہاء کرام فرماتے ہیں کہ مذاق میں بھی نکاح صحیح ہوتا ہے بشرطیکہ شرائط نکاح پائے جائیں اور کوئی مانع بھی نہ ہو کیونکہ نکاح میں نیت کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ اعتبار کلام کا ہو گا۔ نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا : عن ابي هريرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ثلاث جدهن جد وهزلهن جد النكاح والطلاق والرجعة.
ولو عقد بلفظ لا يعرف مائل میں آپ کو معلوم ہو ہی گیا کہ نکاح میں سنجیدگی اور مذاق دونوں باہر جھا
1+1
اگر کسی نے مذاق میں ایسے الفاظ استعمال کر لئے جن سے نکاح منعقد ہو جاتا ہے خواہ وہ ان الفاظ کے معانی کو جانتے ہوں یا نہ جانتے ہوں تو نکاح منعقد ہو جائے گا بشرطیکہ شرائط نکاح موجود ہوں اور کوئی مانع نہ پایا جائے البتہ ان کو یہ معلوم ہو کہ ان الفاظ سے نکاح منعقد ہو جاتا ہے۔
صاحب کتاب نے بزازیہ کے حوالہ سے اس کو مفتی بہ قول قرار دیا ہے ، علامہ شامی نے بھی الدر والغرر کے حوالہ سے نقل کیا ہے کہ الفاظ کے معنی کی حقیقت جاننا شرط نہیں ہے لیکن اتنا معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ ان الفاظ سے نکاح صحیح ہو جاتا ہے۔ تعلم الفاظ صریحہ میں ہے کیونکہ ان کے معانی متعارف و معلوم ہوتے ہیں لہذا وہ الفاظ اپنے متعارف و معروف ہونے کی وجہ سے اسی خاص معنی میں استعمال ہوتے ہیں بشرطیکہ کوئی قرینہ صارفہ نہ ہو اور اگر الفاظ کنائی استعمال کئے ہیں تو مستعمل معنی کی مراد کی تعیین کے لئے نیت کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے۔
علم الشهود ام لا : گواہوں کا سننا اور سمجھنا شرط ہے یا نہیں خلاصہ میں ہے کہ فہم شہود شرط نہیں ہے جبکہ جو ہرہ میں ہے کہ سماع اور فہم شرط ہے حاصل کلام یہ ہے کہ فہم مشہور کی صحیح میں اختلاف ہے لیکن درست اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ فہم شہود ضروری ہے ۔
وَعَلى هَذَا سَائِرُ الْقُرَبِ لَا بُدَّ فِيْهَا مِنَ النِّيَّةِ بِمَعْنَى تَوَقُّفِ حُصُوْلِ الثَّوَابِ عَلَى قَصْدِ التَّقَرُّب بِهَا إِلى اللهِ تَعَالَى مِنْ نَشْرِ الْعِلْمِ تَعْلِيماً وَإِفْتَاءً وَتَصْنِيْفاً.
:ترجمه اور اس پر جملہ قرجمین محمول ہیں کہ ان میں نیت ضروری ہے اس اعتبار سے کہ ثواب کا حصول موقوف بے ان کے ذریعہ اللہ کے تقرب کا ارادہ کرنے پر ان میں سے ) اشاعت علم ہے تعلیم کے ذریعہ ہو یا افتاء کے ذریعہ یا تصنیف کے ذریعہ۔ تشریح: علامہ ابن نجیم مصری فرماتے ہیں کہ جملہ قربات نکاح کی طرح ہیں کہ اگر ان میں اللہ کے تقرب کا ارادہ کر لیا جائے تو ثواب حاصل ہوگا اور اگر تقرب کی نیت نہ کی تو اگر چہ وہ صحیح اور درست ہو جائیں گے لیکن ثواب نہ ملے گا۔ ان ہی تقریبات میں سے اشاعت علم ہے۔ ار علم سیکھنے سے نیت دوسروں کو سکھانے اور اس پر عمل کرنے کی ہو تو ثواب ملے گا اسی طرح فتویٰ دینے سے نیت وں کو کی راہ دکھلانے کی ہوتب ہی عمل آخرت میں ثواب کا سبب ہوگا اور اگر نیت جاہلوں پر بڑائی جتلانے اور تکبر کی جوب پھر یہی علم وبال جان ہو جائے گا۔ حدثنی ابن کعب بن مالک عن ابيه قال سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول من طلب العلم ليجارى به العلماء او ليمارى به السفهاء او يصرف به وجوه الناس إليه ادخله الله الغار. ( ترندی شریف ج راص ۹۴۶)
If there is firm conviction of falling into sin, then it becomes forbidden. So intention is needed to attain reward. Actions themselves are not worship unless approached as worship. For the validity of marriage intention is not a condition, but for obtaining reward intention is necessary, and because of intention it becomes worship. If the purpose of marriage is merely following the Shariah and obeying the prophetic command, then also reward will be given. And it is that one intends chastity: at the time of marriage one intends to protect oneself from illicit glances and immorality, and also to protect the wife from the forbidden. Similarly, the intention of obtaining children by permissible means. If the intention is merely to satisfy lust, then it is prohibited. And we explained 'i'tidal (moderation)': according to the saying of Allamah Mawii, Allamah Haskafi and Allamah Shami interpreted i'tidal as being able to pay maintenance, not being in fear of falling into oppression, and similarly not fearing the omission of obligations and sunnahs. If any one of these is intended, then the state of moderation will no longer remain, so then nikah will not even be sunnah for such a person. His saying in al-Sharh al-Kabir: describing the commentary as 'kabir' (great) is for unveiling and explanation of reality, not for distinction, for he has no small commentary. The meaning of 'al-Sharh al-Kabir' is al-Bahr al-Raiq by Allamah Zain al-Din Ibn Nujaim al-Misri (d. 970), and it is a well-known commentary among scholars and muftis. And since intention is not a condition for its validity, they said: nikah is valid with jest. But they said: if he contracts with a word whose meaning is not known, then there is a difference of opinion, and the fatwa is on its validity, whether the witnesses know or not, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. Translation: And since intention in marriage is not a condition for its validity, the jurists said that marriage with jest is valid, but they said that if the contract is made with a word whose meaning is not known, then there is difference, and the fatwa is on its validity, whether the witnesses know or not, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. Explanation: Since you have learned that intention is not a condition for the validity of marriage, the noble jurists say that marriage in jest is also valid, provided that the conditions of marriage are fulfilled and there is no impediment, because intention is not considered in marriage; rather, the speech is considered. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Abu Huraira reported that the Messenger of Allah said: Three things are serious and in jest: marriage, divorce, and return. And if one contracts with a word that is not known... Now you have learned that both seriousness and jest are equal in marriage. 1+1 If someone in jest uses words by which marriage is contracted, whether he knows the meanings of those words or not, then marriage is contracted, provided the conditions of marriage are present and no impediment exists, but he should know that from those words marriage is contracted. The author of the book, citing al-Bazzaziyyah, declared this the mufta bih (relied upon) opinion. Allamah Shami also narrated from al-Durr wa al-Ghurar that knowing the reality of the meanings of words is not a condition, but one should know that from those words marriage is valid. In clear (sarih) words, it is because their meanings are well-known and understood; hence, those words are used in that specific meaning due to being well-known, provided there is no counter-indication. And if allusive (kinayah) words are used, then intention is necessary to determine the intended meaning. 'Whether the witnesses know or not': Is hearing and understanding by the witnesses a condition? In al-Khulasah, it is said that understanding by the witnesses is not a condition, while in al-Jawharah, it is said that hearing and understanding are conditions. The conclusion is that there is difference in the correctness of the well-known view, but the correct and sound view is that understanding by the witnesses is necessary. And upon this, all other acts of worship (qurubat) are treated: intention is necessary in them, meaning the acquisition of reward depends on intending to draw near to Allah, from spreading knowledge, teaching, giving fatwa, and writing. Translation: And upon this, all other acts of worship are judged, that intention is necessary in them in the sense that the acquisition of reward is dependent on intending to draw near to Allah through them, including spreading knowledge through teaching, giving fatwa, or writing. Explanation: Allamah Ibn Nujaim al-Misri says that all acts of worship are like marriage: if one intends to draw near to Allah in them, then reward will be obtained; and if one does not intend closeness, then even if they are valid and correct, no reward will be given. Among these worship acts is spreading knowledge. If one learns knowledge intending to teach others and act upon it, then reward will be obtained. Similarly, giving fatwa with the intention of showing the right path will be a cause of reward in the Hereafter. But if the intention is to show off to the ignorant and arrogance, then this knowledge will become a burden. It is narrated from Ibn Ka'b ibn Malik from his father: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: Whoever seeks knowledge to vie with scholars, or to argue with fools, or to turn people's faces towards him, Allah will enter him into the Fire. (Tirmidhi, Vol. 1, p. 946)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the maxim that intention (niyyah) is required for reward but not for the validity of certain acts, particularly marriage. The author begins by stating that if one is certain of falling into sin, marriage becomes obligatory, but generally, intention is needed for reward. He clarifies that for the validity of marriage, intention is not a condition; however, for reward, one must intend to follow shari'ah, seek chastity, produce children, etc. He then explains the concept of i'tidal (moderation) as defined by later Hanafi authorities: a person in a moderate state is one who can afford maintenance, does not fear oppression, and does not fear missing obligations or sunnahs. If any of these is compromised, the state is no longer moderate, and marriage is not even sunnah. The author identifies 'al-Sharh al-Kabir' as al-Bahr al-Raiq by Ibn Nujaim (d. 970), a standard reference. The core legal rule is stated: since intention is not a condition for validity, marriage in jest is valid. But there is a dispute regarding words whose meaning is unknown: the relied-upon fatwa (al-mufta bih) is validity, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. The hadith of the Prophet (three things are serious and in jest: marriage, divorce, and return) is cited as evidence. The comment then clarifies that even if one does not know the exact meaning of the words, as long as he knows that such words effect marriage, the marriage is valid. For clear (sarih) words, no intention is needed; they carry their conventional meaning. For allusive (kinayah) words, intention is required to specify the intended meaning. The passage then addresses the condition of witnesses: whether understanding by witnesses is required. After citing differences in al-Khulasah and al-Jawharah, the correct view is that witnesses' understanding is necessary. Finally, the principle is extended to all acts of worship (qurubat) such as teaching, giving fatwa, and writing: they are valid without intention, but reward depends on sincere intention to draw near to Allah. A hadith on the danger of seeking knowledge for worldly purposes is quoted.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention; the deliberate aim to perform an act for the sake of Allah. In this passage, it is distinguished between being required for validity (not required for marriage) and for reward (required for all qurubat).
اعتدال (i'tidal): A state of moderation in which a person is able to afford nafaqah, is not in fear of oppression, and does not fear missing faraid and sunan. It makes nikah sunnah.
بزازية (al-Bazzaziyyah): A well-known Hanafi fatwa collection by al-Bazzazi, used as a source for the fatwa on validity of marriage with unknown words.
قربات (qurubat): Acts of worship that draw one closer to Allah; all good deeds intended as such. They are valid without intention, but reward depends on intention.
اشاعت علم (isha'at al-'ilm): Spreading of sacred knowledge through teaching, issuing fatwas, and writing books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bih (relied-upon fatwa) in the passage, what is the ruling on a marriage contract performed using words whose meaning is unknown to the groom, but he knows that those words effect marriage?
A) The marriage is invalid because the meaning is unknown.
B) The marriage is valid, and the witnesses must understand the words.
C) The marriage is valid, even if the witnesses do not understand.
D) The marriage is valid only if the groom intended marriage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, intention affects reward but not validity in marriage and other contracts; intention becomes necessary for validity only in clear acts of worship (ibadat) and in ambiguous language (kinayah).
